# `mdk` CLI reference

Auto-generated by `mdk docs cli` (or `scripts/gen_cli_reference.py`). Do not edit by hand — regenerate after changing commands.

## Command tree

- `mdk add` — Add one or more role-based agents to the current project.
- `mdk agent` — Inspect + roll back published agent versions (durable registry).
  - `mdk agent history` — Show the version history for ``name``, newest-first.
  - `mdk agent revert` — Roll ``name`` back to ``--to <version>`` (non-destructive).
- `mdk audit` — Run production-readiness scanners over the project or a snapshot.
- `mdk audit-llm` — Run a Claude-orchestrated read-only audit against a runtime target.
  - `mdk audit-llm agent` — Run a Claude-orchestrated audit of one agent against a runtime.
  - `mdk audit-llm project` — Run a Claude-orchestrated audit across every agent in a project.
- `mdk auth` — Manage API keys for the movate runtime.
  - `mdk auth bootstrap-seed` — Mint a fresh bootstrap API key + upload to Key Vault + save locally.
  - `mdk auth create-key` — Mint a new API key.
  - `mdk auth list-keys` — List API keys, newest first.
  - `mdk auth login` — Set a provider API key, verify it, persist it for every project.
  - `mdk auth logout` — Clear the cached SSO token for an OIDC target (ADR 013 L1).
  - `mdk auth pull-runtime-key` — Pull the bootstrap key from Key Vault into the local credentials store.
  - `mdk auth refresh-runtime-key` — Mint + save a fresh runtime bearer in one step.
  - `mdk auth revoke-all` — Revoke ALL active keys for a tenant — compromise response (ADR 013 D5).
  - `mdk auth revoke-key` — Revoke an API key.
  - `mdk auth rotate-key` — Rotate an API key with a zero-downtime grace window (ADR 013 D5).
  - `mdk auth save-runtime-key` — Save a minted runtime bearer key to the credentials store.
  - `mdk auth status` — Show which provider keys are configured and where they came from.
  - `mdk auth use-file` — Migrate machine-global credentials from the OS keychain back to the file.
  - `mdk auth use-keychain` — Migrate machine-global credentials from the file into the OS keychain.
  - `mdk auth whoami` — Show the identity of the current API key on a deployed runtime.
- `mdk authoring` — Evolve an agent through the typed, reversible authoring catalog (ADR 025):...
  - `mdk authoring apply` — Checkpoint → apply → verify an action.
  - `mdk authoring audit` — Show the append-only authoring audit log (every plan/apply/undo, D7e).
  - `mdk authoring history` — Print the authoring action log (oldest-first).
  - `mdk authoring list` — List the authoring action catalog (self-describing).
  - `mdk authoring plan` — Dry-run an action: show its diff + estimate + confirmation gate (NO writes).
  - `mdk authoring replay` — Re-apply the recorded *applied* action sequence through the driver (D7e).
  - `mdk authoring undo` — Revert the last applied action to its pre-action checkpoint.
- `mdk batch` — Bulk async inference: submit a dataset, run one job per row (item 17).
  - `mdk batch list` — List this tenant's recent batches at the target.
  - `mdk batch status` — Show the per-status aggregate + derived state of a batch.
  - `mdk batch submit` — Submit a JSONL dataset as a batch of async runs.
- `mdk bench` — Benchmark an agent across multiple models (cost / latency / quality).
- `mdk benchmark` — Shadow-replay past runs against a candidate model.
  - `mdk benchmark live` — Shadow-replay past runs against a candidate model.
- `mdk canary` — Manage champion/challenger canary rollouts (ADR 016 D3).
  - `mdk canary compare` — Compare live quality champion-vs-challenger (feedback + run/error counts).
  - `mdk canary off` — Kill switch: route 100% to champion (weight 0), or --delete the canary.
  - `mdk canary promote` — Promote a version to champion (assisted — concludes the canary).
  - `mdk canary set` — Set (or update) an agent's canary rollout.
  - `mdk canary status` — Show an agent's current canary config.
- `mdk capabilities` — Show the capability matrix of a deployed runtime.
- `mdk catalog` — Browse, contribute to, and sync the agent catalog (ADR 041).
  - `mdk catalog list` — List catalog entries visible to the caller (filtered + paginated).
  - `mdk catalog publish-version` — Publish a new version of a tenant-private entry.
  - `mdk catalog rate` — Record a 1-5 rating for one catalog entry.
  - `mdk catalog search` — Alias for ``mdk catalog list --q <query>``.
  - `mdk catalog show` — Show detail for one catalog entry (and optionally one version).
  - `mdk catalog submit` — Submit a tenant-private catalog entry from ``<from-dir>``.
  - `mdk catalog sync` — Trigger a manual catalog sync.
- `mdk chat` — Interactive REPL bound to one agent.
- `mdk ci` — CI helpers — pre-flight gates that wrap multi-agent invocations.
  - `mdk ci eval` — Eval every agent in the project; fail on any regression.
- `mdk compose` — Scaffold a multi-agent workflow.yaml from a list of agents.
- `mdk config` — Manage user-level movate config (deployment targets, active target).
  - `mdk config add-target` — Register a deployment target.
  - `mdk config current` — Print the active target as a single line (script-friendly).
  - `mdk config list-targets` — Show all registered targets, highlighting the active one.
  - `mdk config remove-target` — Delete a target.
  - `mdk config set` — Set a user-level config key (writes ``~/.movate/config.yaml``).
  - `mdk config show` — Dump the resolved config (useful for debugging).
  - `mdk config use` — Set the active target — CLI commands default to it when --target is omitted.
- `mdk contexts` — List and inspect shared context files injected into agent prompts.
  - `mdk contexts attach` — Wire an existing context into an agent's ``contexts:`` list.
  - `mdk contexts create` — Create a new context file pre-filled with a minimal template.
  - `mdk contexts detach` — Remove a context from an agent's ``contexts:`` list.
  - `mdk contexts list` — List all context files in the project.
  - `mdk contexts remote` — Manage the runtime's MANAGED contexts registry over the API (ADR 060).
    - `mdk contexts remote attach` — Attach a registry context to an agent (records the ref; D4 resolves it).
    - `mdk contexts remote create` — Create the first version of a managed context from a Markdown file.
    - `mdk contexts remote delete` — Delete a managed context (a version, or all versions of the name).
    - `mdk contexts remote get` — Show one managed context (latest, or a pinned ``--version``).
    - `mdk contexts remote list` — List the tenant's managed contexts (latest version per name).
    - `mdk contexts remote update` — Publish a NEW version of a managed context (rows are immutable).
    - `mdk contexts remote versions` — List a managed context's version history (newest-first).
  - `mdk contexts show` — Print the full body of a context file.
- `mdk costs` — Historical cost reports from recorded runs.
  - `mdk costs report` — Summarise spend per agent or provider from recorded runs.
- `mdk demo` — Demo project scaffold + the dashboard 'wow pack' seeder.
  - `mdk demo clear` — Purge ALL demo-seeded telemetry (and nothing else).
  - `mdk demo doctor` — Confirm the Monday-demo environment is GO (run after ``mdk demo seed``).
  - `mdk demo new` — Generate a complete runnable demo project (FAQ agent + dataset).
  - `mdk demo seed` — Populate the runtime with realistic synthetic telemetry (the "wow pack").
- `mdk deploy` — Build the runtime image + roll out to Azure Container Apps.
- `mdk dev` — Guided agent authoring: scaffold → edit → live-test → deploy.
- `mdk diagnose` — Diagnose recent failures for an agent — cluster + propose typed fixes (ADR...
  - `mdk diagnose show` — Fetch + render a previously-submitted diagnose.
- `mdk diff` — Compare two snapshots or the working tree against a git commit.
- `mdk docs` — Auto-generated project documentation.
  - `mdk docs cli` — Generate the full ``mdk`` CLI command reference.
  - `mdk docs runbook` — Generate an ops runbook from the current project state.
- `mdk doctor` — Environment + configuration sanity check.
  - `mdk doctor agent` — Agent-specific health check: validates, prices, smoke-tests.
- `mdk eval` — Run the eval suite for an agent and gate on a threshold.
- `mdk eval-gen` — Generate eval dataset entries for an agent via LLM.
- `mdk eval-generate` — Author an eval dataset from a plain-English agent description.
- `mdk eval-generate-commit` — Commit selected generated cases to the agent's dataset.
- `mdk eval-harvest` — Harvest prod runs into [bold]proposed[/bold] eval cases (ADR 016 D1).
- `mdk eval-schedule` — Manage continuous-eval cadences per agent (ADR 016 D2).
  - `mdk eval-schedule clear` — Remove an agent's continuous-eval schedule.
  - `mdk eval-schedule list` — List this project's continuous-eval schedules.
  - `mdk eval-schedule set` — Set (or update) an agent's continuous-eval cadence.
- `mdk eval-scheduler-tick` — Run one scheduler tick: enqueue eval jobs for due schedules (ADR 016 D2).
- `mdk eval-scorecard` — Generate test cases on the fly and score against a 10-category scorecard.
- `mdk explain` — Render the decision chain behind a completed run.
- `mdk export` — Package movate primitives as portable artifacts.
  - `mdk export langgraph` — Export a workflow as a standalone LangGraph Python module.
  - `mdk export oci-bundle` — Package an agent as a portable OCI-compatible tar.gz bundle.
  - `mdk export state` — Export operator-critical control-plane state to a portable JSON backup.
  - `mdk export temporal` — Export a workflow as a standalone Temporal Python module.
- `mdk fix` — Auto-remediate common diagnostic findings.
- `mdk fleet` — READ-ONLY cross-target view of deployed runtimes.
  - `mdk fleet logs` — Tail recent logs for a target's API Container App (READ-ONLY).
  - `mdk fleet status` — Show health, version, and agent inventory for every configured target.
- `mdk fmt` — Normalize the style of YAML / prompt / JSONL files.
- `mdk graph` — Inspect a deployed agent's knowledge graph (read-only, graphology JSON).
  - `mdk graph dashboard` — Start the hosted knowledge-graph dashboard and open it in a browser.
  - `mdk graph node` — Fetch one node's detail + provenance (source chunks + url + confidence).
  - `mdk graph serve` — Start the local knowledge-graph viewer and open it in a browser.
  - `mdk graph show` — Fetch ``project``'s knowledge graph as graphology JSON.
- `mdk guardrails` — Manage + test the Safe-AI guardrails (PII / topic / content) configured in...
  - `mdk guardrails disable` — Flip a guardrail's ``enabled: false`` in the project config.
  - `mdk guardrails enable` — Flip a guardrail's ``enabled: true`` in the project config.
  - `mdk guardrails list` — Show the currently-configured guardrails per direction + module.
  - `mdk guardrails test` — Dry-run a string against the configured guardrails.
- `mdk import` — Import agents into MDK from other frameworks (Lyzr today; more later).
  - `mdk import json` — Generic JSON → MDK agent importer.
  - `mdk import lyzr` — Synthesize an MDK agent from a Lyzr Studio agent JSON definition.
  - `mdk import openapi` — Import an OpenAPI spec as one skill per operation.
  - `mdk import state` — Restore a control-plane backup made by [bold]mdk export[/bold].
- `mdk infra` — Provision Azure infrastructure for a movate target.
  - `mdk infra apply` — Provision Azure infrastructure + auto-seed the bootstrap key.
- `mdk init` — Scaffold a new agent or project — always leaving a runnable result.
- `mdk inspect` — Show the [bold]resolved[/bold] view of an agent / workflow / skill — defaults...
  - `mdk inspect agent` — Show the [bold]resolved[/bold] view of an agent — what the executor sees.
- `mdk jobs` — Inspect jobs on a deployed movate runtime.
  - `mdk jobs cancel` — Cooperatively cancel a queued or running job.
  - `mdk jobs dead-letter` — Manage retry-exhausted (dead-letter) jobs: list, show, retry, purge.
    - `mdk jobs dead-letter list` — List this tenant's retry-exhausted (dead-letter) jobs, newest first.
    - `mdk jobs dead-letter purge` — [bold red]Permanently delete[/bold red] this tenant's dead-letter jobs.
    - `mdk jobs dead-letter retry` — Requeue a dead-letter job (or [bold]--all[/bold]) back onto the queue.
    - `mdk jobs dead-letter show` — Show one dead-letter job's full state (incl.
  - `mdk jobs list` — List this tenant's recent jobs on the target runtime, newest first.
  - `mdk jobs list-agents` — List agents registered on the target runtime.
  - `mdk jobs reap` — Run the stale-job reaper once against the LOCAL runtime.
  - `mdk jobs show` — Show the current state of one job.
  - `mdk jobs wait` — Block on a job until it reaches a terminal state.
- `mdk judge` — Author + commit an LLM-as-judge rubric (evals/judge.yaml) for an agent.
  - `mdk judge commit` — Commit a reviewed [bold]judge.yaml[/bold] to the agent.
  - `mdk judge generate` — Author a complete [bold]evals/judge.yaml[/bold] for [bold]<agent>[/bold].
- `mdk kb` — Knowledge-base ingest + search.
  - `mdk kb clear` — Delete chunks from ``agent``'s KB.
  - `mdk kb ingest` — Ingest a knowledge-base file, directory, or web page into ``agent``'s KB.
  - `mdk kb ingest-all` — Scan the project and ingest every KB directory found.
  - `mdk kb list` — List chunks in ``agent``'s KB.
  - `mdk kb reindex` — Rebuild ``agent``'s KB vector index.
  - `mdk kb search` — Semantic search over ``agent``'s KB.
  - `mdk kb stats` — Summary stats for ``agent``'s KB: chunk count, source breakdown, embedding...
- `mdk keys` — Manage this tenant's own provider API keys, encrypted at rest (BYOK, ADR 018).
  - `mdk keys delete` — Remove this tenant's key for a provider (falls back to the shared key).
  - `mdk keys list` — List configured providers + masked fingerprints (never the values).
  - `mdk keys set` — Store (or rotate) this tenant's key for [bold]provider[/bold].
  - `mdk keys test` — Make a cheap provider call with the stored key to validate it.
- `mdk knowledge` — Inspect and validate knowledge-base assets.
  - `mdk knowledge add` — Append one entry to the KB corpus interactively or via --json.
  - `mdk knowledge edit` — Patch one entry in the KB corpus by id.
  - `mdk knowledge list` — List KB corpus entries as a table.
  - `mdk knowledge query` — Query the KB corpus and show ranked results.
  - `mdk knowledge remove` — Remove one entry from the KB corpus by id.
  - `mdk knowledge validate` — Check which eval queries return zero KB corpus matches.
- `mdk logs` — Inspect a run record: input, output, cost, latency, errors.
- `mdk mcp` — Run the authoring MCP server: expose the typed action catalog (ADR 025) as...
  - `mdk mcp serve` — Serve the authoring catalog over MCP (newline-delimited JSON-RPC on stdio).
- `mdk memory` — Agent memory — list / get / set / evict / summarise / query stored entries.
  - `mdk memory delete` — Remove a single memory entry.
  - `mdk memory evict` — Bulk-delete memory entries older than a threshold.
  - `mdk memory get` — Print one memory entry's value as JSON.
  - `mdk memory list` — List every memory entry for an agent.
  - `mdk memory query` — Substring search across an agent's memory values.
  - `mdk memory set` — Insert or replace a memory entry.
  - `mdk memory summarise` — Operator-readable summary of an agent's memory.
- `mdk menu` — Show workspace status and a contextual list of next steps.
- `mdk migrate` — Restore files from a snapshot into the current workspace.
- `mdk migrate-state` — Rename this project's legacy ``.movate/`` runtime-state dir to ``.mdk/`` (ADR...
- `mdk models` — Browse the MDK model catalog — pricing, context windows, and capabilities.
  - `mdk models list` — List all models in the MDK catalog with pricing and capabilities.
  - `mdk models show` — Show pricing and capability details for a specific model.
- `mdk monitor` — Live dashboard of recent runs.
- `mdk observability` — Ask questions about your fleet's telemetry.
  - `mdk observability analyze` — Trigger the overnight analyst on demand (requires admin scope).
  - `mdk observability ask` — Ask a natural-language question; get a grounded answer with citations.
  - `mdk observability digest` — Show the analyst's daily markdown digest for a date (or the latest).
  - `mdk observability health` — Show the latest health score + digest for a project.
  - `mdk observability troubleshoot` — Correlate failures + drift + deploys into a likely root cause.
- `mdk patterns` — Discover the governed agent-pattern templates (ADR 038) `mdk init --pattern`...
  - `mdk patterns list` — List the governed agent patterns + their topology + governance summary.
- `mdk plan` — Generate a project plan from a natural-language description.
- `mdk playground` — ChatGPT-like browser UI for testing deployed agents.
  - `mdk playground serve` — Launch the ChatGPT-like Chainlit playground for testing agents.
- `mdk policy` — Export / import / diff project policy.yaml — promote a vetted policy from dev...
  - `mdk policy diff` — Show what would change if you imported ``source``.
  - `mdk policy export` — Emit the active policy.yaml as deterministic YAML or JSON.
  - `mdk policy import` — Read a policy doc and write it to policy.yaml.
- `mdk pricing` — Show the price-per-1k-tokens table for all configured models.
- `mdk profiles` — Manage named environment contexts (dev / staging / prod / customer).
  - `mdk profiles create` — Register a new profile (or update an existing one).
  - `mdk profiles current` — Print the active profile name (or exit 1 if none set).
  - `mdk profiles delete` — Remove a profile from the registry.
  - `mdk profiles list` — List every registered profile; mark the active one with *.
  - `mdk profiles show` — Render one profile's details + active status.
  - `mdk profiles use` — Activate a profile.
- `mdk project` — Manage tenant-scoped projects + members (ADR 040).
  - `mdk project add-agent` — Attach a new agent to a project.
  - `mdk project archive` — Soft-delete (archive) a project.
  - `mdk project create` — Create a new project in the active tenant.
  - `mdk project list` — List this tenant's projects, newest-first.
  - `mdk project members` — Manage a project's member roster (viewer / editor / owner).
    - `mdk project members add` — Invite a principal to the project with a role.
    - `mdk project members list` — List a project's members (creation order).
    - `mdk project members remove` — Remove a member from the project.
  - `mdk project show` — Show one project's detail.
  - `mdk project update` — Rename / re-describe a project.
- `mdk promote` — Record a snapshot's promotion to a profile.
- `mdk replay` — Re-execute a past run with the same input.
- `mdk report` — Offline rollup of agent health from the local store (ADR 031 D3).
- `mdk rollback` — Restore the project to a prior snapshot.
- `mdk run` — Run an agent or workflow against the given input.
- `mdk runs` — Inspect run results on a deployed movate runtime.
  - `mdk runs show` — Show a single run including the agent's ``output``.
- `mdk scaffold` — Generate boilerplate for movate artifacts (tools, etc).
  - `mdk scaffold tool` — Generate a new tool directory under ``<target>/<name>/``.
- `mdk schedule` — Manage cron schedules that enqueue agent/workflow jobs (ADR 017 D2).
  - `mdk schedule clear` — Remove a cron schedule by its handle.
  - `mdk schedule list` — List this project's cron schedules.
  - `mdk schedule set` — Set (or update) a cron schedule that enqueues agent/workflow jobs.
- `mdk scheduler-tick` — Run one unified scheduler tick — enqueue ALL due jobs (ADR 017 D2).
- `mdk schema` — Author + compile schema files (canonical / shorthand / JSON Schema).
  - `mdk schema compile` — Compile a schema file to JSON Schema.
- `mdk secrets` — Per-profile secret storage (values; distinct from [bold]mdk env[/bold]).
  - `mdk secrets delete` — Remove a secret from the active profile.
  - `mdk secrets export-shell` — Emit shell ``export`` statements for every secret in the profile.
  - `mdk secrets get` — Print a secret's value to stdout.
  - `mdk secrets list` — List secret names in the active profile.
  - `mdk secrets set` — Store a secret in the active profile.
  - `mdk secrets where` — Print the on-disk path for the active profile's secrets file.
- `mdk serve` — Start the movate FastAPI runtime.
- `mdk show` — Show the resolved spec for an agent, workflow, or skill.
- `mdk simulate` — Stress-test a chatbot by running it through multi-turn scenarios.
- `mdk skills` — Inspect, scaffold, and test the skill registry.
  - `mdk skills add-mcp` — Register an MCP server as a skill in one command.
  - `mdk skills info` — Show full detail for a skill.
  - `mdk skills list` — Print every skill registered in the project's ``skills/`` folder.
  - `mdk skills remote` — Manage the runtime's MANAGED skills registry over the API (ADR 060).
    - `mdk skills remote attach` — Attach a registry skill to an agent (records the ref; D4 resolves it).
    - `mdk skills remote create` — Publish a skill bundle to the managed registry (first version).
    - `mdk skills remote delete` — Delete a managed skill (a version, or all versions of the name).
    - `mdk skills remote get` — Show one managed skill (latest, or a pinned ``--version``).
    - `mdk skills remote list` — List the tenant's managed skills (latest version per name).
    - `mdk skills remote update` — Publish a NEW version of a managed skill (rows are immutable).
    - `mdk skills remote versions` — List a managed skill's version history (newest-first).
  - `mdk skills run` — Invoke a skill directly, bypassing the agent + tool-use loop.
  - `mdk skills scaffold` — Scaffold a starter skill from the packaged template.
  - `mdk skills search` — Search the project's skill registry by tag, freetext, and/or kind.
  - `mdk skills validate` — Validate skill compatibility for agent(s).
- `mdk snapshot` — Capture / compare / restore project state.
  - `mdk snapshot create` — Capture the current project state as an immutable snapshot.
  - `mdk snapshot delete` — Remove a snapshot from disk.
  - `mdk snapshot list` — List every snapshot in the project's ``.movate/snapshots/`` dir.
  - `mdk snapshot show` — Display a snapshot's manifest in detail.
- `mdk submit` — Queue a job at a deployed runtime and (optionally) wait for completion.
- `mdk teams-bot` — Microsoft Teams bot — Movate's self-serve front door for non-technical users.
  - `mdk teams-bot serve` — Boot the Teams bot webhook on ``host:port``.
- `mdk templates` — Discover the agent + workflow templates `mdk init -t` and `mdk add` accept.
  - `mdk templates list` — List every template `mdk init -t <name>` / `mdk add <name>` accepts.
  - `mdk templates show` — Show full metadata + on-disk file tree for one template.
- `mdk tenants` — Manage tenant budgets + (future) per-tenant overrides.
  - `mdk tenants clear-budget` — Remove the budget cap for ``tenant_id`` (unlimited spend).
  - `mdk tenants list` — List every tenant with a configured budget row.
  - `mdk tenants quota` — View or update per-tenant quotas (ADR 036 D2).
    - `mdk tenants quota set` — Write the per-tenant quota row to the config file.
    - `mdk tenants quota show` — Show the configured quota + current usage + remaining for ``tenant_id``.
  - `mdk tenants set-budget` — Set or update the monthly cost budget for ``tenant_id``.
  - `mdk tenants show` — Show current-month spend vs budget for ``tenant_id``.
- `mdk tools` — Manage the shared tool registry (ADR 052).
  - `mdk tools info` — Show full detail for a tool descriptor.
  - `mdk tools list` — List tool descriptors in the registry.
  - `mdk tools publish` — Publish a tool descriptor to the registry.
  - `mdk tools resolve` — Test tool resolution against the registry.
- `mdk trace` — Inspect and replay traces.
  - `mdk trace replay` — Replay a run or workflow_run from local storage.
- `mdk trigger` — Manage inbound event/webhook triggers that enqueue agent/workflow jobs (ADR...
  - `mdk trigger create` — Register an inbound event/webhook trigger.
  - `mdk trigger delete` — Remove a trigger by its handle.
  - `mdk trigger list` — List this project's triggers (no secrets).
- `mdk tune` — Sweep one knob across a list of values and show the outputs.
- `mdk validate` — Validate ``agent.yaml`` (or ``workflow.yaml``) plus its references.
- `mdk voice` — Terminal voice conversation + voice provider tooling.
  - `mdk voice ask` — Ask in one shot: spoken audio in → transcript + answer + spoken audio out.
  - `mdk voice bench` — Run the voice eval/regression harness over a golden audio corpus.
  - `mdk voice call` — Initiate an outbound phone call and connect it to an mdk voice agent.
  - `mdk voice providers` — Voice provider tooling — list available STT/TTS providers.
    - `mdk voice providers list` — List available STT and TTS voice providers on the target runtime.
  - `mdk voice say` — Speak a one-shot answer: text in → the agent answers → spoken audio out.
  - `mdk voice transcribe` — Transcribe an audio file: audio in → transcript out (STT only).
  - `mdk voice try` — Start a terminal voice conversation with an agent.
- `mdk watch` — Re-run ``movate validate`` whenever the agent's files change.
- `mdk webhooks` — Manage outbound webhook subscriptions for lifecycle events (ADR 035 D2).
  - `mdk webhooks attempts` — List recent delivery attempts for a subscription (newest-first).
  - `mdk webhooks create` — Subscribe a URL to lifecycle events.
  - `mdk webhooks delete` — Remove a webhook subscription (revokes its signing secret).
  - `mdk webhooks disable` — Disable a subscription (the worker stops delivering until re-enabled).
  - `mdk webhooks enable` — Re-enable a disabled subscription.
  - `mdk webhooks list` — List this tenant's webhook subscriptions.
  - `mdk webhooks show` — Show one subscription's current state (no full secret).
- `mdk worker` — Drain the queue, dispatch each job, persist the result.
- `mdk workflow` — Inspect + resume (HITL) workflow runs on a deployed movate runtime.
  - `mdk workflow history` — Fetch and display the full event history for a Temporal workflow run.
  - `mdk workflow list` — List workflow definitions on the target runtime, newest-first.
  - `mdk workflow publish` — Promote a workflow version to "published".
  - `mdk workflow replay` — Replay a Temporal-backed workflow run against its recorded history.
  - `mdk workflow revert` — Roll a workflow back to a prior version (non-destructive).
  - `mdk workflow runs` — List this tenant's workflow runs on the target runtime, newest first.
  - `mdk workflow show` — Show the full spec + bundle metadata for one workflow.
  - `mdk workflow signal` — Signal a human decision to resume a paused workflow run.
  - `mdk workflow validate` — Validate a local workflow.yaml against the target runtime.

## Commands

### `mdk`

```

 Usage: mdk [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 mdk — Movate Development Kit. Declarative platform for AI agents and workflows.

 New here? Run mdk menu for a guided next-step view.

 Common workflows:
   $ mdk menu                       # status + suggested next step
   $ mdk init my-agent              # scaffold
   $ mdk run my-agent '{...}'       # one-shot
   $ mdk eval my-agent              # score against dataset
   $ mdk bench my-agent             # multi-model comparison
   $ mdk doctor                     # check environment

 Also installed as movate (transitional alias; dropped in a future major release).

 Run mdk --install-completion to enable shell tab-completion.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --verbose                              Enable DEBUG-level logging.                               │
│ --quiet               -q               Suppress INFO logging; print only warnings and errors.    │
│ --target              -t         TEXT  Default deployment target for remote commands (submit,    │
│                                        jobs *). Overridden by a per-command --target. Falls back │
│                                        to MDK_TARGET env var (or legacy MOVATE_TARGET), then to  │
│                                        the active config target.                                 │
│                                        [env var: MDK_TARGET, MOVATE_TARGET]                      │

│ --install-completion                   Install completion for the current shell.                 │

│                                        customize the installation.                               │
│ --help                -h               Show this message and exit.                               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Develop ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ menu                   Show workspace status and a contextual list of next steps.                │
│ dev                    Guided agent authoring: scaffold → edit → live-test → deploy.             │
│ init                   Scaffold a new agent or project — always leaving a runnable result.       │
│ add                    Add one or more role-based agents to the current project.                 │
│ compose                Scaffold a multi-agent workflow.yaml from a list of agents.               │

│                        --pattern` accepts.                                                       │

│ knowledge              Inspect and validate knowledge-base assets. validate reports which eval   │
│                        queries return zero corpus matches.                                       │
│ kb                     Knowledge-base ingest + search. Run mdk kb with no arguments for an       │

│ graph                  Inspect a deployed agent's knowledge graph (read-only, graphology JSON).  │

│                        docs/adr/002-skills-and-contexts.md for the design.                       │
│ authoring              Evolve an agent through the typed, reversible authoring catalog (ADR      │
│                        025): add contexts, edit instructions, set models, ingest KB, add         │
│                        skills/evals — each planned, validated, and undoable. The conversational  │
│                        copilot lands in a later release; this is the scriptable spine.           │
│ mcp                    Run the authoring MCP server: expose the typed action catalog (ADR 025)   │
│                        as MCP tools (plan_*/apply_*/validate/run) so an IDE/agent drives the     │
│                        same plan→apply→verify spine as `mdk authoring`. Local control-plane      │
│                        tool; composes catalog actions only.                                      │
│ docs                   Auto-generated project documentation. mdk docs runbook generates a        │
│                        markdown ops runbook from the current project state — refresh after       │
│                        significant changes.                                                      │
│ inspect                Show the resolved view of an agent / workflow / skill — defaults applied, │
│                        schemas compiled, contexts prepended. Different from mdk show (which      │
│                        prints raw YAML fields).                                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Run & evaluate ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮

│                        Multi-turn chat, a past-conversations sidebar, file uploads, live         │
│                        streaming, and 👍/👎/comment feedback persisted to the runtime's Postgre… │
│                        + Langfuse for analysis + agent tuning.                                   │

│                        install 'movate-cli'``).                                                  │

│ diff                   Compare two snapshots or the working tree against a git commit.           │

│ snapshot               Capture / compare / restore project state. Snapshots are immutable +      │
│                        content-addressed (git-style hash); two snapshots of identical state      │
│                        collide deterministically. Pairs with mdk diff, rollback, promote (next   │
│                        in Sprint N).                                                             │

│                        MOVATE_MEMORY_FILE to change.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

### `mdk add`

```

 Usage: mdk add [OPTIONS] [ARGS]...

 Add one or more role-based agents to the current project.

 Examples:

   # List the available roles
   $ mdk add --list

   # Preview a template's files without writing anything
   $ mdk add rag-qa --preview

   # Drop a RAG Q&A agent into ./agents/rag-qa/
   $ mdk add rag-qa

   # Start blank — minimal agent (string in → string out), draft the prompt yourself
   $ mdk add default my-agent

   # Batch: bootstrap a support workspace in one command
   $ mdk add rag-qa ticket-triager email-responder

   # Remove an agent (dry-run; --apply to commit)
   $ mdk add --remove rag-qa --apply

   # Refresh against the latest template version
   $ mdk add --update rag-qa --apply

 See also: mdk dev <name> for a guided
 scaffold → edit → live-test → deploy loop (the front door for
 authoring a single agent end-to-end).

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   args      [ARGS]...  One or more template names to add. Pass --list to see available options.  │
│                        Single-template form supports a trailing rename: mdk add rag-qa           │
│                        pricing-qa.                                                               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --name                 TEXT  Explicit agent name override. Only valid when adding a single       │
│                              template. Use this instead of the positional rename form when       │
│                              scripting (less ambiguous).                                         │
│ --target               PATH  Override the destination directory. Default: ./agents/<name>/ if    │
│                              ./agents/ exists, else ./<name>/.                                   │
│ --force        -f            Overwrite an existing agent directory.                              │
│ --list                       Show the catalog of available role + core templates and exit.       │
│ --search               TEXT  Filter --list output by substring match against the template name,  │
│                              description, or highlight.                                          │
│ --no-validate                Skip the post-scaffold validation pass. By default, every added     │
│                              agent is loaded via load_agent to confirm schemas + prompt +        │
│                              references all resolve.                                             │
│ --preview                    Print the template's files to stdout without writing anything.      │
│                              Useful for answering 'what does this template look like?' without   │
│                              changing project state.                                             │
│ --remove                     Remove an existing agent (counterpart to add). Surfaces dangling    │
│                              references in workflows + baselines. Dry-run by default; pass       │
│                              --apply to commit.                                                  │
│ --update                     Refresh an existing agent against the latest template version.      │
│                              Shows a per-file diff. Dry-run by default; pass --apply to commit   │
│                              (preserves the agent's name).                                       │
│ --apply                      Commit changes for --remove or --update. Without --apply, those     │
│                              flags run as a dry-run preview only — no files written.             │
│ --no-skills                  Skip auto-scaffolding of skills declared in the template's skills:  │
│                              field. By default, declared skills are scaffolded under             │
│                              skills/<name>/ if missing.                                          │
│ --help                       Show this message and exit.                                         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk agent`

```

 Usage: mdk agent [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Inspect + roll back published agent versions (durable registry).

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ history   Show the version history for ``name``, newest-first.                                   │
│ revert    Roll ``name`` back to ``--to <version>`` (non-destructive).                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk agent history`

```

 Usage: mdk agent history [OPTIONS] NAME

 Show the version history for ``name``, newest-first.

 The most-recently-published version is marked as current — that's
 what a versionless run/resolve serves. Each row shows who published
 it (``created_by``) and when, so a team can audit "who changed what."

 Examples:

   # Version history of the faq-bot agent
   $ mdk agent history faq-bot

   # As JSON, for scripting
   $ mdk agent history faq-bot --json

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      TEXT  Agent name (the agent.yaml ``name``). [required]                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --tenant-id        TEXT     Tenant scope. Defaults to 'local' for CLI use. Override in           │
│                             production where the tenant comes from the auth context.             │
│                             [default: local]                                                     │
│ --limit            INTEGER  Max number of versions to show (newest-first). [default: 50]         │
│ --json                      Emit the version history as JSON instead of a table.                 │
│ --help                      Show this message and exit.                                          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk agent revert`

```

 Usage: mdk agent revert [OPTIONS] NAME

 Roll ``name`` back to ``--to <version>`` (non-destructive).

 Re-publishes the target version's bundle forward as a NEW latest
 version — the prior history is left untouched, so you can revert
 again (even back to where you were). The new version is the same
 bundle as ``--to`` with a ``+revert.N`` provenance suffix so it
 doesn't collide with the immutable original row.

 Examples:

   # Roll faq-bot back to the 0.2.0 bundle
   $ mdk agent revert faq-bot --to 0.2.0

   # Non-interactive (CI)
   $ mdk agent revert faq-bot --to 0.2.0 --yes

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      TEXT  Agent name. [required]                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --to                 TEXT  The prior version to roll back to (must exist in the history).     │
│                               [required]                                                         │
│    --tenant-id          TEXT  Tenant scope. Defaults to 'local' for CLI use. [default: local]    │
│    --yes        -y            Skip the confirm prompt (use in scripts / CI).                     │
│    --help                     Show this message and exit.                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk audit`

```

 Usage: mdk audit [OPTIONS] [TARGET]

 Run production-readiness scanners over the project or a snapshot.

 Categories shipped this sprint:

   missing-evals       — agent has no evals/dataset.jsonl
   missing-description  — agent.yaml lacks `description:`
   missing-owner        — agent.yaml lacks `owner:`
   exposed-secret       — regex scan for committed credentials
   empty-prompt         — prompt.md is empty / whitespace-only
   no-test-signal       — no examples AND no dataset
   missing-kb-corpus    — kb-lookup declared but no corpus in kb/
   large-context        — declared context > 4 KB advisory limit

 Examples:

   # Scan current project, default-mode (errors fail; warnings don't)
   $ mdk audit

   # Strict CI gate — fail on warnings too
   $ mdk audit current --strict

   # Audit a snapshot before promoting it
   $ mdk audit abc12345

   # Limit to one scanner category
   $ mdk audit current --category exposed-secret

   # JSON for CI annotations
   $ mdk audit current --json | jq '.findings[] | select(.severity == "error")'

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   target      [TARGET]  What to audit: ``current`` (the live project state) or a snapshot hash / │
│                         prefix. Defaults to ``current``.                                         │
│                         [default: current]                                                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --strict                  Promote warnings to errors. CI-friendly: require a clean bill of       │
│                           health before merging.                                                 │
│ --json                    Emit JSON instead of a Rich table — pipe-friendly for CI annotations.  │
│ --category  -c      TEXT  Limit to specific scanner categories. Repeatable. Valid: empty-prompt, │
│                           exposed-secret, floating-model-tag, large-context,                     │
│                           missing-description, missing-evals, missing-fallback,                  │
│                           missing-kb-corpus, missing-owner, missing-version, no-test-signal,     │
│                           prompt-too-long, schema-no-required                                    │
│ --project   -p      PATH  Project root. Defaults to walking up from cwd for movate.yaml.         │
│ --help                    Show this message and exit.                                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

│ agent     Run a Claude-orchestrated audit of one agent against a runtime.                        │
│ project   Run a Claude-orchestrated audit across every agent in a project.                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk audit-llm agent`

```

 Usage: mdk audit-llm agent [OPTIONS] AGENT

 Run a Claude-orchestrated audit of one agent against a runtime.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    agent      TEXT  Agent name to audit. [required]                                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --target          -t      TEXT   Runtime target the audit endpoint lives on (resolved via     │
│                                     movate.config).                                              │
│                                     [required]                                                   │
│    --category        -c      TEXT   Limit to specific categories. Repeatable. Valid:             │
│                                     ambiguous_prompts, missing_eval_coverage, security_smells,   │
│                                     cost_outliers, kb_quality, schema_drift, model_choice.       │
│                                     Default: all.                                                │
│    --severity-floor          TEXT   Filter floor. One of: info, warn, error, critical.           │
│                                     [default: info]                                              │
│    --model                   TEXT   Override the audit sub-agents' provider string (defaults to  │
│                                     a tenant default).                                           │
│    --budget-usd              FLOAT  Server-side spend cap. 0.0 = no cap. Default: $1.00.         │
│                                     [default: 1.0]                                               │
│    --json                           Emit the audit view as JSON (machine-readable,               │
│                                     pipe-friendly).                                              │
│    --help                           Show this message and exit.                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth`

```

 Usage: mdk auth [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Manage API keys for the movate runtime.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ create-key            Mint a new API key.                                                        │
│ list-keys             List API keys, newest first.                                               │
│ whoami                Show the identity of the current API key on a deployed runtime.            │
│ revoke-key            Revoke an API key. Idempotent — re-revoking is a silent no-op.             │
│ rotate-key            Rotate an API key with a zero-downtime grace window (ADR 013 D5).          │
│ revoke-all            Revoke ALL active keys for a tenant — compromise response (ADR 013 D5).    │
│ login                 Set a provider API key, verify it, persist it for every project.           │
│ logout                Clear the cached SSO token for an OIDC target (ADR 013 L1).                │
│ use-keychain          Migrate machine-global credentials from the file into the OS keychain.     │
│ use-file              Migrate machine-global credentials from the OS keychain back to the file.  │
│ status                Show which provider keys are configured and where they came from.          │
│ save-runtime-key      Save a minted runtime bearer key to the credentials store.                 │
│ refresh-runtime-key   Mint + save a fresh runtime bearer in one step.                            │
│ bootstrap-seed        Mint a fresh bootstrap API key + upload to Key Vault + save locally.       │
│ pull-runtime-key      Pull the bootstrap key from Key Vault into the local credentials store.    │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth bootstrap-seed`

```

 Usage: mdk auth bootstrap-seed [OPTIONS] TARGET

 Mint a fresh bootstrap API key + upload to Key Vault + save locally.

 Solves the chicken-and-egg of fresh deployments: the runtime
 needs a known bearer in its ``api_keys`` table to authenticate
 deploys, but minting that bearer normally requires an existing
 bearer. This command does the one-time setup that breaks the
 cycle:

   1. Mint a fresh `mvt_<env>_<tenant>_<keyid>_<secret>` key
      using the same `mint_api_key()` the runtime would use.
   2. Upload it to Key Vault as the secret `bootstrap-api-key`.
      The Container App's Bicep references this secret as
      `MOVATE_SEED_API_KEY`; on every pod restart the runtime's
      `_seed_bootstrap_key()` inserts the matching ApiKeyRecord
      in the database (idempotent — exists-check skips reseeding).
   3. Save the same value to the local credentials store so
      `mdk deploy --target <name>` works immediately.

 Run this ONCE per environment after `mdk infra apply` (which
 chains into bootstrap-seed automatically by default, so most
 operators never invoke this directly) and before the first
 `mdk deploy`. Subsequent deploys (and revision recycles) keep
 working because the Bicep's secretRef + the runtime's seed code
 together ensure the key is reseeded on every cold start.

 Examples:

   # Fresh dev environment bootstrap:
   $ mdk auth bootstrap-seed dev --keyvault movate-dev-kv-mvt

   # Rotate the bootstrap key (security event, etc.):
   $ mdk auth bootstrap-seed dev --keyvault movate-dev-kv-mvt --force

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    target      TEXT  Deployment target name (from `mdk config list-targets`). [required]       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --keyvault         TEXT  Azure Key Vault name (no FQDN — e.g. `movate-dev-kv-mvt`). The mint  │
│                             result is uploaded as the secret `bootstrap-api-key` which the       │
│                             runtime's Bicep wires as `MOVATE_SEED_API_KEY`.                      │
│                             [required]                                                           │
│    --tenant-id        TEXT  Tenant id baked into the key (≥ 8 chars per TENANT_PREFIX_LEN). The  │
│                             seed key gets `scope=fleet-admin` so it can mint per-tenant keys     │
│                             later.                                                               │
│                             [default: demotenant]                                                │
│    --env              TEXT  Key env class: `live` for production, `test` for staging.            │
│                             [default: live]                                                      │
│    --force                  Overwrite the Key Vault secret if it already exists. Without this    │
│                             flag, the command exits with a hint if the secret is already present │
│                             (so operators don't accidentally rotate the bootstrap key in shared  │
│                             environments).                                                       │
│    --help                   Show this message and exit.                                          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth create-key`

```

 Usage: mdk auth create-key [OPTIONS]

 Mint a new API key.

 Full key is printed to **stdout once** — it is irrecoverable after
 that. The CLI prints a "save this now" warning to **stderr** so
 the warning doesn't pollute scripted ``> /vault.txt`` redirection.

 Scopes (ADR 013 L2) follow least privilege: when ``--scope`` is
 omitted the key gets ``read,run,eval`` (the same grant a scopeless
 legacy key resolves to) — NOT admin. Pass ``--scope admin`` (and/or
 ``fleet-admin``) explicitly for a management key.

 Examples:

   # Interactive use; copy the key into your password manager.
   $ movate auth create-key --tenant-id <uuid> --env live --label ci-bot

   # An admin key that can manage other keys + create agents.
   $ movate auth create-key --tenant-id <uuid> --scope admin,read

   # Scripting: the bare key on stdout, warnings on stderr.
   $ KEY=$(movate auth create-key --tenant-id <uuid> --env live --quiet)

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --tenant-id          TEXT  Tenant id (≥8 chars). [required]                                   │
│    --env                TEXT  `live` or `test`. [default: live]                                  │
│    --label              TEXT  Optional human-readable note.                                      │
│    --scope              TEXT  Least-privilege scope(s) (ADR 013). Repeatable and/or              │
│                               comma-listed: `--scope read,run` or `--scope read --scope run`.    │
│                               Valid: read, run, eval, kb:write, admin, fleet-admin. Omit to      │
│                               default to read,run,eval (matches legacy keys).                    │
│    --quiet      -q            Print only the key_id (for scripting). Disables warnings.          │
│    --help                     Show this message and exit.                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth list-keys`

```

 Usage: mdk auth list-keys [OPTIONS]

 List API keys, newest first.

 Without --target, reads local storage (operator tool).
 With --target, calls GET /api/v1/auth/keys
 on the deployed runtime and shows keys for the calling tenant.

 Examples:

   $ mdk auth list-keys                     # local storage
   $ mdk auth list-keys --target dev        # deployed runtime
   $ mdk auth list-keys --target dev --include-revoked

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --tenant-id                TEXT  Filter to one tenant. Omit for all. Ignored when --target is    │
│                                  used.                                                           │
│ --include-revoked                Show revoked keys too.                                          │
│ --target           -t      TEXT  Query a deployed runtime via HTTP instead of local storage.     │
│                                  Reads the bearer from the target's key_env. Returns keys        │
│                                  belonging to the calling tenant's identity.                     │
│ --help                           Show this message and exit.                                     │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth login`

```

 Usage: mdk auth login [OPTIONS] [PROVIDER]

 Set a provider API key, verify it, persist it for every project.

 With --target, runs the OIDC device-code SSO
 flow for an ``auth='oidc'`` deployment target instead: prints a
 verification URL + user code, waits for browser approval, then caches the
 short-lived token (auto-refreshed on later calls). Humans use this in
 place of long-lived ``mvt_*`` keys.

 Examples:

   # Interactive — prompts for the key, hides input
   $ mdk auth login openai

   # Save to project .env instead of machine-global
   $ mdk auth login anthropic --save-to project

   # CI-style: pass key non-interactively, skip verify
   $ mdk auth login openai --key "$OPENAI_API_KEY" --no-verify

   # SSO device-code login for an oidc target
   $ mdk auth login --target prod

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   provider      [PROVIDER]  Provider to set the API key for: openai, anthropic, azure, gemini,   │
│                             lyzr, deepgram, cartesia, elevenlabs, azure-speech (voice),          │
│                             servicenow, msgraph, workday, salesforce, sap (connectors),          │
│                             telegram, or temporal (durable workflow backend). Omit to pick       │
│                             interactively.                                                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --key                TEXT  Pass the key non-interactively (CI scripts). Without --key, the CLI   │
│                            prompts interactively with hidden input.                              │
│ --no-verify                Skip the live verification call. Useful when the provider is          │
│                            unreachable from the operator's network at setup time.                │
│ --save-to            TEXT  Where to write the key: global (~/.movate/credentials,                │
│                            machine-global) or project (./.env, project-only).                    │
│                            [default: global]                                                     │
│ --target     -t      TEXT  Run SSO device-code login for an auth='oidc' deployment target (ADR   │
│                            013). Mutually exclusive with the provider argument — when set, the   │
│                            provider-key flow is skipped and the IdP device-authorization flow    │
│                            runs instead.                                                         │
│ --help                     Show this message and exit.                                           │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth logout`

```

 Usage: mdk auth logout [OPTIONS]

 Clear the cached SSO token for an OIDC target (ADR 013 L1).

 Removes the access token, refresh token, and expiry cached by
 mdk auth login --target <t> from the credentials store. The
 next authenticated call to that target will require a fresh
 mdk auth login. Idempotent — clearing an already-empty cache
 is a no-op.

 Example:

   $ mdk auth logout --target prod

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --target  -t      TEXT  OIDC deployment target whose cached SSO token to clear. [required]    │
│    --help                  Show this message and exit.                                           │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth pull-runtime-key`

```

 Usage: mdk auth pull-runtime-key [OPTIONS] TARGET

 Pull the bootstrap key from Key Vault into the local credentials store.

 Recovery path when ``~/.movate/credentials`` has been cleared (new
 laptop, new shell user, deliberate rotation of local state) and
 the deployed Container App's `bootstrap-api-key` secret is the
 canonical source of truth. One `az keyvault secret show` + one
 `CredentialsStore.set` — no minting, no `az containerapp exec`,
 no chicken-and-egg.

 Use this AFTER `mdk auth bootstrap-seed <target>` has been run
 once for the environment. To rotate the bootstrap key itself,
 use `mdk auth bootstrap-seed <target> --force` instead.

 Examples:

   # New laptop, dev already provisioned:
   $ mdk auth pull-runtime-key dev --keyvault movate-dev-kv-mvt

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    target      TEXT  Deployment target name (from `mdk config list-targets`). [required]       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --keyvault           TEXT  Azure Key Vault name (no FQDN — e.g. `movate-dev-kv-mvt`). The     │
│                               same vault where `bootstrap-seed` uploaded the secret.             │
│                               [required]                                                         │
│    --secret-name        TEXT  Key Vault secret name to read. Defaults to `bootstrap-api-key`     │
│                               (the value `mdk auth bootstrap-seed` uploads).                     │
│                               [default: bootstrap-api-key]                                       │
│    --help                     Show this message and exit.                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth refresh-runtime-key`

```

 Usage: mdk auth refresh-runtime-key [OPTIONS] TARGET

 Mint + save a fresh runtime bearer in one step.

 Recovery path for the "my saved key returns 401 after a deploy"
 failure mode. The auth design is opaque token + per-key
 `secret_hash + salt` lookup against the runtime's storage (NOT
 JWT signing — there is no shared signing secret to rotate). When
 a Container App revision recycles and the runtime falls back to
 a non-durable storage backend (SQLite-in-pod when MOVATE_DB_URL
 isn't honored), the ApiKeyRecord table vanishes with the pod's
 filesystem and every previously-minted key returns 401.

 Without this command, the operator has to manually:

 1. Find the right subscription / resource group / Container App.
 2. Run `az containerapp exec ... mdk auth create-key`.
 3. Copy the printed key.
 4. Run `mdk auth save-runtime-key <target> <key>`.

 This command does all four steps as one verb. Reads the target
 config to derive the Azure addressing, shells out to
 `az containerapp exec` to mint a fresh key inside the live pod,
 parses the printed `mvt_...` value, and writes it to
 `~/.movate/credentials` for autoload across shells.

 Long-term fix is at the storage layer: `mdk doctor target <name>`
 surfaces whether the runtime is on durable Postgres or
 ephemeral SQLite. If it's the latter, recoveries like this one
 will be needed on every revision recycle.

 Examples:

   # Recover from 401 after a deploy:
   $ mdk auth refresh-runtime-key dev

   # Mint for a non-default tenant:
   $ mdk auth refresh-runtime-key prod --tenant customer-acme --env live

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    target      TEXT  Deployment target name (from `mdk config list-targets`). [required]       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --tenant               TEXT  Tenant id to mint the key for. Defaults to `demotenant` (matches    │
│                              the default used by `mdk auth bootstrap-seed`). Must be at least    │
│                              TENANT_PREFIX_LEN (8) chars — the wire format embeds the first 8    │
│                              characters as the tenant_prefix segment, so anything shorter fails  │
│                              validation.                                                         │
│                              [default: demotenant]                                               │
│ --env                  TEXT  Key env class: `live` for production deploys, `test` for staging.   │
│                              [default: live]                                                     │
│ --label                TEXT  Optional human-readable note attached to the key.                   │
│ --container-app        TEXT  Override the auto-derived Container App name. Default:              │
│                              `movate-{azure_env}-api` (e.g. `movate-dev-api`).                   │
│ --help                       Show this message and exit.                                         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth revoke-all`

```

 Usage: mdk auth revoke-all [OPTIONS]

 Revoke ALL active keys for a tenant — compromise response (ADR 013 D5).

 Destructive. Prompts for confirmation; pass
 -y to skip. Reports how many keys were revoked.

 Safety: pass --except <key_id> to spare one
 key so you keep a working credential. With --target the
 runtime auto-spares your calling key by default (so a remote bulk
 revoke can't lock you out); --except overrides which key
 is spared.

 Without --target, operates on local storage and requires
 --tenant-id. With --target, calls
 POST /api/v1/auth/keys/revoke-all.

 Examples:

   $ mdk auth revoke-all --tenant-id <uuid> --except <keep-this>
   $ mdk auth revoke-all --target dev   # spares your calling key

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --tenant-id          TEXT  Tenant whose keys to bulk-revoke (local mode). Required without       │
│                            --target. Ignored with --target (the runtime uses the caller's        │
│                            tenant).                                                              │
│ --except             TEXT  Key id to SPARE from the bulk revoke (so you aren't locked out). With │
│                            --target this overrides the auto-spare of your calling key.           │
│ --target     -t      TEXT  Bulk-revoke on a deployed runtime via HTTP instead of local storage.  │
│ --yes        -y            Skip the confirm prompt (use in scripts / CI).                        │
│ --help                     Show this message and exit.                                           │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth revoke-key`

```

 Usage: mdk auth revoke-key [OPTIONS] KEY_ID

 Revoke an API key. Idempotent — re-revoking is a silent no-op.

 Prompts ``Revoke key <id>? Y/N`` before doing anything; pass
 ``-y`` to bypass for scripts. In a non-TTY context without
 ``-y`` we abort rather than block — so CI pipelines fail loud
 when they forget the flag instead of hanging.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    key_id      TEXT  Key id to revoke. [required]                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --yes   -y        Skip the confirm prompt (use in scripts / CI).                                 │
│ --help            Show this message and exit.                                                    │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth rotate-key`

```

 Usage: mdk auth rotate-key [OPTIONS] KEY_ID

 Rotate an API key with a zero-downtime grace window (ADR 013 D5).

 Mints a successor (inheriting the old key's env/scopes/label) and keeps
 the OLD key valid for ``--grace`` (default 24h). Both keys
 authenticate until the window lapses, so in-flight clients have time to
 pick up the new key — no downtime. After the window only the successor
 works.

 Prints the new key to stdout **once** (pipe into your vault) and the
 old key's grace-expiry to stderr.

 Without --target, rotates in local storage (operator tool).
 With --target, calls
 POST /api/v1/auth/keys/{key_id}/rotate on the runtime.

 Examples:

   $ NEW=$(mdk auth rotate-key <key_id> --yes)
   $ mdk auth rotate-key <key_id> --grace 7d --target dev

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    key_id      TEXT  Key id of the key to rotate. [required]                                   │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --grace             TEXT     Grace window the OLD key stays valid (zero-downtime). Seconds or a  │
│                              suffix: 24h, 7d, 30m. Default 24h; 0 = immediate cutover; capped at │
│                              30d server-side.                                                    │
│ --ttl-days          INTEGER  Validity of the new (successor) key in days. 0 = no expiry.         │
│                              [default: 90]                                                       │
│ --target    -t      TEXT     Rotate on a deployed runtime via HTTP instead of local storage.     │
│ --yes       -y               Skip the confirm prompt.                                            │
│ --help                       Show this message and exit.                                         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth save-runtime-key`

```

 Usage: mdk auth save-runtime-key [OPTIONS] TARGET KEY

 Save a minted runtime bearer key to the credentials store.

 The bearer-key flow today is two-step: (1) run ``mdk auth
 create-key`` inside the deployed Container App via ``az
 containerapp exec``, copy the printed secret; (2) ``export
 MDK_DEV_KEY=...`` locally. Step 2 has to run in every new shell.

 This command replaces step 2 with a single write to
 ``~/.movate/credentials``. Future shells autoload the variable
 automatically (the loader pattern-matches ``MDK_*_KEY`` entries —
 see :mod:`movate.credentials.loader`).

 Examples:

   # Inline (works but leaks the secret to shell history):
   $ mdk auth save-runtime-key dev mvt_live_demotena_…_…

   # Piped — preferred for the recovery flow (no shell history,
   # no `ps` exposure):
   $ az containerapp exec -g movate-dev-rg -n movate-dev-api \\
       --command "mdk auth create-key --tenant-id demotenant \\
                    --env live --quiet" \\
     | mdk auth save-runtime-key dev -

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    target      TEXT  Deployment target name (from `mdk config list-targets`). [required]       │
│ *    key         TEXT  The full `mvt_<env>_<tenant>_<keyid>_<secret>` value printed by `mdk auth │
│                        create-key`. Quote it if your shell would otherwise interpret special     │
│                        characters. Pass `-` to read the key from stdin instead — recommended for │
│                        piped recovery flows so the secret never lands in shell history or `ps`   │
│                        output.                                                                   │
│                        [required]                                                                │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth status`

```

 Usage: mdk auth status [OPTIONS]

 Show which provider keys are configured and where they came from.

 Renders a table per provider showing the resolved value's source
 (shell / dotenv / credentials_file / unset). Operators see at a
 glance which keys are wired and where to fix gaps.

 With ``--verify``, additionally round-trips each key-auth runtime
 target's saved bearer against its deployed runtime (reusing the same
 admin-scoped probe ``mdk deploy`` / adopt-time verification use) so the
 operator learns whether a saved key *actually authenticates*, not just
 that it's set. This is opt-in because it makes network calls.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --verify          Round-trip each key-auth runtime target's saved bearer against its deployed    │
│                   runtime (one authenticated call per target) and show ✓/✗ + reason. Off by      │
│                   default — this makes network calls. OIDC targets are skipped (their auth model │
│                   differs).                                                                      │
│ --help            Show this message and exit.                                                    │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth use-file`

```

 Usage: mdk auth use-file [OPTIONS]

 Migrate machine-global credentials from the OS keychain back to the file.

 The reverse of mdk auth use-keychain. Copies every entry
 out of the OS keychain into the plaintext ``~/.movate/credentials``
 file (mode 0600). Opt-in and reversible — the keychain
 entry is left intact unless you pass --remove-source.

 Afterwards, unset MOVATE_CRED_BACKEND (or set it to
 ``file``) so ``mdk`` reads from the file again.

 Example:

   $ mdk auth use-file

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --remove-source          After copying, delete the credentials from the keychain backend. Off by │
│                          default so a botched migration never strands your keys.                 │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth use-keychain`

```

 Usage: mdk auth use-keychain [OPTIONS]

 Migrate machine-global credentials from the file into the OS keychain.

 Copies every entry from the plaintext ``~/.movate/credentials`` file
 into the OS keychain (macOS Keychain / Windows Credential Manager /
 Linux Secret Service via the optional ``keyring`` package). The
 migration is opt-in and reversible — the source file is
 left untouched unless you pass --remove-source, so a
 botched migration can never strand your keys.

 Afterwards, set MOVATE_CRED_BACKEND=keychain in your
 shell profile so every ``mdk`` invocation reads from the keychain.

 Needs the optional ``keyring`` dependency: install with
 pip install 'mdk'.

 Examples:

   # Copy keys into the keychain, keep the file as a backup:
   $ mdk auth use-keychain

   # Copy then remove the plaintext file (DLP-clean):
   $ mdk auth use-keychain --remove-source

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --remove-source          After copying, delete the credentials from the file backend. Off by     │
│                          default so a botched migration never strands your keys.                 │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk auth whoami`

```

 Usage: mdk auth whoami [OPTIONS]

 Show the identity of the current API key on a deployed runtime.

 Calls GET /api/v1/auth/me with the bearer token from
 the configured target (or MDK_API_KEY) and prints key_id, tenant,
 env, label, and expiry.

 Examples:

   $ mdk auth whoami --target dev
   $ MDK_API_KEY=mvt_live_... mdk auth whoami

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target  -t      TEXT  Deployment target to query. Reads the bearer from the target's key_env.  │
│                         Omit to use the MDK_API_KEY env var and MDK_RUNTIME_URL.                 │
