### `mdk eval-schedule set`

```

 Usage: mdk eval-schedule set [OPTIONS] AGENT

 Set (or update) an agent's continuous-eval cadence.

 Examples:

   # Cheap mock smoke eval every 30 minutes
   $ mdk eval-schedule set rag-qa --cadence 30m --mock

   # Real eval every 6h, alert on a >3% drop
   $ mdk eval-schedule set rag-qa --cadence 6h --tolerance 0.03 --notify-email me@co.com

 Drive the tick from cron: mdk eval-scheduler-tick every few
 minutes (Azure: a Container Apps Job). The tick only enqueues schedules
 that are actually due.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    agent      TEXT  Agent directory OR bare name (resolved to ./agents/<name>). [required]     │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --cadence             TEXT                       How often to eval: int seconds or a duration │
│                                                     (30m, 6h, 1d).                               │
│                                                     [required]                                   │
│    --mock                                           Use the deterministic MockProvider (cheap    │
│                                                     smoke cadence, no tokens).                   │
│    --runs                INTEGER RANGE [1<=x<=10]   Runs per case. [default: 1]                  │
│    --gate-mode           TEXT                       mean | min | p10. [default: mean]            │
│    --gate                FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Per-case pass score. [default: 0.7]          │
│    --objective           TEXT                       Only eval cases for this objective id        │
│                                                     (sampling).                                  │
│    --tolerance           FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Allowable mean_score/pass_rate drop vs       │
│                                                     baseline before drift fires.                 │
│                                                     [default: 0.05]                              │
│    --baseline-id         TEXT                       Pin a baseline eval_id. Default: diff        │
│                                                     against the prior eval.                      │
│    --notify-email        TEXT                       Email to alert on drift (needs SMTP          │
│                                                     configured).                                 │
│    --disabled                                       Create the schedule but leave it dormant (no │
│                                                     enqueue).                                    │
│    --format              [table|json|markdown]      [default: table]                             │
│    --help                                           Show this message and exit.                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk eval-scheduler-tick`

```

 Usage: mdk eval-scheduler-tick [OPTIONS]

 Run one scheduler tick: enqueue eval jobs for due schedules (ADR 016 D2).

 The cron entrypoint. Drive it from an external scheduler — on Azure a
 Container Apps Job with a cron trigger; locally any cron or a manual run.
 Enqueues a JobKind.EVAL job per due schedule (reusing the
 existing eval-job path) and stamps each so it won't re-enqueue inside its
 cadence window. A running worker then executes the jobs + checks drift.

 Examples:

   # Run the tick (cron calls this on an interval)
   $ mdk eval-scheduler-tick

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --format        [table|json|markdown]  [default: table]                                          │
│ --help                                 Show this message and exit.                               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk eval-scorecard`

```

 Usage: mdk eval-scorecard [OPTIONS] [AGENT]

 Generate test cases on the fly and score against a 10-category scorecard.

 Examples:

   $ mdk eval-scorecard agents/faq
   $ mdk eval-scorecard agents/faq --count 25 --mix edge
   $ mdk eval-scorecard agents/faq --mix adversarial [/dim]
         --judge-model anthropic/claude-haiku-4-5-20251001

   # Project-wide sweep — one scorecard per agent + rollup:
   $ mdk eval-scorecard --all --mix standard

 The 10 categories:

 LLM-judged: accuracy, faithfulness, format, safety, refusal,
 hallucination, completeness, instruction_following.

 Programmatic: latency, cost.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   agent      [AGENT]  Path to the agent directory (e.g. agents/faq). Omit with --all to sweep    │
│                       every agent in the project.                                                │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --all                                                            Run the scorecard against every │
│                                                                  agent under ./agents/ in the    │
│                                                                  current project. Renders a      │
│                                                                  per-agent scorecard for each,   │
│                                                                  then a project-level rollup     │
│                                                                  table at the end. Mutex with    │
│                                                                  the agent argument.             │
│ --count                       -n      INTEGER RANGE [1<=x<=100]  Number of LLM-generated test    │
│                                                                  cases to score (1-100).         │
│                                                                  [default: 10]                   │
│ --mix                                 TEXT                       Test-case mix: standard         │
│                                                                  (typical inputs), edge          │
│                                                                  (boundary/malformed),           │
│                                                                  adversarial (red-team / prompt  │
│                                                                  injection), domain (KB-aware —  │
│                                                                  seeds inputs from the agent's   │
│                                                                  knowledge base and contexts).   │
│                                                                  [default: standard]             │
│ --mock                                                           Use the mock provider for both  │
│                                                                  generation + agent execution    │
│                                                                  (CI / offline).                 │
│ --judge-model                         TEXT                       Override the LLM judge          │
│                                                                  provider/model. Defaults to the │
│                                                                  agent's own model. Example:     │
│                                                                  --judge-model                   │
│                                                                  anthropic/claude-haiku-4-5-202… │
│ --generator-model                     TEXT                       Override the LLM provider/model │
│                                                                  used to GENERATE test cases.    │
│                                                                  Defaults to the agent's own     │
│                                                                  model — but if your shell only  │
│                                                                  has an Anthropic key and the    │
│                                                                  agent uses openai/...,          │
│                                                                  generation fails silently with  │
│                                                                  auth errors. Setting this flag  │
│                                                                  (or its alias --judge-model)    │
│                                                                  routes generation through a     │
│                                                                  provider you actually have keys │
│                                                                  for. Example: --generator-model │
│                                                                  anthropic/claude-haiku-4-5-202… │
│ --target                              TEXT                       Score the agent(s) against a    │
│                                                                  DEPLOYED runtime instead of     │
│                                                                  running locally in-process.     │
│                                                                  Resolves to a target from       │
│                                                                  ~/.movate/config.yaml (URL +    │
│                                                                  key_env env var). Cases are     │
│                                                                  submitted as jobs to the        │
│                                                                  deployment's                    │
│                                                                  /api/v1/agents/<name>/runs      │
│                                                                  endpoint; the LLM judge still   │
│                                                                  runs locally (uses your         │
│                                                                  provider keys, not the          │
│                                                                  deployment's). Useful for       │
│                                                                  scoring what's ACTUALLY in      │
│                                                                  production rather than what     │
│                                                                  your local bundle would do.     │
│                                                                  Same plumbing as mdk run        │
│                                                                  --target.                       │
│ --output                      -o      [table|json|markdown]      Output format. ``table``        │
│                                                                  (default) renders the Rich      │
│                                                                  scorecard for human             │
│                                                                  consumption. ``json`` emits a   │
│                                                                  machine-readable document for   │
│                                                                  CI scraping — suppresses the    │
│                                                                  table + greppable summary line. │
│                                                                  [default: table]                │
│ --gate-overall                        FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Minimum overall mean across all │
│                                                                  10 categories (0.0-1.0).        │
│ --gate-accuracy                       FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Accuracy floor.                 │
│ --gate-faithfulness                   FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Faithfulness floor.             │
│ --gate-format                         FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Format-compliance floor.        │
│ --gate-safety                         FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Safety floor.                   │
│ --gate-refusal                        FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Refusal-appropriateness floor.  │
│ --gate-hallucination                  FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Hallucination floor.            │
│ --gate-completeness                   FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Completeness floor.             │
│ --gate-instruction-following          FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Instruction-following floor.    │
│ --gate-citation-accuracy              FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Citation-accuracy floor. Only   │
│                                                                  meaningful for RAG-style agents │
│                                                                  whose output cites sources.     │
│                                                                  Non-citing agents score 1.0 by  │
│                                                                  convention; this gate is a      │
│                                                                  no-op for them.                 │
│ --gate-latency                        FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Latency-score floor.            │
│ --gate-cost                           FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Cost-score floor.               │
│ --disable-category                    TEXT                       Disable a scorecard category    │
│                                                                  for this run only. Repeatable.  │
│                                                                  Stacks on top of                │
│                                                                  scorecard.disabled_categories   │
│                                                                  in project.yaml. Use to skip a  │
│                                                                  category for a one-off run      │
│                                                                  without editing the project     │
│                                                                  config — e.g. an exploratory    │
│                                                                  run that doesn't care about     │
│                                                                  latency.                        │
│ --baseline-file                       PATH                       Path to a prior scorecard JSON  │
│                                                                  to diff against. Emits a        │
│                                                                  per-category drift table +      │
│                                                                  exits 2 if any category dropped │
│                                                                  by more than                    │
│                                                                  --regression-tolerance. The     │
│                                                                  file shape auto-detects         │
│                                                                  (single-agent vs --all).        │
│ --output-baseline                     PATH                       Write this run's scorecard JSON │
│                                                                  to the given path. Use after a  │
│                                                                  main-branch merge to refresh    │
│                                                                  the committed baseline; CI then │
│                                                                  diffs PRs against it via        │
│                                                                  --baseline-file.                │
│ --regression-tolerance                FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=1.0]  Allowable score drop vs         │
│                                                                  baseline before flagging a      │
│                                                                  regression (0.0-1.0). Default   │
│                                                                  0.0 = any drop is a regression; │
│                                                                  0.05 allows for sampling noise. │
│                                                                  [default: 0.0]                  │
│ --runs                                INTEGER RANGE [1<=x<=10]   Run + judge each case N times   │
│                                                                  and AVERAGE per-category scores │
│                                                                  (1-10). Default 1. Use 3+ to    │
│                                                                  widen the score distribution —  │
│                                                                  at N=1 the LLM judge gives      │
│                                                                  binary-ish rolls, so a 10-case  │
│                                                                  sample often produces every     │
│                                                                  category scoring exactly 1.00   │
│                                                                  (no signal). At N=3 a case      │
│                                                                  rolling 1.0/1.0/0.0 surfaces as │
│                                                                  0.667 instead. Cost scales      │
│                                                                  linearly (N=5 = 5x agent + 5x   │
│                                                                  judge calls per case).          │
│                                                                  [default: 1]                    │
│ --variant                             TEXT                       A/B comparison mode: run the    │
│                                                                  SAME generated cases against a  │
│                                                                  second model and show a         │
│                                                                  side-by-side comparison table.  │
│                                                                  Pass the model string for the   │
│                                                                  challenger (e.g.                │
│                                                                  anthropic/claude-3-5-haiku-202… │
│                                                                  The baseline is the agent's     │
│                                                                  declared model; the variant is  │
│                                                                  the challenger. Cases are       │
│                                                                  generated ONCE and reused for   │
│                                                                  both runs so the comparison is  │
│                                                                  apples-to-apples. Gates still   │
│                                                                  apply to the baseline run only. │
│                                                                  Incompatible with --all (run    │
│                                                                  per-agent instead and compare   │
│                                                                  the resulting tables).          │
│ --yes                         -y                                 Skip the preview confirmation   │
│                                                                  prompt — generate test cases,   │
│                                                                  show the preview table, then    │
│                                                                  proceed directly to scoring     │
│                                                                  without asking 'Score these N   │
│                                                                  cases?'. Useful when you want   │
│                                                                  to SEE the cases before they    │
│                                                                  run but don't need to confirm   │
│                                                                  manually. Has no effect when    │
│                                                                  --no-preview is also set.       │
│ --no-preview                                                     Skip the generate-and-preview   │
│                                                                  step entirely — go straight to  │
│                                                                  scoring (the pre-2026           │
│                                                                  behaviour). Implied in --all    │
│                                                                  mode, JSON output (-o json),    │
│                                                                  and non-TTY contexts (CI        │
│                                                                  pipelines). Use this flag for   │
│                                                                  the same effect in an           │
│                                                                  interactive terminal when you   │
│                                                                  already trust the generator.    │
│ --help                                                           Show this message and exit.     │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk explain`

```

 Usage: mdk explain [OPTIONS] [RUN_ID]

 Render the decision chain behind a completed run.

 Shows the input, LLM call metrics (model, tokens, cost, latency), and
 the final output in the order the executor processed them. When the run
 failed, the error is shown instead of an output section.

 Add ``--steps`` to also see the per-step execution breakdown: a tree of
 LLM turns, each parenting the skill/retrieval calls it dispatched (with
 per-node cost, latency, and tokens), followed by the flat skill-call
 table. No external tracing backend required.

 Examples::

     mdk explain abc123               # explain run abc123 (full id or unique prefix)
     mdk explain --last               # explain the most-recent run
     mdk explain abc123 --json        # machine-readable JSON
     mdk explain --last --steps       # include the per-step turn/skill tree

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   run_id      [RUN_ID]  Run ID to explain (full id or a unique short prefix, e.g. the 8-char id  │
│                         `mdk run` prints). Omit with --last to explain the most-recent run.      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --last           Explain the most-recent run (ignores RUN_ID if both given).                     │
│ --json           Emit machine-readable JSON instead of the human view.                           │
│ --steps          Render the per-step execution breakdown from the executor's tool-use loop: a    │
│                  tree of LLM turns, each parenting the skill/retrieval calls it made (with       │
│                  per-node cost, latency, and tokens), followed by the flat skill-call table. No  │
│                  Langfuse backend required — data is captured by the executor itself (ADR 024).  │
│ --help           Show this message and exit.                                                     │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk export`

```

 Usage: mdk export [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Package movate primitives as portable artifacts. oci-bundle ships an agent as a tar.gz with an OCI
 Artifact Manifest for any container registry.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ oci-bundle   Package an agent as a portable OCI-compatible tar.gz bundle.                        │
│ langgraph    Export a workflow as a standalone LangGraph Python module.                          │
│ temporal     Export a workflow as a standalone Temporal Python module.                           │
│ state        Export operator-critical control-plane state to a portable JSON backup.             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk export langgraph`

```

 Usage: mdk export langgraph [OPTIONS] PATH

 Export a workflow as a standalone LangGraph Python module.

 Compiles the workflow IR to a self-contained Python file with a
 ``StateGraph``, typed state, and a ``build_graph()`` function. The
 generated code does NOT require the mdk runtime — it uses only the
 ``langgraph`` SDK and can be run, customized, or integrated into any
 LangChain/LangGraph pipeline.

 This command does NOT require the ``mdk`` extra — it
 generates code, it doesn't run it.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    path      TEXT  Path to a workflow.yaml file or the workflow directory. [required]          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --output   -o      TEXT  Output file path (default: <workflow-name>_langgraph.py).               │
│ --force                  Overwrite existing file.                                                │
│ --dry-run                Print the generated Python to stdout instead of writing.                │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk export oci-bundle`

```

 Usage: mdk export oci-bundle [OPTIONS] AGENT

 Package an agent as a portable OCI-compatible tar.gz bundle.

 The output is a single tar.gz containing the full agent directory
 plus an oci-manifest.json (OCI Artifact Manifest) and
 a human-readable manifest.yaml. Operators can ship
 the bundle anywhere — registry, S3, scp — and the receiver gets
 everything needed to run the agent.

 Examples:

   $ mdk export oci-bundle triage
   $ mdk export oci-bundle triage --output /tmp/triage.tar.gz
   $ mdk export oci-bundle triage --dry-run

 Future: oras push <registry>/agents/triage:v1 triage.tar.gz
 will work today (the OCI Artifact Manifest is standards-compliant).
 A planned mdk publish (Sprint R+) wraps this.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      AGENT  Agent name (resolved under agents/<name>) or a literal path to an agent    │
│                       directory.                                                                 │
│                       [required]                                                                 │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --output   -o      PATH  Where to write the bundle. Defaults to <agent-name>-<version>.tar.gz in │
│                          the current directory.                                                  │
│ --force    -f            Overwrite the output file if it already exists.                         │
│ --dry-run                Show what would be packaged (files + sizes) without writing. Useful     │
│                          before paying the tarball-write cost on a big agent.                    │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk export state`

```

 Usage: mdk export state [OPTIONS] [FILE]

 Export operator-critical control-plane state to a portable JSON backup.

 Exports the agent registry (all versions), api keys
 (hash+salt only), canary configs, eval/job schedules,
 and per-tenant provider keys (BYOK ciphertext). High-volume /
 reconstructible history (runs, jobs, evals, KB, threads, memory) is
 excluded — the primary DR for history is Azure Postgres PITR
 (see docs/runbooks/dr-backup.md).

 Runs DB-direct against the env-selected backend (MOVATE_DB_URL
 → Postgres, else SQLite). To back up a remote DB, run where that env points.

 Examples:

   # Default-named file in the cwd
   $ mdk export

   # Named, gzipped
   $ MOVATE_DB_URL=postgresql://... mdk export prod-backup.json.gz

   # Stream to stdout (pipe to a vault / object store)
   $ mdk export - | gzip > backup.json.gz

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   file      [FILE]  Where to write the backup. Defaults to ./movate-backup-<ts>.json. A .gz      │
│                     suffix gzips it. Pass - to stream JSON to stdout.                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --force  -f        Overwrite the output file if it already exists.                               │
│ --help             Show this message and exit.                                                   │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk export temporal`

```

 Usage: mdk export temporal [OPTIONS] PATH

 Export a workflow as a standalone Temporal Python module.

 Compiles the workflow IR to a self-contained Python file with a
 ``@workflow.defn`` class, activity stubs, and a ``main()`` that
 executes it. The generated code uses the ``temporalio`` SDK.

 This command does NOT require a running Temporal server — it
 generates code, it doesn't run it. However, ``mdk`` must
 be installed for the compiler to resolve the SDK types.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    path      TEXT  Path to a workflow.yaml file or the workflow directory. [required]          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --output   -o      TEXT  Output file path (default: <workflow-name>_temporal.py).                │
│ --force                  Overwrite existing file.                                                │
│ --dry-run                Print the generated Python to stdout instead of writing.                │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk fix`

```

 Usage: mdk fix [OPTIONS]

 Auto-remediate common diagnostic findings.

 Default is a dry-run preview. Add --apply to actually
 write changes. Use mdk doctor to diagnose first if
 you want the full picture before committing to a fix.

 Examples:

   $ mdk fix                                # preview all fixes
   $ mdk fix --apply                        # write all fixes
   $ mdk fix --only ensure-gitignore --apply  # just one fix
   $ mdk fix --list                         # show fix ids + descriptions

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --apply                Actually write the changes. Default is a --dry-run preview — pass --apply │
│                        to commit.                                                                │
│ --only           TEXT  Run only the named fix(es). Repeatable: --only ensure-gitignore --only    │
│                        ensure-movate-dir. Use mdk fix --list to see all fix ids.                 │
│ --skip           TEXT  Skip the named fix(es). Repeatable. Mutually wins-against --only.         │
│ --list                 List all available fixes (id + label + description) and exit. No          │
│                        diagnosis, no writes.                                                     │
│ --explain        TEXT  Print the full description + current applicability of one fix and exit.   │
│                        Example: --explain ensure-gitignore.                                      │
│ --help                 Show this message and exit.                                               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk fleet`

```

 Usage: mdk fleet [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 READ-ONLY cross-target view of deployed runtimes. Run mdk fleet with no subcommand for the status
 table.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ status   Show health, version, and agent inventory for every configured target.                  │

```

### `mdk fleet logs`

```

 Usage: mdk fleet logs [OPTIONS] TARGET

 Tail recent logs for a target's API Container App (READ-ONLY).

 Shells out to ``az containerapp logs show`` for the
 ``movate-{azure_env}-api`` app — the same name derivation
 ``mdk deploy`` uses. Authenticates from your own ``az login`` session;
 no movate-held secret is passed. The target must carry Azure config
 (``azure_subscription`` / ``azure_resource_group`` / ``azure_env``);
 a pure read-only HTTP target (no deploy config) can't be log-tailed.

 Example:

   $ mdk fleet logs prod --tail 100

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    target      TEXT  Name of a registered target (must have Azure config). [required]          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --tail        INTEGER  Number of recent log lines to show. [default: 50]                         │
│ --help                 Show this message and exit.                                               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk fleet status`

```

 Usage: mdk fleet status [OPTIONS]

 Show health, version, and agent inventory for every configured target.

 Probes every target in ~/.movate/config.yaml concurrently
 with a short per-target timeout, so one dead target doesn't stall the
 view. READ-ONLY — issues only ``GET /healthz`` + ``GET /api/v1/agents``.

 Examples:

   # Human-readable table, active target marked with ●
   $ mdk fleet

   # Machine-readable, e.g. CI health gate
   $ mdk fleet status --json | jq '.[] | select(.reachable == false)'

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --json          Emit a machine-readable JSON array instead of the table (pipe to jq).            │
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk fmt`

```

 Usage: mdk fmt [OPTIONS] [PATHS]...

 Normalize the style of YAML / prompt / JSONL files.

 Default behavior is to rewrite files in place. Use --check
 in CI to fail the build on style drift, or --diff to
 preview changes locally before applying them.

 Examples:

   $ mdk fmt                          # format the whole project
   $ mdk fmt --check                  # CI gate
   $ mdk fmt --diff                   # preview only
   $ mdk fmt agents/triage/           # just one agent

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   paths      [PATHS]...  Files or directories to format. Omit to format the whole project from   │
│                          the current working directory.                                          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --check            CI mode: exit 1 if any file would change, don't write. Mutually exclusive     │
│                    with --diff.                                                                  │
│ --diff             Print unified diff per changed file without writing. Mutually exclusive with  │
│                    --check.                                                                      │
│ --quiet  -q        Only print the summary line; suppress per-file output.                        │
│ --help             Show this message and exit.                                                   │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk graph dashboard`

```

 Usage: mdk graph dashboard [OPTIONS]

 Start the hosted knowledge-graph dashboard and open it in a browser.

 The dashboard extends the base ``mdk graph serve`` viewer with: entity
 search via the runtime API, an analytics sidebar (centrality leaderboard,
 shortest-path finder, community browser), a growth timeline sparkline,
 a project switcher, and KB provenance view on node drill-down.

 Same security model as ``serve``: the runtime bearer stays server-side.
 Use ``--host 0.0.0.0`` for hosted/shared access (the graph API is
 read-only, and the runtime gates writes via its own auth).

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target             TEXT     Deployed runtime target (from ~/.movate/config.yaml). Defaults to  │
│                               the active target. The bearer is resolved from the target's        │
│                               key_env / OIDC and kept server-side.                               │
│ --project            TEXT     Project id whose knowledge graph to explore. Required to load      │
│                               graph data, run analytics, and stream live growth. Env:            │
│                               MDK_GRAPH_PROJECT_ID.                                              │
│                               [env var: MDK_GRAPH_PROJECT_ID]                                    │
│ --runtime-url        TEXT     Headless mode (hosted container, ADR 081): runtime base URL to     │
│                               proxy to, bypassing ~/.movate/config.yaml. Requires --api-key.     │
│                               Env: MDK_GRAPH_RUNTIME_URL.                                        │
│                               [env var: MDK_GRAPH_RUNTIME_URL]                                   │
│ --api-key            TEXT     Headless mode: read-scoped runtime bearer used server-side (never  │
│                               sent to the browser). Requires --runtime-url. Env:                 │
│                               MDK_GRAPH_API_KEY.                                                 │
│                               [env var: MDK_GRAPH_API_KEY]                                       │
│ --port               INTEGER  Bind port for the dashboard. Defaults to 8901. [default: 8901]     │
│ --host               TEXT     Bind host. 127.0.0.1 (default) restricts to localhost. Use 0.0.0.0 │
│                               for hosted/shared access (the graph API is read-only + auth-gated  │
│                               by the runtime).                                                   │
│                               [default: 127.0.0.1]                                               │
│ --no-open                     Don't auto-open the browser.                                       │
│ --help                        Show this message and exit.                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk graph serve`

```

 Usage: mdk graph serve [OPTIONS]

 Start the local knowledge-graph viewer and open it in a browser.

 Resolves the runtime URL + bearer for ``--target``, starts a local proxy
 server, prints the URL, and (unless ``--no-open``) opens it. The bearer
 stays server-side; the browser only ever talks to this local server.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target             TEXT     Deployed runtime target to view (from ~/.movate/config.yaml).      │
│                               Defaults to the active target. The bearer is resolved from the     │
│                               target's key_env / OIDC and kept server-side.                      │
│ --project            TEXT     Project id whose knowledge graph to view. Required to fetch the    │
│                               project graph + live-growth stream. Env: MDK_GRAPH_PROJECT_ID.     │
│                               [env var: MDK_GRAPH_PROJECT_ID]                                    │
│ --runtime-url        TEXT     Headless mode (hosted container, ADR 081): runtime base URL to     │
│                               proxy to, bypassing ~/.movate/config.yaml. Requires --api-key.     │
│                               Env: MDK_GRAPH_RUNTIME_URL.                                        │
│                               [env var: MDK_GRAPH_RUNTIME_URL]                                   │
│ --api-key            TEXT     Headless mode: read-scoped runtime bearer used server-side (never  │
│                               sent to the browser). Requires --runtime-url. Env:                 │
│                               MDK_GRAPH_API_KEY.                                                 │
│                               [env var: MDK_GRAPH_API_KEY]                                       │
│ --port               INTEGER  Local bind port for the viewer. Defaults to 8900. [default: 8900]  │
│ --host               TEXT     Local bind host. 127.0.0.1 (default) restricts to localhost — the  │
│                               right default since the bearer lives in this process.              │
│                               [default: 127.0.0.1]                                               │
│ --no-open                     Don't auto-open the browser (useful for CI / SSH tunnels /         │
│                               headless).                                                         │
│ --help                        Show this message and exit.                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk graph show`

 Usage: mdk graph show [OPTIONS] PROJECT

 Fetch ``project``'s knowledge graph as graphology JSON.

 Prints a summary table by default; ``--json`` emits the graphology
 document verbatim so a client (or ``jq``) consumes it with no

│    --root          TEXT                  Center the window on a node id (bounded k-hop           │
│                                          expansion).                                             │
│    --depth         INTEGER RANGE [x>=1]  Hops from --root (server caps at 6).                    │
│    --limit         INTEGER RANGE [x>=1]  Node/edge cap (server default 500, max 5000).           │

### `mdk guardrails disable`

```

 Usage: mdk guardrails disable [OPTIONS] PATH

 Flip a guardrail's ``enabled: false`` in the project config.

 Same minimal-diff semantics as ``enable``. Other config under the
 module (types, banned_terms, etc.) is preserved — re-enabling
 later restores the previous state without reconfiguration.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    path      TEXT  ``<direction>.<module>`` to disable. [required]                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --config  -c      PATH  Project config file to update. Defaults to ./movate.yaml.                │
│                         [default: movate.yaml]                                                   │
│ --help                  Show this message and exit.                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk guardrails enable`

```

 Usage: mdk guardrails enable [OPTIONS] PATH

 Flip a guardrail's ``enabled: true`` in the project config.

 Minimal-diff write — only the targeted module's ``enabled`` flag
 changes; all other config is preserved. The change is written to
 disk; the executor picks it up on the next ``mdk run``.

 Doesn't fill in surrounding fields (``rubric``, ``banned_terms``,
 etc.) — those are operator decisions; we just flip the bit. After
 enable, run mdk guardrails list to see what's missing.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    path      TEXT  ``<direction>.<module>`` to enable. Valid paths: input.pii, input.topic,    │
│                      input.content, output.pii, output.topic, output.content.                    │
│                      [required]                                                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --config  -c      PATH  Project config file to update. Defaults to ./movate.yaml.                │
│                         [default: movate.yaml]                                                   │
│ --help                  Show this message and exit.                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```
