### `mdk guardrails test`

```

 Usage: mdk guardrails test [OPTIONS] TEXT

 Dry-run a string against the configured guardrails.

 Examples:

 # Test an obvious PII leak (input direction)
 $ mdk guardrails test "reach me at jane@example.com"

 # Same string, output direction
 $ mdk guardrails test "...sensitive..." --direction output

 # Topic restriction check
 $ mdk guardrails test "tell me about Apple products"

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    text      TEXT  Text to dry-run against the configured guardrails. The text is NOT sent to  │
│                      any provider — this is a pure local check using the regex / substring       │
│                      engines.                                                                    │
│                      [required]                                                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --direction  -d      TEXT  Which direction's config to test against: ``input`` (default — checks │
│                            what the agent would see before calling the model) or ``output``      │
│                            (what the model's response would go through before reaching the       │
│                            caller).                                                              │
│                            [default: input]                                                      │
│ --help                     Show this message and exit.                                           │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk import`

```

 Usage: mdk import [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Import agents into MDK from other frameworks (Lyzr today; more later).

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ lyzr      Synthesize an MDK agent from a Lyzr Studio agent JSON definition.                      │
│ json      Generic JSON → MDK agent importer.                                                     │
│ openapi   Import an OpenAPI spec as one skill per operation.                                     │
│ state     Restore a control-plane backup made by mdk export.                                     │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk import json`

```

 Usage: mdk import json [OPTIONS] JSON_FILE

 Generic JSON → MDK agent importer.

 Examples:

   # Import a JSON description into ./agents/<name>/
   $ mdk import json ./exported-agent.json

   # Override the output dir + agent name
   $ mdk import json ./exported-agent.json -o ./customer-agents --name billing-agent

   # Re-import (overwrite existing files)
   $ mdk import json ./exported-agent.json --force

 The original JSON is preserved at ``<agent>/source.json`` for
 diff / audit.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    json_file      FILE  Path to a JSON file describing an MDK agent. [required]                │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --output  -o      PATH  Parent directory for the new agent. Default: ./agents [default: agents]  │
│ --name            TEXT  Override the agent name (otherwise read from the JSON's `name` field or  │
│                         the JSON filename stem). Must be lowercase-alphanumeric-hyphen.          │
│ --force                 Overwrite an existing agent directory of the same name.                  │
│ --help                  Show this message and exit.                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk import lyzr`

```

 Usage: mdk import lyzr [OPTIONS] JSON_FILE

 Synthesize an MDK agent from a Lyzr Studio agent JSON definition.

 Examples:

   # Import as a Lyzr-runtime agent (calls Lyzr at runtime)
   $ mdk import lyzr ./tesla-manager.json

   # Import as MDK-native (migration target — runs through LiteLLM)
   $ mdk import lyzr ./tesla-manager.json --runtime litellm

   # Custom output location
   $ mdk import lyzr ./tesla-manager.json -o ./customer-agents

 The original Lyzr JSON is preserved at ``<agent>/lyzr-original.json``
 for diffing + audit.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    json_file      FILE  Path to a Lyzr agent JSON file (export from Lyzr Studio). [required]   │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --output   -o      PATH  Parent directory for the new agent. Default: ./agents [default: agents] │
│ --runtime          TEXT  MDK runtime for the imported agent. 'lyzr' calls back to Lyzr at        │
│                          inference time (eval/bench an existing agent). 'litellm' makes the      │
│                          agent MDK-native (migration target).                                    │
│                          [default: lyzr]                                                         │
│ --force                  Overwrite existing agent directory of the same name.                    │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk import openapi`

```

 Usage: mdk import openapi [OPTIONS] SPEC

 Import an OpenAPI spec as one skill per operation.

 Examples:

   $ mdk import openapi petstore.yaml
   $ mdk import openapi stripe.json --prefix stripe- --target ./skills/stripe
   $ mdk import openapi spec.json --only getPetById --only listPets
   $ mdk import openapi spec.json --dry-run

 After import, edit each ``skill.yaml`` to:
   • Replace the ``auth`` placeholder with your real env var name
   • Tighten the input schema if you have stricter types than the spec
   • Add a useful ``description`` if the operation's summary was vague

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    spec      PATH  Path to the OpenAPI 3.x spec (JSON or YAML). [required]                     │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target   -t      PATH  Parent directory for the generated skill dirs (default: ./skills/). One │
│                          skill subdirectory per operation.                                       │
│                          [default: skills]                                                       │
│ --prefix           TEXT  Prefix prepended to every generated skill name. Useful for multi-spec   │
│                          imports (e.g. --prefix stripe- so operations from stripe.json don't     │
│                          collide with shopify.json).                                             │
│ --server           TEXT  Override the server URL. Default uses spec.servers[0].url; pass         │
│                          --server to point at a different environment (staging / prod) without   │
│                          editing the spec.                                                       │
│ --only             TEXT  Generate only the named operation(s). Repeatable. Useful when you want  │
│                          one specific skill from a 500-op spec.                                  │
│ --force    -f            Overwrite existing skill directories under --target.                    │
│ --dry-run                Print what would be generated without writing anything.                 │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk import state`

```

 Usage: mdk import state [OPTIONS] FILE

 Restore a control-plane backup made by mdk export.

 Loads the snapshot into the env-selected backend (MOVATE_DB_URL
 → Postgres, else SQLite). Idempotent: ``skip-existing`` (the
 default) leaves rows that already exist untouched, so a re-run imports 0 new
 rows. Reports per-entity imported/skipped counts.

 Provider keys restore as Fernet ciphertext — the target
 environment MUST set the same MOVATE_PROVIDER_KEY_SECRET used
 at export time, or the restored keys won't decrypt at run time (re-set them
 with mdk keys set if the secret differs). Api keys
 restore with their original hash+salt, so every issued key keeps working.

 Examples:

   # Safe restore into a fresh deployment
   $ MOVATE_DB_URL=postgresql://... mdk import movate-backup-....json

   # Force-refresh every row from the backup
   $ mdk import backup.json.gz --mode overwrite

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    file      PATH  The backup file to restore (gzip auto-detected by a .gz suffix). [required] │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --mode          TEXT          skip-existing (safe default — never clobber rows that already      │
│                               exist) or overwrite (re-save every row).                           │
│                               [default: skip-existing]                                           │
│ --format        [table|json]  table | json [default: table]                                      │
│ --help                        Show this message and exit.                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk infra`

```

 Usage: mdk infra [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Provision Azure infrastructure for a movate target. Wraps the Bicep deploy + auto-chains into mdk
 auth bootstrap-seed so a fresh environment becomes one command.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ apply   Provision Azure infrastructure + auto-seed the bootstrap key.                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk infra apply`

```

 Usage: mdk infra apply [OPTIONS] TARGET

 Provision Azure infrastructure + auto-seed the bootstrap key.

 Resolves the target's Azure addressing (subscription + resource
 group + env), pins the subscription via az account set
 if needed, runs az deployment group create against
 the canonical infra/azure/main.bicep, then chains
 into mdk auth bootstrap-seed so the deployed runtime
 has a known seed key before any mdk deploy.

 Examples:

   # Fresh environment bootstrap, end to end:
   $ mdk infra apply dev --keyvault movate-dev-kv-mvt

   # Re-apply infra after a Bicep change (skip seed —
   # the bootstrap key already exists):
   $ mdk infra apply dev --no-seed

   # Preview the az command without executing:
   $ mdk infra apply dev --keyvault movate-dev-kv-mvt --dry-run

   # Override the param file (CI / staging):
   $ mdk infra apply staging --keyvault movate-staging-kv-mvt \\
       --parameters infra/azure/main.staging.bicepparam

 Exit codes:

 * 0 — Bicep applied + seed minted (or seed skipped via --no-seed)
 * 1 — Bicep deploy failed (operator sees az stderr verbatim)
 * 2 — config / argument error before any az call ran

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    target      TEXT  Deployment target name (from `mdk config list-targets`). [required]       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --keyvault            TEXT  Azure Key Vault name (no FQDN — e.g. `movate-dev-kv-mvt`). Required  │
│                             when --no-seed isn't set, because the auto-chain into bootstrap-seed │
│                             needs to know where to upload the secret. With --no-seed, the        │
│                             operator owns secret population separately.                          │
│ --bicep               TEXT  Path to the Bicep template, relative to cwd. Defaults to             │
│                             infra/azure/main.bicep — the canonical entry point in the movate-cli │
│                             source tree.                                                         │
│                             [default: infra/azure/main.bicep]                                    │
│ --parameters  -p      TEXT  Path to a .bicepparam file. When omitted, defaults to                │
│                             infra/azure/main.<env>.bicepparam (derived from the target's         │
│                             azure_env). Pass @<file>-style overrides on the az command line via  │
│                             --az-arg.                                                            │
│ --name        -n      TEXT  Deployment name passed to az deployment group create -n. Defaults to │
│                             main — overwrites the same named deployment each apply (the Bicep    │
│                             template itself is idempotent).                                      │
│                             [default: main]                                                      │
│ --no-seed                   Skip the auto-chain into mdk auth bootstrap-seed after a successful  │
│                             Bicep deploy. Use this when the bootstrap key was already minted in  │
│                             a prior run + you just want to refresh infra (e.g. scale changes),   │
│                             or when you intend to mint the seed key manually for an unusual      │
│                             tenant id.                                                           │
│ --dry-run                   Print the az deployment group create command that WOULD run, plus    │
│                             the bootstrap-seed follow-up, without executing either. Nothing on   │
│                             Azure is touched.                                                    │
│ --help                      Show this message and exit.                                          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk init`

```

 Usage: mdk init [OPTIONS] [NAME] [DESCRIPTION]

 Scaffold a new agent or project — always leaving a runnable result.

 mdk init is context-aware (ADR 026). The DEFAULT does the
 intuitive thing for where you are:

   Outside a project → bootstrap a runnable PROJECT
     (project.yaml + AGENTS.md + .env.example + .gitignore + agents/ +
     an initial snapshot baseline). Add -t / --llm
     / a description and the agent lands under agents/<name>/
     so mdk run <name> works from the project root.
   Inside a project → ADD the agent under
     agents/<name>/ (same as mdk add).
   --bare → a STANDALONE single-dir agent (no project) — run
     it with mdk run . from inside the folder.

 --llm "<description>" LLM-generates the agent: a shape-aware
 (Q&A / classifier / extractor / RAG / tool-use) agent.yaml +
 prompt.md + schemas + seed eval cases. If the description
 contains a URL it auto-crawls + ingests that page into the agent's KB
 then runs a grounded verify; a tool-use intent scaffolds a runnable skill
 STUB; under --mock it also runs a post-scaffold eval baseline.
 Set a persistent scaffolder model with
 mdk config set scaffold.model <model>.

 Available agent templates:

   default    — minimal echo agent (string-in, string-out)
   faq        — question → answer + confidence
   summarizer — text + max_words → summary + word_count
   classifier — text + labels → chosen label
   chatbot    — message → reply (designed for `mdk chat`)
   extractor  — text → strict typed fields
   (more role templates available — see `mdk add --list`)

 Examples:

   $ mdk init my-proj                          # new project (empty agents/)
   $ mdk init faq-agent -t faq                 # new project + the faq agent
   $ mdk init faq-agent --llm "FAQ bot for our SaaS pricing"  # LLM-generated
   $ mdk init sitebot "answer questions about https://example.com"  # crawl + ground
   $ mdk init triager -t ticket-triager        # (run inside a project → adds it)
   $ mdk init scratch --bare                   # standalone agent (mdk run .)
   $ mdk init --project                        # bootstrap current dir in place

 See also:
   mdk dev <name> — the guided front door: scaffolds (if
     needed) then drops you into a live edit → test → deploy loop.
   mdk run <name> / validate <name> — resolve an
     agent by name from the project root; use mdk run . for a
     standalone agent.
   mdk add <template> — drop another role agent into this
     project (mdk add --list for the catalog).
   mdk kb ingest <agent> <url|path> — populate a grounded
     agent's KB (e.g. when --llm had no URL to crawl).
   mdk report — offline rollup of how your agents are doing.
   mdk authoring audit / replay — the copilot's
     reversible-action audit log.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   name             [NAME]         Name for the project (outside a project) or the agent (inside  │
│                                   a project, or with -t/--llm/--bare). Lowercase, hyphenated.    │
│                                   Omit with --project to bootstrap the current directory in      │
│                                   place.                                                         │
│   description      [DESCRIPTION]  Optional natural-language description. When set, treated as    │
│                                   shorthand for --llm (LLM-generates the agent): mdk init        │
│                                   faq-agent "FAQ agent for our SaaS pricing".                    │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --project                                          Explicitly bootstrap just the project         │
│                                                    workspace (back-compat flag — outside a       │
│                                                    project this is already the default). Creates │
│                                                    project.yaml + AGENTS.md + .env.example +     │
│                                                    .gitignore + an empty agents/ + an initial    │
│                                                    snapshot.                                     │
│ --template        -t                      TEXT     Template to scaffold the agent from. One of:  │
│                                                    calc-agent, chatbot, classifier,              │
│                                                    code-reviewer, compliance-checker, default,   │
│                                                    email-responder, extractor, faq, hr-policy,   │
│                                                    lead-qualifier, lookup-agent,                 │
│                                                    meeting-summarizer, rag-qa, research-agent,   │
│                                                    resume-screener, sql-writer, summarizer,      │
│                                                    ticket-triager. Setting it scaffolds an agent │
│                                                    (under agents/<name>/ in the project, or      │
│                                                    standalone with --bare). Bare mdk init <name> │
│                                                    (no -t, no --llm) outside a project just      │
│                                                    bootstraps the project with an empty agents/. │
│ --pattern                                 TEXT     Scaffold a GOVERNED agent-pattern template    │
│                                                    (ADR 038). One of: chatbot, goal-oriented,    │
│                                                    monitor, simulation, task-oriented. Sugar     │
│                                                    that resolves to the matching pattern         │
│                                                    template — chatbot scaffolds a single agent;  │
│                                                    the others scaffold a WORKFLOW bundle         │
│                                                    (workflow.yaml + nested agents/) under        │
│                                                    workflows/<name>/. Each bakes in bounds +     │
│                                                    budgets + eval-gates. See mdk patterns list.  │
│                                                    Mutually exclusive with -t/--llm.             │
│ --target,--at                             PATH     Where to scaffold the new agent / project.    │
│                                                    PARENT directory: the agent or project ends   │
│                                                    up at <target>/<name>/. Accepts absolute      │
│                                                    paths (~/projects, /abs/path) and the --at    │
│                                                    alias which reads more naturally for          │
│                                                    --project (e.g. mdk init --project foo --at   │
│                                                    ~/work).                                      │
│                                                    [default: .]                                  │
│ --force                                            Overwrite existing directory.                 │
│ --skip-snapshot                                    Skip creating the initial snapshot in         │
│                                                    --project mode. Mostly for tests; production  │
│                                                    use should keep the baseline.                 │
│ --with-agents                             TEXT     Comma-separated role templates to scaffold    │
│                                                    immediately after the project is created.     │
│                                                    Only meaningful with --project. Example:      │
│                                                    --with-agents                                 │
│                                                    rag-qa,ticket-triager,code-reviewer           │
│                                                    bootstraps a support workspace in one         │
│                                                    command.                                      │
│ --llm                                     TEXT     Natural-language description of the agent.    │
│                                                    The CLI uses an LLM to generate agent.yaml +  │
│                                                    prompt.md + schemas + seed eval cases.        │
│                                                    Validates by loading the result back; retries │
│                                                    once on failure. Pair with --mock for         │
│                                                    hermetic CI.                                  │
│ --llm-model                               TEXT     Model to use when --llm is set. Defaults to   │
│                                                    openai/gpt-4o-mini-2024-07-18 (cheap,         │
│                                                    reliable JSON output).                        │
│                                                    [default: openai/gpt-4o-mini-2024-07-18]      │
│ --dry-run                                          Still calls the model (needs a provider key)  │
│                                                    and previews the generated agent without      │
│                                                    writing any files. For offline previews with  │
│                                                    no key, add --mock. Only meaningful with      │
│                                                    --llm; ignored otherwise.                     │
│ --mock                                             Offline path: uses the deterministic mock     │
│                                                    provider (no API key) to write a generic      │
│                                                    scaffold — no real model is called. For       │
│                                                    hermetic CI. Only meaningful with --llm;      │
│                                                    ignored otherwise.                            │
│ --no-ingest                                        Skip the auto-ingest step. By default, when   │
│                                                    an --llm description contains a URL and       │
│                                                    scaffolds a grounded (RAG) agent, mdk init    │
│                                                    crawls that URL into the new agent's KB so it │
│                                                    can answer immediately. Pass --no-ingest for  │
│                                                    a scaffold-only run (you can ingest later     │
│                                                    with mdk kb ingest). Auto-ingest is always    │
│                                                    skipped under --mock / --dry-run (no          │
│                                                    network).                                     │
│ --no-verify                                        Skip the post-scaffold grounded verify (F8).  │
│                                                    By default, after an --llm description        │
│                                                    scaffolds a grounded (RAG) agent AND          │
│                                                    auto-ingest populates its KB, mdk init runs   │
│                                                    ONE probe query through the new agent to      │
│                                                    confirm it answers grounded from the KB. The  │
│                                                    verify is best-effort + never changes the     │
│                                                    exit code on a successfully-scaffolded agent. │
│                                                    It's skipped automatically when there is      │
│                                                    nothing to verify (non-grounding scaffold,    │
│                                                    --no-ingest, or an empty KB); under --mock it │
│                                                    runs a structural smoke only (the agent       │
│                                                    executes against the mock provider, no real   │
│                                                    grounding is asserted). Independent of        │
│                                                    --no-ingest.                                  │
│ --no-baseline                                      Skip the post-scaffold eval baseline (F4').   │
│                                                    By default, after a template or --llm         │
│                                                    scaffold AND when run under --mock, mdk init  │
│                                                    runs the new agent's eval dataset through the │
│                                                    deterministic mock provider and prints a      │
│                                                    one-line baseline pass-rate (e.g. baseline:   │
│                                                    5/5 cases pass under --mock) — a known-good   │
│                                                    starting point that also catches a template   │
│                                                    whose evals don't run. Best-effort + never    │
│                                                    changes the exit code on a                    │
│                                                    successfully-scaffolded agent. It runs only   │
│                                                    under --mock (a hermetic, zero-cost step);    │
│                                                    without --mock measure anytime with mdk eval  │
│                                                    --mock.                                       │
│ --shape                                   TEXT     ADR 029: explicit override for what --llm     │
│                                                    should scaffold. single-agent (a agent.yaml + │
│                                                    prompt + schemas + evals), workflow (a        │
│                                                    multi-step pipeline: workflow.yaml + state    │
│                                                    schema + N constituent agents +               │
│                                                    workflow-level evals). Default is auto — the  │
│                                                    planner sniffs the description for step       │
│                                                    markers (step 1 → step 2, →, then ... then,   │
│                                                    pipeline of, multi-step) and picks. Workflows │
│                                                    land under workflows/<name>/ in a project (or │
│                                                    beside the current dir with --bare).          │
│ --workflow-nodes                          INTEGER  ADR 029: advanced — cap the planner at N      │
│                                                    constituent agents in workflow shape. Default │
│                                                    auto (planner picks 2-4 from the              │
│                                                    description); hard ceiling is 6 to keep       │
│                                                    generation cost bounded. Only meaningful with │
│                                                    --shape workflow (or an auto-detected         │
│                                                    workflow shape).                              │
│ --open-editor         --no-open-editor             After project mode creates the workspace,     │
│                                                    launch VS Code (or Cursor, or open the folder │
│                                                    in Finder on macOS) on the new project.       │
│                                                    Default ON when an editor is on PATH and      │
│                                                    stdout is a tty; pass --no-open-editor in CI  │
│                                                    / headless environments. The same option is   │
│                                                    offered as a menu pick afterwards so the      │
│                                                    operator can still launch it manually if      │
│                                                    auto-launch was skipped.                      │
│                                                    [default: open-editor]                        │
│ --bare                                             Escape hatch (ADR 026 D1): scaffold a         │
│                                                    STANDALONE single-dir agent at                │
│                                                    <target>/<name>/ — no project.yaml, no        │
│                                                    agents/ wrapper. The pre-ADR-026 -t / --llm   │
│                                                    output. Use it to drop an agent into a        │
│                                                    non-mdk repo or for a quick throwaway         │
│                                                    experiment; run it with mdk run . from inside │
│                                                    the dir. Without --bare, mdk init <name>      │
│                                                    -t/--llm yields a runnable PROJECT (or adds   │
│                                                    to the current one when inside a project).    │
│ --help                                             Show this message and exit.                   │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk inspect`

```

 Usage: mdk inspect [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Show the resolved view of an agent / workflow / skill — defaults applied, schemas compiled,
 contexts prepended. Different from mdk show (which prints raw YAML fields).

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ agent   Show the resolved view of an agent — what the executor sees.                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk inspect agent`

```

 Usage: mdk inspect agent [OPTIONS] AGENT

 Show the resolved view of an agent — what the executor sees.

 Different from mdk show (raw YAML fields). inspect
 walks the agent through the same loader the executor uses, then
 surfaces every layer that contributed to the final state:

   • Model defaults from movate.yaml / policy.yaml
   • JSON Schemas after inline-shorthand expansion
   • Contexts prepended to the prompt
   • Skills resolved through the registry (backend + entry)

 Examples:

   $ mdk inspect agent triage                  # full resolved view
   $ mdk inspect agent triage --only prompt    # just the prompt
   $ mdk inspect agent triage --only model --only schemas
   $ mdk inspect agent triage --json | jq '.model'

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      AGENT  Agent name (resolved under agents/<name>) or a literal path to an agent    │
│                       directory.                                                                 │
│                       [required]                                                                 │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --only        TEXT  Show only the named section(s). Repeatable. Valid ids: identity, model,      │
│                     prompt, schemas, skills, contexts. Default: show every section.              │
│ --json              Emit the resolved bundle as JSON — pipe-friendly for CI / jq.                │
│ --raw               Also print the raw agent.yaml + prompt.md alongside the resolved view. Makes │
│                     "what changed under resolution?" debugging trivial — both sides on screen at │
│                     once.                                                                        │
│ --help              Show this message and exit.                                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk jobs`

```

 Usage: mdk jobs [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Inspect jobs on a deployed movate runtime.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ show          Show the current state of one job.                                                 │
│ wait          Block on a job until it reaches a terminal state.                                  │
│ cancel        Cooperatively cancel a queued or running job.                                      │
│ list          List this tenant's recent jobs on the target runtime, newest first.                │
│ list-agents   List agents registered on the target runtime.                                      │
│ reap          Run the stale-job reaper once against the LOCAL runtime.                           │
│ dead-letter   Manage retry-exhausted (dead-letter) jobs: list, show, retry, purge.               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk jobs cancel`

```

 Usage: mdk jobs cancel [OPTIONS] JOB_ID

 Cooperatively cancel a queued or running job.

 A queued job is cancelled immediately (it's never
 executed). A running job is flagged: the worker finishes
 its in-flight work (cancellation is cooperative — there is no
 mid-LLM-call interruption), then discards the result and records the
 job as cancelled. An already-finished job is a no-op.

 Requires the run scope on the API key.

   $ movate jobs cancel "$JOB_ID"

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    job_id      TEXT  Job id from `movate submit`. [required]                                   │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target  -t      TEXT          Deployment target name.                                          │
│ --output  -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                                 │
│ --help                          Show this message and exit.                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk jobs dead-letter`

```

 Usage: mdk jobs dead-letter [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Manage retry-exhausted (dead-letter) jobs: list, show, retry, purge.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ list    List this tenant's retry-exhausted (dead-letter) jobs, newest first.                     │
│ show    Show one dead-letter job's full state (incl. the failure error).                         │
│ retry   Requeue a dead-letter job (or --all) back onto the queue.                                │
│ purge   Permanently delete this tenant's dead-letter jobs.                                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk jobs dead-letter list`

```

 Usage: mdk jobs dead-letter list [OPTIONS]

 List this tenant's retry-exhausted (dead-letter) jobs, newest first.

 Examples:

 # All dead-letters on the active target
 $ movate jobs dead-letter list

 # Just one agent's, pipe-friendly
 $ movate jobs dead-letter list -a faq-agent -o json | jq '.jobs[].job_id'

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --agent   -a      TEXT          Only dead-letters for this agent/workflow name.                  │
│ --limit   -n      INTEGER       Max rows (server caps at 100). [default: 20]                     │
│ --target  -t      TEXT          Deployment target name.                                          │
│ --output  -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                                 │
│ --help                          Show this message and exit.                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk jobs dead-letter purge`

```

 Usage: mdk jobs dead-letter purge [OPTIONS]

 Permanently delete this tenant's dead-letter jobs.

 Destructive + irreversible. Requires the admin scope.
 Prompts for confirmation unless --yes is passed (or
 -o json, which is non-interactive). ``--before`` keeps
 recent dead-letters and prunes only stale ones.

   $ movate jobs dead-letter purge --before 2026-05-01 --yes

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --before          TEXT          Only purge dead-letters completed before this ISO-8601 instant   │
│                                 (e.g. 2026-05-01).                                               │
│ --yes     -y                    Skip the confirmation prompt.                                    │
│ --target  -t      TEXT          Deployment target name.                                          │
│ --output  -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                                 │
│ --help                          Show this message and exit.                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk jobs dead-letter retry`

```

 Usage: mdk jobs dead-letter retry [OPTIONS] [JOB_ID]

 Requeue a dead-letter job (or --all) back onto the queue.

 Resets the job to a fresh queued state (attempt budget
 cleared) so the worker picks it up again. Requires the run
 scope on the API key.

   # One job
   $ movate jobs dead-letter retry "$JOB_ID"

   # Every dead-letter for the tenant
   $ movate jobs dead-letter retry --all

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   job_id      [JOB_ID]  Dead-letter job id to requeue. Omit with --all to requeue every one.     │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --all                           Requeue every dead-letter job for this tenant.                   │
│ --target  -t      TEXT          Deployment target name.                                          │
│ --output  -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                                 │
│ --help                          Show this message and exit.                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk jobs dead-letter show`

```

 Usage: mdk jobs dead-letter show [OPTIONS] JOB_ID

 Show one dead-letter job's full state (incl. the failure error).

 Reuses the standard job-poll route — the id just happens to be a
 dead-lettered job. Exits 1 (the job is in a failed terminal state).

│ --output  -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                                 │
│ --help                          Show this message and exit.                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk jobs list`

```

 Usage: mdk jobs list [OPTIONS]

 List this tenant's recent jobs on the target runtime, newest first.

 Examples:

 # 20 most recent jobs on the active target
 $ movate jobs list

 # Just failures, last 50
 $ movate jobs list -s error -n 50

 # In-flight jobs only, pipe-friendly

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --status  -s      [queued|running|success|error|safety_  Only show jobs in this state (queued,   │
│                   blocked|dead_letter|cancelled]         running, success, error,                │
│                                                          safety_blocked).                        │
│ --limit   -n      INTEGER                                Max rows to return (server caps at      │
│                                                          100).                                   │
│                                                          [default: 20]                           │
│ --target  -t      TEXT                                   Deployment target name.                 │
│ --output  -o      [table|json]                           [default: table]                        │
│ --help                                                   Show this message and exit.             │

### `mdk jobs reap`

```

 Usage: mdk jobs reap [OPTIONS]

 Run the stale-job reaper once against the LOCAL runtime.

 Crash-recovery one-shot: finds jobs orphaned in RUNNING past the
 visibility timeout and requeues them (or dead-letters once the retry
 budget is exhausted). Mirrors how mdk scheduler-tick runs
 locally — it builds the local runtime and calls the storage reaper
 directly; it does NOT hit a deployed runtime's HTTP API.

 In production the worker loop + scheduler tick run this automatically;
 this command is an operator escape hatch for the local queue.

 Examples:

   # Reclaim stale jobs with the default timeout
   $ mdk jobs reap

   # Treat jobs stuck >1h as orphaned
   $ mdk jobs reap --visibility-timeout 3600

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --visibility-timeout          FLOAT         Seconds a job may sit in RUNNING before it's treated │
│                                             as orphaned and reclaimed. Defaults to the 15-min    │
│                                             reaper default. Must be generously larger than the   │
│                                             longest expected job.                                │
│ --output              -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                     │
│ --help                                      Show this message and exit.                          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk jobs show`

╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target  -t      TEXT          Deployment target name.                                          │
│ --output  -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                                 │

### `mdk jobs wait`

```

 Block on a job until it reaches a terminal state.

 Use when you submitted with fire-and-forget and now want to wait:

 $ JOB_ID=$(movate submit faq-agent '{"text": "..."}' | jq -r .job_id)

│ --poll-interval          FLOAT         Seconds between polls. [default: 1.0]                     │
│ --output         -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                          │
