### `mdk judge`

```

 Usage: mdk judge [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Author + commit an LLM-as-judge rubric (evals/judge.yaml) for an agent. Claude reads the agent's
 spec and writes a rubric covering the requested (or inferred) scoring dimensions.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ generate   Author a complete evals/judge.yaml for <agent>.                                       │
│ commit     Commit a reviewed judge.yaml to the agent.                                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk judge commit`

```

 Usage: mdk judge commit [OPTIONS] AGENT

 Commit a reviewed judge.yaml to the agent.

 The runtime re-validates the YAML against JudgeConfig
 before any byte hits disk — a malformed hand edit is rejected with
 422 and the agent's existing judge.yaml stays put.

 Example:

   # Round-trip: generate, edit, commit
   $ mdk judge generate rag-qa -o judge.yaml
   $ vim judge.yaml
   $ mdk judge commit rag-qa --yaml judge.yaml

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    agent      TEXT  Agent name registered on the target runtime. [required]                    │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --yaml    -y      PATH  Path to the reviewed judge.yaml body to commit. Use - to read from    │
│                            stdin.                                                                │
│                            [required]                                                            │
│    --target  -t      TEXT  Deployment target name. Omit to use the active target.                │
│    --help                  Show this message and exit.                                           │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk judge generate`

```

 Usage: mdk judge generate [OPTIONS] AGENT

 Author a complete evals/judge.yaml for <agent>.

 Examples:

   # Let Claude infer dimensions; print to stdout
   $ mdk judge generate rag-qa

   # Specific dimensions; write to file for review
   $ mdk judge generate rag-qa -d accuracy,tone -o judge.yaml

   # Hermetic / offline (MockProvider on the server)
   $ mdk judge generate rag-qa --mock

 This does NOT modify the agent. Review the output, edit
 if needed, then commit with mdk judge commit.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    agent      TEXT  Agent name registered on the target runtime. [required]                    │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --dimensions        -d                   TEXT                        Comma-separated list of     │
│                                                                      rubric dimensions (e.g.     │
│                                                                      accuracy,tone,schema_adher… │
│                                                                      Omit to let the engineer    │
│                                                                      infer a sensible set from   │
│                                                                      the agent's shape.          │
│ --include-examples      --no-examples                                Anchor the rubric with 2-3  │
│                                                                      concrete scored examples.   │
│                                                                      Default on; pass            │
│                                                                      --no-examples for a leaner  │
│                                                                      rubric when the agent has   │
│                                                                      no dataset yet.             │
│                                                                      [default: include-examples] │
│ --model             -m                   TEXT                        Optional LiteLLM-style      │
│                                                                      provider/model for the      │
│                                                                      ENGINEER model that authors │
│                                                                      the rubric (distinct from   │
│                                                                      the judge model the         │
│                                                                      generated YAML uses at eval │
│                                                                      time).                      │
│ --budget-usd                             FLOAT RANGE [0.0<=x<=10.0]  Hard ceiling on the         │
│                                                                      generation call's cost in   │
│                                                                      USD.                        │
│                                                                      [default: 0.1]              │
│ --target            -t                   TEXT                        Deployment target name      │
│                                                                      (from `mdk config           │
│                                                                      list-targets`). Omit to use │
│                                                                      the active target.          │
│ --output            -o                   PATH                        Write the generated YAML    │
│                                                                      here. Use - for stdout.     │
│                                                                      Defaults to stdout —        │
│                                                                      review, edit, then mdk      │
│                                                                      judge commit.               │
│ --mock                                                               Use the deterministic       │
│                                                                      MockProvider on the server  │
│                                                                      (no API key needed). For    │
│                                                                      hermetic CI + offline demos │
│                                                                      — the resulting rubric is a │
│                                                                      canned anchor, not authored │
│                                                                      from the agent's spec.      │
│ --format            -f                   [table|json]                Summary output format (yaml │
│                                                                      body is always              │
│                                                                      printed/written).           │
│                                                                      [default: table]            │
│ --help                                                               Show this message and exit. │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk kb`

```

 Usage: mdk kb [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Knowledge-base ingest + search. Run mdk kb with no arguments for an interactive guided menu.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ ingest       Ingest a knowledge-base file, directory, or web page into ``agent``'s KB.           │
│ search       Semantic search over ``agent``'s KB. Prints top-K with scores.                      │
│ list         List chunks in ``agent``'s KB. Useful for debugging                                 │
│              "is my content actually in there?" without dropping into SQL.                       │
│ stats        Summary stats for ``agent``'s KB: chunk count, source                               │
│              breakdown, embedding model(s) in use, total + per-source character                  │
│              counts. Useful for sanity-checking after a big ingest.                              │
│ ingest-all   Scan the project and ingest every KB directory found.                               │
│ clear        Delete chunks from ``agent``'s KB. Use ``--source`` to remove                       │
│              just one document; omit for a full wipe. Confirmation required                      │
│              unless ``--yes`` is set.                                                            │
│ reindex      Rebuild ``agent``'s KB vector index.                                                │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk kb clear`

```

 Usage: mdk kb clear [OPTIONS] [AGENT]

 Delete chunks from ``agent``'s KB. Use ``--source`` to remove just one document; omit for a full
 wipe. Confirmation required unless ``--yes`` is set.

 Omit ``agent`` for an interactive picker. Pass ``--target`` to clear
 a deployed agent's KB instead of the local store.

 Examples:

   # Drop just one stale document
   $ mdk kb clear faq-agent --source handbook.md

   # Full wipe, no prompt (CI)
   $ mdk kb clear faq-agent --yes

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   agent      [AGENT]  Agent whose KB to clear. Omit for picker.                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --source             TEXT  Only delete chunks from this source path. Omit to wipe the agent's    │
│                            entire KB.                                                            │
│ --tenant-id          TEXT  Tenant scope. [default: local]                                        │
│ --yes        -y            Skip the confirmation prompt (CI / scripting).                        │
│ --target             TEXT  Clear a DEPLOYED runtime's KB instead of the local store. Resolves    │
│                            URL + bearer from ~/.movate/config.yaml and calls DELETE              │
│                            /api/v1/agents/<agent>/kb (with ?source= when --source is set). The   │
│                            runtime scopes by its own auth tenant, so --tenant-id is ignored on   │
│                            the remote path.                                                      │
│ --help                     Show this message and exit.                                           │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk kb ingest`

```

 Usage: mdk kb ingest [OPTIONS] [AGENT] [PATH_OR_URL]

 Ingest a knowledge-base file, directory, or web page into ``agent``'s KB.

 The source can be a filesystem path (file or directory) OR a single
 web-page URL starting with ``http://`` / ``https://`` — a URL is
 fetched, stripped to readable text, and chunked + embedded + stored
 through the same pipeline local files use (so ``mdk kb stats`` /
 ``search`` see it identically, with the URL as the source).

 Both arguments are optional — omit them to get an interactive picker
 that auto-detects agents in the current project and defaults the
 path to ``agents/<agent>/kb/``.

 Use ``--dry-run`` to preview chunk count + size distribution
 without consuming any embedding budget. Useful when tuning a
 new corpus before committing to the real ingest.

 Use ``--model`` to select a non-default embedding provider, e.g.
 ``--model cohere/embed-english-v3.0``. The model used at ingest
 MUST match the model used at search time.

 Use ``--clean-source`` when updating an existing document to remove
 stale chunks before writing new ones.

 Use ``--ocr-lang`` / ``--ocr-backend`` for non-English or noisy scans.

 Examples:

   # Ingest an agent's kb/ directory locally
   $ mdk kb ingest faq-agent agents/faq-agent/kb/

   # Preview chunking without spending embedding budget
   $ mdk kb ingest faq-agent ./docs --dry-run

   # Ingest a single web page
   $ mdk kb ingest faq-agent https://example.com/handbook

   # Upload to a deployed runtime's KB
   $ mdk kb ingest faq-agent ./docs --target prod

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   agent       [AGENT]        Agent name (must match a directory under ./agents/ — we don't       │
│                              enforce this at the storage layer, but the skill-side lookup at run │
│                              time scopes by agent so a mismatch returns no results). Omit for    │
│                              interactive picker.                                                 │
│   source      [PATH_OR_URL]  File or directory to ingest, OR a single web-page URL (starts with  │
│                              http:// or https://). Directories are walked recursively; supported │
│                              file formats: .md, .txt, .pdf, .docx, .html, .png, .jpg, .jpeg,     │
│                              .tiff. Hidden dirs (.git, .venv) skipped. A URL is fetched,         │
│                              stripped to readable text, and ingested through the same pipeline.  │
│                              Defaults to agents/<agent>/kb/ when omitted.                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --tenant-id           TEXT     Tenant scope. Defaults to 'local' for CLI use. Override in        │
│                                production where the tenant comes from the auth context.          │
│                                [default: local]                                                  │
│ --model               TEXT     Embedding model. Bare names (``text-embedding-3-small``) and      │
│                                ``openai/`` prefixed strings go directly to OpenAI. Any other     │
│                                ``provider/model`` string (``cohere/embed-english-v3.0``,         │
│                                ``voyage/voyage-3``, etc.) is routed through LiteLLM — set the    │
│                                matching provider env var (COHERE_API_KEY, VOYAGE_API_KEY, …).    │
│                                [default: text-embedding-3-small]                                 │
│ --api-key-env         TEXT     Env var holding the API key for embedding calls. Defaults to      │
│                                ``OPENAI_API_KEY``. Override when using a non-OpenAI provider     │
│                                (e.g. ``COHERE_API_KEY``).                                        │
│                                [default: OPENAI_API_KEY]                                         │
│ --dry-run                      Chunk + report what WOULD be ingested without calling the         │
│                                embedding API or writing to storage. Use to validate chunk sizes  │
│                                + counts before paying for embeddings.                            │
│ --clean-source                 Delete all existing chunks for each source file before            │
│                                re-ingesting. Use when updating a document — ensures stale        │
│                                paragraphs don't persist alongside the new content. Without this  │
│                                flag, dedup on content_hash means deleted paragraphs remain in    │
│                                the KB.                                                           │
│ --changed-only                 Skip files whose content hasn't changed since last ingest.        │
│                                Compares file mtime against the most recent chunk's created_at    │
│                                for that source path. Useful in CI to avoid re-embedding          │
│                                unchanged docs.                                                   │
│ --skip-graph                   Skip the knowledge-graph extraction step. By default every ingest │
│                                now builds the graph (entities + relations) for GraphRAG          │
│                                retrieval. Pass --skip-graph to opt out (e.g. when running        │
│                                without an ANTHROPIC_API_KEY or when you only need vector         │
│                                search).                                                          │
│ --ocr-lang            TEXT     Tesseract language code(s) for scanned PDFs / images. Accepts     │
│                                Tesseract 3-letter codes; use '+' for multi-language (e.g.        │
│                                'eng+fra'). Defaults to 'eng'. Sets MOVATE_OCR_LANG for this      │
│                                invocation only.                                                  │
│ --ocr-backend         TEXT     OCR engine: 'tesseract' (default, needs pytesseract + Tesseract   │
│                                binary) or 'easyocr' (pure-Python, better on noisy scans, larger  │
│                                install). Sets MOVATE_OCR_BACKEND for this invocation only.       │
│ --target              TEXT     Upload to a DEPLOYED runtime's KB endpoint instead of ingesting   │
│                                locally. Resolves URL + bearer from ~/.movate/config.yaml; the    │
│                                runtime parses + embeds server-side into ITS storage (e.g. Azure  │
│                                Postgres). The agent must already exist on the target. Local-only │
│                                flags (--model, --api-key-env, --tenant-id, --clean-source,       │
│                                --changed-only, --ocr-*) don't apply — the runtime owns those.    │
│ --crawl                        Only meaningful when the source is a URL: follow same-site <a     │
│                                href> links from the start page and ingest a BOUNDED set of pages │
│                                (each chunk's source = its own page URL). Stays on the start      │
│                                URL's host, skips non-HTML/mailto/external links, dedups visited  │
│                                URLs, and isolates per-page failures (a 404/timeout is skipped,   │
│                                not fatal). Bound it with --max-pages / --max-depth. Passing      │
│                                --crawl with a filesystem path is an error.                       │
│ --max-pages           INTEGER  Hard cap on the number of pages a --crawl ingests (default 25).   │
│                                Keeps the crawl bounded.                                          │
│                                [default: 25]                                                     │
│ --max-depth           INTEGER  Hard cap on --crawl link-follow depth: the start page is depth 0, │
│                                its links depth 1, etc. (default 2).                              │
│                                [default: 2]                                                      │
│ --help                         Show this message and exit.                                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk kb ingest-all`

```

 Usage: mdk kb ingest-all [OPTIONS]

 Scan the project and ingest every KB directory found.

 Looks in two places:


 1. ``<project>/kb/``              → scoped to ``--shared-agent`` (default: __shared__)
 2. ``<project>/agents/<name>/kb/`` → scoped to agent ``<name>``

 Each directory is walked recursively; files with extensions
 ``.md``, ``.markdown``, ``.txt``, ``.pdf``, ``.docx``, ``.html``,
 ``.png``, ``.jpg``, ``.jpeg``, ``.tiff`` are ingested. Hidden
 directories (``.git``, ``.venv``) are skipped.

 Examples:

   # Ingest every KB dir in the current project
   $ mdk kb ingest-all

   # Preview what would be ingested (no API calls)
   $ mdk kb ingest-all --dry-run

   # Re-ingest after updating documents
   $ mdk kb ingest-all --clean-source

   # Scope the project-level kb/ to a specific agent
   $ mdk kb ingest-all --shared-agent rag-qa

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --project       -p      PATH  Project root to scan. Defaults to the current directory. Looks for │
│                               ``kb/`` at the project root and ``agents/<name>/kb/`` for each     │
│                               agent.                                                             │
│                               [default: .]                                                       │
│ --shared-agent          TEXT  Agent name to use for files ingested from the project-level        │
│                               ``kb/`` directory. Defaults to __shared__. Override when you want  │
│                               the shared KB scoped to a specific agent at search time.           │
│                               [default: __shared__]                                              │
│ --model                 TEXT  Embedding model for all ingested files. Bare names go directly to  │
│                               OpenAI; any ``provider/model`` string is routed through LiteLLM.   │
│                               [default: text-embedding-3-small]                                  │
│ --api-key-env           TEXT  Env var holding the API key for embedding calls.                   │
│                               [default: OPENAI_API_KEY]                                          │
│ --tenant-id             TEXT  Tenant scope. Defaults to 'local'. [default: local]                │
│ --clean-source                Delete existing chunks for each source file before re-ingesting.   │
│                               Use when updating documents to remove stale paragraphs.            │
│ --changed-only                Skip files whose content hasn't changed since last ingest.         │
│                               Compares file mtime against the most recent chunk's created_at for │
│                               that source path. Useful in CI to avoid re-embedding unchanged     │
│                               docs.                                                              │
│ --watch                       Watch KB directories for file changes and re-ingest automatically. │
│                               Polls every 2 seconds. Ctrl-C to stop.                             │
│ --dry-run                     Preview what WOULD be ingested without calling the embedding API   │
│                               or writing to storage. Prints a table of discovered directories    │
│                               and file counts.                                                   │
│ --ocr-lang              TEXT  Tesseract language code(s) for scanned PDFs / images (e.g.         │
│                               'eng+fra').                                                        │
│ --ocr-backend           TEXT  OCR engine: 'tesseract' (default) or 'easyocr'.                    │
│ --help                        Show this message and exit.                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk kb list`

```

 Usage: mdk kb list [OPTIONS] [AGENT]

 List chunks in ``agent``'s KB. Useful for debugging "is my content actually in there?" without
 dropping into SQL.

 Omit ``agent`` for an interactive picker. Pass ``--target`` to list a
 deployed agent's KB instead of the local store.

 Examples:

   # Confirm a doc's chunks landed
   $ mdk kb list faq-agent

   # Filter to one source file on a deployed agent
   $ mdk kb list faq-agent --source handbook.md --target prod

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   agent      [AGENT]  Agent whose KB to inspect. Omit for picker.                                │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --source           TEXT                        Filter to chunks from a specific source path      │
│                                                (file URI).                                       │
│ --limit            INTEGER RANGE [1<=x<=1000]  Max rows to render. Defaults to 50; bump for full │
│                                                dumps.                                            │
│                                                [default: 50]                                     │
│ --tenant-id        TEXT                        Tenant scope (matches the value used at ingest).  │
│                                                [default: local]                                  │
│ --target           TEXT                        Inspect a DEPLOYED runtime's KB instead of the    │
│                                                local store. Resolves URL + bearer from           │
│                                                ~/.movate/config.yaml and calls GET               │
│                                                /api/v1/agents/<agent>/kb. The runtime scopes by  │
│                                                its own auth tenant, so --tenant-id is ignored on │
│                                                the remote path.                                  │
│ --help                                         Show this message and exit.                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk kb reindex`

```

 Usage: mdk kb reindex [OPTIONS] [AGENT]

 Rebuild ``agent``'s KB vector index.

 Default (no flag): rebuild the index from the EXISTING stored vectors
 — no embedding calls, no API key. Use after changing index params or
 when the index is degraded.

 ``--reembed``: re-run the embedding model over every stored chunk's
 text, overwrite each vector, THEN rebuild the index. Expensive (costs
 money) and needs an embedding key. Required when the embedding
 model / dimension changes. Confirmation required unless ``--yes``.

 Omit ``agent`` for an interactive picker. Pass ``--target`` to
 reindex a deployed agent's KB instead of the local store.

 Examples:

   # Rebuild the index from existing vectors (free)
   $ mdk kb reindex faq-agent

   # Re-embed everything after an embedding-model change
   $ mdk kb reindex faq-agent --reembed --yes

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   agent      [AGENT]  Agent whose KB index to rebuild. Omit for picker.                          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --reembed                    Re-run the embedding model over EVERY stored chunk's text,          │
│                              overwrite each vector, then rebuild the index. Expensive — needs an │
│                              embedding API key. Required when the embedding model / dimension    │
│                              changes. Without this flag, reindex rebuilds the index from the     │
│                              EXISTING stored vectors (no LLM calls, no key).                     │
│ --model                TEXT  Embedding model for the --reembed path (ignored without --reembed). │
│                              Must match the dimension of the deployment's vector column.         │
│                              [default: text-embedding-3-small]                                   │
│ --api-key-env          TEXT  Env var holding the embedding API key for --reembed. Defaults to    │
│                              OPENAI_API_KEY.                                                     │
│                              [default: OPENAI_API_KEY]                                           │
│ --tenant-id            TEXT  Tenant scope (matches the value used at ingest). [default: local]   │
│ --yes          -y            Skip the --reembed confirmation prompt (CI / scripting).            │
│ --target               TEXT  Reindex a DEPLOYED runtime's KB instead of the local store.         │
│                              Resolves URL + bearer from ~/.movate/config.yaml and calls POST     │
│                              /api/v1/agents/<agent>/kb/reindex. The runtime owns the             │
│                              re-embedding (with ITS key) + index rebuild, so local --model /     │
│                              --api-key-env / --tenant-id don't apply on the remote path.         │
│ --help                       Show this message and exit.                                         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk kb search`

```

 Usage: mdk kb search [OPTIONS] [AGENT] [QUESTION]

 Semantic search over ``agent``'s KB. Prints top-K with scores.

 Both arguments are optional — omit them to get an interactive picker
 that auto-detects agents and prompts for the search question.

 Use this to validate that retrieval is finding the right chunks
 BEFORE running the agent end-to-end — saves the cost of agent
 iterations on a bad KB.

 Default mode is vector-only (cosine similarity over OpenAI
 embeddings). ``--hybrid`` adds a parallel BM25 lexical search
 + reciprocal rank fusion; recommended for queries containing
 product names, error codes, or other rare terms. ``--rewrite N``
 fans out across N+1 LLM-generated paraphrases — best on vague
 or under-specified questions.

 Pass ``--target`` to search a deployed agent's KB instead of the
 local store — the runtime embeds the query server-side, so no local
 embedding key is needed.

 Examples:

   # Sanity-check retrieval before running the agent
   $ mdk kb search faq-agent "what is the refund window?"

   # Hybrid (vector + BM25) for rare-term queries, top 10
   $ mdk kb search faq-agent "error E1042" --hybrid -k 10

   # Search a deployed agent's KB
   $ mdk kb search faq-agent "refund window?" --target prod

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   agent         [AGENT]     Agent whose KB to search. Omit for interactive picker.               │
│   question      [QUESTION]  Free-text question to retrieve against. Omit to be prompted.         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --k            -k      INTEGER RANGE [1<=x<=50]  Number of top results to return. [default: 5]   │
│ --tenant-id            TEXT                      Tenant scope (matches the value used at         │
│                                                  ingest).                                        │
│                                                  [default: local]                                │
│ --model                TEXT                      Embedding model used to embed the query. MUST   │
│                                                  match the model used at ingest time — different │
│                                                  models produce incomparable vector spaces. Bare │
│                                                  names (``text-embedding-3-small``) and          │
│                                                  ``openai/`` prefixed strings go directly to     │
│                                                  OpenAI; any other ``provider/model`` string is  │
│                                                  routed through LiteLLM.                         │
│                                                  [default: text-embedding-3-small]               │
│ --api-key-env          TEXT                      Env var holding the API key for query           │
│                                                  embedding. Defaults to ``OPENAI_API_KEY``;      │
│                                                  override for non-OpenAI providers.              │
│                                                  [default: OPENAI_API_KEY]                       │
│ --full                                           Print full chunk text (default truncates to 200 │
│                                                  chars).                                         │
│ --hybrid                                         Combine vector + BM25 lexical search via        │
│                                                  reciprocal rank fusion. Typically 15-25% better │
│                                                  recall on real corpora — vector catches         │
│                                                  paraphrase, BM25 catches rare-term hits. No     │
│                                                  extra API cost (BM25 runs locally).             │
│ --rewrite              INTEGER RANGE [0<=x<=8]   Expand the query into N alternative paraphrases │
│                                                  via a small LLM, run retrieval for each, fuse   │
│                                                  the rankings with RRF. Catches vague queries    │
│                                                  that miss specific KB terminology (e.g.         │
│                                                  'refunds?' → KB chunks talking about 'return    │
│                                                  policy'). Adds ~200ms latency + ~$0.0001/query. │
│                                                  Stacks with --hybrid. 0 = disabled (default).   │
│                                                  [default: 0]                                    │
│ --rerank                                         Add a rerank stage that re-scores upstream      │
│                                                  candidates by relevance to the question,        │
│                                                  correcting 'noisy top-K' where vector/BM25      │
│                                                  scores rank irrelevant chunks high. Fetches 3x  │
│                                                  candidates upstream then trims to top-K. Use    │
│                                                  --rerank-mode to choose between LLM (default)   │
│                                                  and local cross-encoder backends. Stacks with   │
│                                                  --hybrid and --rewrite.                         │
│ --rerank-mode          TEXT                      Which rerank backend to use when --rerank is    │
│                                                  set. 'llm' (default) — one batched LLM call via │
│                                                  LiteLLM (~200ms, ~$0.0002/query, zero extra     │
│                                                  deps). 'cross_encoder' — local                  │
│                                                  sentence-transformers cross-encoder (~50ms CPU, │
│                                                  zero API cost, requires 'pip install            │
│                                                  movate-cli' ~300MB).                            │
│                                                  [default: llm]                                  │
│ --multi-hop            INTEGER RANGE [0<=x<=5]   Iterative retrieve → reason → retrieve loop.    │
│                                                  Each hop runs the full retrieval pipeline       │
│                                                  (--hybrid / --rewrite / --rerank apply          │
│                                                  per-hop), then a planner LLM decides 'done' or  │
│                                                  generates a refined sub-query. Best on          │
│                                                  multi-fact questions ('how does X interact with │
│                                                  Y?'). Adds N planner calls + N retrieval        │
│                                                  passes. 0 = disabled (default).                 │
│                                                  [default: 0]                                    │
│ --trace                                          Render a per-stage trace table after the        │
│                                                  results: which stages fired, how long each      │
│                                                  took, candidate counts in/out. Useful for       │
│                                                  debugging 'why didn't this chunk surface?' or   │
│                                                  'where's my latency going?'. Adds ~0.1ms of     │
│                                                  overhead per stage (negligible).                │
│ --target               TEXT                      Search a DEPLOYED runtime's KB instead of the   │
│                                                  local store. Resolves URL + bearer from         │
│                                                  ~/.movate/config.yaml and calls POST            │
│                                                  /api/v1/agents/<agent>/kb/search; the runtime   │
│                                                  embeds the question server-side with ITS        │
│                                                  configured model. Only --k and --hybrid apply   │
│                                                  remotely — the runtime owns --model /           │
│                                                  --api-key-env / --tenant-id and the advanced    │
│                                                  rewrite/rerank/multi-hop/trace stages.          │
│ --help                                           Show this message and exit.                     │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk kb stats`

```

 Usage: mdk kb stats [OPTIONS] [AGENT]

 Summary stats for ``agent``'s KB: chunk count, source breakdown, embedding model(s) in use, total
 + per-source character counts. Useful for sanity-checking after a big ingest.

 Use ``--by-source`` to flip the per-source table into a
 distribution view (sorted by chunk count DESC with a %-of-total
 column) — quick triage for 'is one document dominating?'.

 Omit ``agent`` for an interactive picker. Pass ``--target`` to
 summarize a deployed agent's KB instead of the local store.

 Examples:

   # Sanity-check a corpus after ingest
   $ mdk kb stats faq-agent

   # Is one document dominating the KB?
   $ mdk kb stats faq-agent --by-source

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   agent      [AGENT]  Agent whose KB to summarize. Omit for picker.                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --tenant-id        TEXT                  Tenant scope (matches ingest value). [default: local]   │
│ --by-source                              Distribution-view: sort per-source rows by chunk count  │
│                                          DESCENDING + add a percentage column. Useful for        │
│                                          triaging KB quality — 'which doc dominates retrieval?'  │
│                                          and 'is any one source contributing most of the         │
│                                          chunks?'. Default sort (without this flag) is           │
│                                          alphabetical by source path.                            │
│ --top              INTEGER RANGE [x>=0]  Cap the per-source table at the top N rows (most chunks │
│                                          first when combined with --by-source). 0 = show all.    │
│                                          Useful when an agent's KB has hundreds of source files. │
│                                          [default: 0]                                            │
│ --target           TEXT                  Summarize a DEPLOYED runtime's KB instead of the local  │
│                                          store. Resolves URL + bearer from ~/.movate/config.yaml │
│                                          and calls GET /api/v1/agents/<agent>/kb/stats           │
│                                          (aggregated server-side). The runtime scopes by its own │
│                                          auth tenant, so --tenant-id is ignored on the remote    │
│                                          path.                                                   │
│ --help                                   Show this message and exit.                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk keys`

```

 Usage: mdk keys [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Manage this tenant's own provider API keys, encrypted at rest (BYOK, ADR 018).

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ set      Store (or rotate) this tenant's key for provider.                                       │
│ list     List configured providers + masked fingerprints (never the values).                     │
│ delete   Remove this tenant's key for a provider (falls back to the shared key).                 │
│ test     Make a cheap provider call with the stored key to validate it.                          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk keys set`

```

 Usage: mdk keys set [OPTIONS] PROVIDER

 Store (or rotate) this tenant's key for provider.

 The key is encrypted at rest with ``MOVATE_PROVIDER_KEY_SECRET`` (Fernet);
 only a masked fingerprint is printed back — the value is never
 stored in plaintext or echoed.

 Examples:

   # Prompt for the key, hidden
   $ mdk keys set openai

   # Rotate the Anthropic key (overwrites in place)
   $ mdk keys set anthropic

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    provider      TEXT  Provider namespace, e.g. openai | anthropic (the part before '/' in     │
│                          model.provider).                                                        │
│                          [required]                                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --api-key        TEXT  The provider key. Omit to be prompted HIDDEN (recommended — keeps it off  │
│                        your shell history).                                                      │
│ --help                 Show this message and exit.                                               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk keys test`

```

 Usage: mdk keys test [OPTIONS] PROVIDER

 Make a cheap provider call with the stored key to validate it.

 Decrypts the stored key and runs a 1-token completion through LiteLLM so
 you can confirm the key works before relying on it. The key is used only
 in-memory for this call — never printed.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    provider      TEXT  Provider namespace to validate (e.g. openai). [required]                │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --model        TEXT  Model to probe (default: a cheap per-provider default).                     │
│ --help               Show this message and exit.                                                 │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk knowledge`

```

 Inspect and validate knowledge-base assets. validate reports which eval queries return zero corpus
 matches.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ validate   Check which eval queries return zero KB corpus matches.                               │
│ add        Append one entry to the KB corpus interactively or via --json.                        │
│ remove     Remove one entry from the KB corpus by id.                                            │
│ edit       Patch one entry in the KB corpus by id.                                               │
│ list       List KB corpus entries as a table.                                                    │
│ query      Query the KB corpus and show ranked results.                                          │

### `mdk knowledge add`

```

 Usage: mdk knowledge add [OPTIONS]

 Append one entry to the KB corpus interactively or via --json.

 In a TTY, prompts for each required field. In CI/non-TTY, pass
 --json '{"id":"...","title":"...","resolution":"..."}' .

 Required fields: id, title, resolution.
 Optional: symptom, tags.

 Examples:

   $ mdk knowledge add
   $ mdk knowledge add --json '{"id":"KB-042","title":"T","resolution":"R"}'

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --json    -j      TEXT  JSON object with entry fields (id, title, symptom, resolution, tags).    │
│                         Omit to be prompted interactively.                                       │
│ --corpus  -c      TEXT  Path to corpus JSON. Defaults to kb/kb-lookup-corpus.json in the project │
│                         root.                                                                    │
│ --help                  Show this message and exit.                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk knowledge edit`

```

 Usage: mdk knowledge edit [OPTIONS] ENTRY_ID

 Patch one entry in the KB corpus by id.

 Only the fields listed in --set are updated; all
 other fields are preserved. Pass --set '{"id": "new-id"}'
 to rename an entry.

 Examples:

   $ mdk knowledge edit KB-042 --set '{"resolution": "Updated answer"}'
   $ mdk knowledge edit KB-042 --set '{"tags": ["billing", "refunds"]}'

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    entry_id      TEXT  The id of the entry to edit. [required]                                 │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --set     -s      TEXT  JSON object of fields to update, e.g. --set '{"resolution": "New      │
│                            answer"}' . Only listed keys are changed; others are preserved.       │
│                            [required]                                                            │
│    --corpus  -c      TEXT  Path to corpus JSON. Defaults to kb/kb-lookup-corpus.json.            │
│    --help                  Show this message and exit.                                           │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk knowledge query`

```

 Usage: mdk knowledge query [OPTIONS] QUERY

 Query the KB corpus and show ranked results.

 Wraps the same in-memory retrievers (:mod:`movate.knowledge`) the
 v0.8 production engine will plug into — so what you see here is
 what an agent's `retriever` workflow node would see at runtime,
 minus embeddings/reranking (those land in v0.8).

 Examples:

   # Default BM25 against the canonical kb-lookup corpus:
   $ mdk knowledge query "login fails after restart"

   # Substring retriever for a tiny corpus + structured output:
   $ mdk knowledge query "refund window" -r substring --json

   # FAQ-shaped corpus with custom body fields:
   $ mdk knowledge query "shipping" \
       --body-field question --body-field answer \
       --corpus kb/faq.json

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    query      TEXT  Free-text search query. The retriever tokenizes + scores against the       │
│                       corpus.                                                                    │
│                       [required]                                                                 │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --corpus      -c      TEXT     Path to corpus JSON. Defaults to kb/kb-lookup-corpus.json.        │
│ --top-k       -k      INTEGER  How many results to return (1-50). [default: 5]                   │
│ --retriever   -r      TEXT     Retriever kind. bm25 (default) — Robertson/Sparck-Jones with IDF  │
│                                + length normalization, good for corpora over ~50 entries.        │
│                                substring — token-overlap baseline, cheaper + more deterministic  │
│                                for tiny corpora.                                                 │
│                                [default: bm25]                                                   │
│ --body-field          TEXT     Corpus entry field(s) to index for body matching. Repeatable.     │
│                                Default matches the canonical kb-lookup corpus shape (title +     │
│                                symptom + resolution). Override with --body-field for FAQ corpora │
│                                (--body-field question --body-field answer).                      │
│                                [default: title, symptom, resolution]                             │
│ --json                         Emit results as a JSON array of {doc_id, score, entry} on stdout. │
│                                Used by scripts + the v0.8 workflow retriever node. Default is    │
│                                the operator-friendly Rich table.                                 │
│ --help                         Show this message and exit.                                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk knowledge remove`

```

 Usage: mdk knowledge remove [OPTIONS] ENTRY_ID

 Remove one entry from the KB corpus by id.

 Examples:

 $ mdk knowledge remove KB-042 --yes

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    entry_id      TEXT  The id of the entry to remove. [required]                               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --corpus  -c      TEXT  Path to corpus JSON. Defaults to kb/kb-lookup-corpus.json.               │
│ --yes     -y            Skip confirmation prompt.                                                │
│ --help                  Show this message and exit.                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk knowledge validate`

```

 Usage: mdk knowledge validate [OPTIONS] AGENT

 Check which eval queries return zero KB corpus matches.

 Loads the corpus and each agent's evals/dataset.jsonl,
 then runs the same keyword scoring as the kb-lookup skill. Queries that
 produce no hits indicate corpus gaps — entries you need to add before
 eval accuracy will improve.

 Examples:

   $ mdk knowledge validate
   $ mdk knowledge validate rag-qa
   $ mdk knowledge validate rag-qa --corpus kb/my-corpus.json
   $ mdk knowledge validate --show-passing

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   agent      TEXT  Agent name or path. Omit to validate all agents in agents/ that have an eval  │
│                    dataset.                                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --corpus        -c      TEXT  Path to corpus JSON, or a filename relative to kb/. Defaults to    │
│                               kb/kb-lookup-corpus.json in the project root.                      │
│ --show-passing                Also show queries that DID get at least one corpus match.          │
│ --help                        Show this message and exit.                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk logs`

```

 Usage: mdk logs [OPTIONS] [RUN_ID]

 Inspect a run record: input, output, cost, latency, errors.

 Examples::

 mdk logs abc123               # show run abc123
 mdk logs --last               # show the most-recent run
 mdk logs --last --agent faq   # most-recent faq run
 mdk logs abc123 --tail        # poll until terminal (default 300s)
 mdk logs abc123 --tail -t 60  # poll with 60s timeout
 mdk logs abc123 --raw         # raw JSON record

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   run_id      [RUN_ID]  Run ID to inspect.  Omit with --last to show the most-recent run.        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --agent    -a      TEXT                  Filter --last by agent name.                            │
│ --last                                   Show the most-recent run (ignores RUN_ID if both        │
│                                          given).                                                 │
│ --tail     -f                            Poll until the run reaches a terminal status.           │
│ --raw                                    Print the raw RunRecord JSON and exit.                  │
│ --timeout  -t      INTEGER RANGE [x>=1]  Seconds to wait before giving up when --tail is active  │
│                                          (default: 300s).                                        │
│                                          [default: 300]                                          │
│ --help                                   Show this message and exit.                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk mcp`

```

 Usage: mdk mcp [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Run the authoring MCP server: expose the typed action catalog (ADR 025) as MCP tools
 (plan_*/apply_*/validate/run) so an IDE/agent drives the same plan→apply→verify spine as `mdk
 authoring`. Local control-plane tool; composes catalog actions only.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ serve   Serve the authoring catalog over MCP (newline-delimited JSON-RPC on stdio).              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk mcp serve`

```

 Usage: mdk mcp serve [OPTIONS]

 Serve the authoring catalog over MCP (newline-delimited JSON-RPC on stdio).

 Runs until the client closes stdin. The catalog is exposed as a
 ``plan_<action>`` + ``apply_<action>`` tool per action, plus ``validate`` and
 ``run``; schemas come from the catalog. ``--list-tools`` prints the manifest
 and exits — useful for wiring up an MCP host config or a quick check.

 Examples:

   # Inspect the tool manifest (no server)
   $ mdk mcp serve --list-tools

   # Run the stdio MCP server for an IDE/agent host
   $ mdk mcp serve --project .

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --project     -p      PATH  Project root the catalog operates against.                           │
│ --list-tools                Print the generated MCP tool manifest as JSON and exit (no server).  │
│ --help                      Show this message and exit.                                          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk menu`

```

 Usage: mdk menu [OPTIONS]

 Show workspace status and a contextual list of next steps.

 Examples:

   $ mdk menu                # interactive
   $ mdk menu --dry-run      # show status + suggestions, no prompt

 Each menu entry maps to a real mdk subcommand —
 pick one and the menu shells out to it, preserving stdio so
 the output matches running directly. Add --help
 after any subcommand name shown in the menu to learn more.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --dry-run          List status + suggestions without prompting. Useful in scripts (e.g. CI       │
│                    status reports) and for tests.                                                │
│ --help             Show this message and exit.                                                   │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk migrate`

```

 Usage: mdk migrate [OPTIONS] SNAP

 Restore files from a snapshot into the current workspace.

 Defaults to a safe --dry-run preview — add
 --apply to actually write files. Use
 --filter 'agents/**' to scope the restore to specific
 files, or omit --filter to restore everything in the
 snapshot.

 Examples:

   $ mdk migrate abc1234                              # preview
   $ mdk migrate abc1234 --apply                      # restore all
   $ mdk migrate abc1234 --filter 'agents/**' --apply # agents only
   $ mdk migrate abc1234 --backup --apply --yes       # CI-safe

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    snap      TEXT  Snapshot hash or prefix to migrate from. Run mdk snapshot list to browse    │
│                      available snapshots.                                                        │
│                      [required]                                                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --filter   -f                 GLOB  Shell glob applied to each file's relative path. Examples:   │
│                                     --filter 'agents/**' or --filter 'agents/triage/**'. Omit to │
│                                     migrate every file in the snapshot.                          │
│ --dry-run      --apply              --dry-run (default): preview changes without writing.        │
│                                     --apply: actually restore files to the workspace.            │
│                                     [default: dry-run]                                           │
│ --backup       --no-backup          Auto-snapshot the current workspace before applying changes. │
│                                     Only meaningful when used with --apply; ignored in dry-run   │
│                                     mode.                                                        │
│                                     [default: no-backup]                                         │
│ --yes      -y                       Skip the confirmation prompt (non-interactive / CI).         │
│ --help                              Show this message and exit.                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk migrate-state`

```

 Usage: mdk migrate-state [OPTIONS] [PATH]

 Rename this project's legacy ``.movate/`` runtime-state dir to ``.mdk/`` (ADR 011).

 Moves the directory (via ``git mv`` when inside a repo, so history + tracked
 eval baselines are preserved) and rewrites the project's ``.gitignore`` so
 ``.mdk/`` is ignored with the same committed-baseline exception. No-op when
 there's no legacy ``.movate/``; refuses to clobber a non-empty ``.mdk/``.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   path      [PATH]  Project root to migrate (default: current directory). [default: .]           │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --dry-run          Show what would change; write nothing.                                        │
│ --help             Show this message and exit.                                                   │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

│ --has-vision                        Only show models that accept image inputs.                   │

│                                     [default: table]                                             │

### `mdk monitor`

```

 Usage: mdk monitor [OPTIONS]

 Live dashboard of recent runs.

 Polls storage on an interval, re-renders a Rich table in place.
 Ctrl+C to quit. Use --once for a single
 snapshot if you don't have a TTY.

 Pairs with mdk costs report (historical view) the
 way htop pairs with ps.

 Examples:

   $ mdk monitor                       # live, 3s refresh
   $ mdk monitor --agent triage        # one agent
   $ mdk monitor --status error        # only failures
   $ mdk monitor --interval 1          # tighter refresh
   $ mdk monitor --once                # one snapshot, exit

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --agent      -a      TEXT     Filter to one agent (e.g. --agent triage).                         │
│ --tenant-id          TEXT     Filter to one tenant (omit for cross-tenant in single-tenant       │
│                               deploys).                                                          │
│ --status             TEXT     Filter to one status. Common: success / error / queued. Empty =    │
│                               show all.                                                          │
│ --limit              INTEGER  How many recent runs to show. Default 20. [default: 20]            │
│ --interval   -i      FLOAT    Refresh interval in seconds (default 3.0). Minimum 0.5 to avoid    │
│                               hammering storage.                                                 │
│                               [default: 3.0]                                                     │
│ --once                        Render one snapshot and exit. Useful for cron / CI smoke (the live │
│                               loop expects a TTY).                                               │
│ --clear                       Use alternate-screen mode so the live table doesn't accumulate     │
│                               scrollback. Restores the terminal on exit. Recommended for         │
│                               long-running sessions.                                             │
│ --help                        Show this message and exit.                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk playground`

```

 Usage: mdk playground [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 ChatGPT-like browser UI for testing deployed agents. Powered by Chainlit. Multi-turn chat, a
 past-conversations sidebar, file uploads, live streaming, and 👍/👎/comment feedback persisted to
 the runtime's Postgres + Langfuse for analysis + agent tuning.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ serve   Launch the ChatGPT-like Chainlit playground for testing agents.                          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk playground serve`

```

 Usage: mdk playground serve [OPTIONS]

 Launch the ChatGPT-like Chainlit playground for testing agents.

 The browser UI lists agents from the configured runtime; pick one and
 chat with it multi-turn. Attach files (text extracted into context,
 optionally persisted to the agent's KB), resume past conversations
 from the sidebar, watch tokens stream live (when the runtime supports
 it), and capture 👍/👎/comment feedback that the runtime persists to
 Postgres (and pushes to Langfuse if configured).

 Capability-aware: the playground asks the runtime what it supports
 and auto-upgrades to server-managed sessions / streaming / the
 feedback API when available, falling back to client-managed history +
 buffered responses otherwise.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --runtime-url            TEXT     Base URL of the runtime to test against. Defaults to the local │
│                                   ``mdk serve`` default. For a deployed runtime, pass the ACA    │
│                                   URL (e.g. https://...azurecontainerapps.io). Passing this (or  │
│                                   its env var) pins a SINGLE runtime and disables the            │
│                                   multi-target chat-profile picker.                              │
│                                   [env var: MDK_PLAYGROUND_RUNTIME_URL, MOVATE_RUNTIME_URL]      │
│                                   [default: http://127.0.0.1:8000]                               │
│ --api-key                TEXT     Bearer token for the runtime. Required when the runtime        │
│                                   enforces auth (production); optional for local dev. Read from  │
│                                   ``MDK_PLAYGROUND_API_KEY`` or ``MOVATE_API_KEY`` env vars by   │
│                                   default — never paste keys on the command line.                │
│                                   [env var: MDK_PLAYGROUND_API_KEY, MOVATE_API_KEY]              │
│ --port                   INTEGER  Bind port for the Chainlit UI. Defaults to 8765 — leaves       │
│                                   Chainlit's docs default (8000) free for the runtime if they    │
│                                   run side-by-side.                                              │
│                                   [default: 8765]                                                │
│ --host                   TEXT     Bind host. ``127.0.0.1`` (default) restricts to localhost; use │
│                                   ``0.0.0.0`` for container deployments behind a trusted reverse │
│                                   proxy.                                                         │
│                                   [default: 127.0.0.1]                                           │
│ --headless                        Don't auto-open the browser. Default behavior opens            │
│                                   ``http://<host>:<port>`` on serve; ``--headless`` is useful    │
│                                   for CI / container deploys / SSH tunnels.                      │
│ --no-history                      Disable thread persistence (the past-conversations sidebar /   │
│                                   resume). The playground runs ephemeral — each refresh starts a │
│                                   fresh chat. By default threads persist to a local SQLite file  │
│                                   at ``~/.mdk/playground/threads.db`` (or a Postgres URL from    │
│                                   ``MDK_PLAYGROUND_THREADS_URL`` / ``DATABASE_URL``).            │
│ --persist-uploads                 Auto-ingest uploaded files into the agent's KB (instead of     │
│                                   only holding their text as conversation context). Off by       │
│                                   default — uploads stay session-scoped and you opt in per file  │
│                                   via the 'Add to agent's KB permanently' button in the chat.    │
│                                   ``--persist-uploads`` flips the default to always-ingest.      │
│ --all-targets                     Force multi-target mode: surface ONE chat profile per target   │
│                                   registered in ``~/.movate/config.yaml`` (the same targets      │
│                                   ``mdk config list-targets`` shows). Pick a target, then its    │
│                                   agents. This is the AUTO default when targets are configured   │
│                                   and no ``--runtime-url`` is given; the flag makes it explicit  │
│                                   (and errors if no targets are registered).                     │
│ --no-targets                      Force single-runtime mode even when targets are configured —   │
│                                   talk only to ``--runtime-url`` (default: the local runtime).   │
│                                   Skips the chat-profile target picker.                          │
│ --voice                           Enable voice mode: talk to the agent with your mic. Captures   │
│                                   audio in the browser, streams it to the runtime's voice        │
│                                   WebSocket (``WS /api/v1/agents/{name}/voice``), renders the    │
│                                   live transcript + the agent's answer, and plays the            │
│                                   synthesized reply back. Off by default — the text playground   │
│                                   is unchanged. The target runtime must expose the voice route   │
│                                   (voice Phase 1); if it doesn't, the UI shows a friendly 'voice │
│                                   not enabled' message and text still works.                     │
│ --help                            Show this message and exit.                                    │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk policy`

```

 Usage: mdk policy [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Export / import / diff project policy.yaml — promote a vetted policy from dev → staging → prod
 without copy-paste.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ export   Emit the active policy.yaml as deterministic YAML or JSON.                              │
│ import   Read a policy doc and write it to policy.yaml.                                          │
│ diff     Show what would change if you imported ``source``.                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk policy diff`

```

 Usage: mdk policy diff [OPTIONS] SOURCE

 Show what would change if you imported ``source``.

 Reads the active policy.yaml from cwd, reads ``source``, and prints
 a side-by-side line diff of their normalized YAML representations.
 Read-only — nothing on disk changes. Run this in a promotion
 pipeline as a safety check before ``mdk policy import``.

 Exits 0 if the documents match (including when both are absent /
 empty), 1 if they differ. Useful in CI: ``mdk policy diff
 release/policy.yaml`` fails the build when prod has drifted from
 what's checked in.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    source      PATH  Candidate policy file to compare against the active policy.yaml.          │
│                        [required]                                                                │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk policy export`

```

 Usage: mdk policy export [OPTIONS]

 Emit the active policy.yaml as deterministic YAML or JSON.

 Reads ``policy.yaml`` from cwd (or ``movate.yaml`` for the legacy
 name), normalizes it (sorted keys, defaults stripped), and writes
 to stdout — or to ``--output <path>`` for piping into a vault /
 git-commit / cross-env promotion script.

 Examples:

   # Print the active policy to stdout
   $ mdk policy export

   # Promote dev's policy to staging by exporting it to JSON
   $ mdk policy export -o /tmp/dev-policy.json --format json

   # Drop into a release artifact
   $ mdk policy export -o release/policy.yaml

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --output  -o      PATH  Write the exported policy to this file instead of stdout. File extension │
│                         determines the format if --format isn't passed (``.json`` ⇒ json,        │
│                         anything else ⇒ yaml).                                                   │
│ --format  -f      TEXT  Output format: 'yaml' (default) or 'json'. Inferred from --output's      │
│                         extension when both are passed and --format isn't.                       │
│ --help                  Show this message and exit.                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk policy import`

```

 Usage: mdk policy import [OPTIONS] SOURCE

 Read a policy doc and write it to policy.yaml.

 Validates against :class:`ProjectConfig` before writing, so a
 malformed input never overwrites a working policy. Refuses to
 overwrite an existing target unless ``--force`` is passed.

 Examples:

   # Adopt a policy exported from another environment
   $ mdk policy import /tmp/dev-policy.json

   # Overwrite the current policy.yaml with a new one
   $ mdk policy import release/policy.yaml --force

   # Stage a policy at a non-standard path
   $ mdk policy import shared-policy.yaml -t infra/staging-policy.yaml

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    source      PATH  Policy file to import (JSON or YAML). [required]                          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target  -t      PATH  Path to write the imported policy. Defaults to policy.yaml in cwd. Use   │
│                         --target to write to a non-standard location (e.g. an alternate          │
│                         environment's checked-in policy file).                                   │
│                         [default: policy.yaml]                                                   │
│ --force                 Overwrite ``--target`` if it already exists (default refuses).           │
│ --help                  Show this message and exit.                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```
