### `mdk profiles`

```

 Usage: mdk profiles [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Manage named environment contexts (dev / staging / prod / customer). Each profile bundles a target
 + tenant_id + description. The active profile drives `mdk secrets`, `mdk env`, `mdk promote`
 (Sprint O).

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ current   Print the active profile name (or exit 1 if none set).                                 │
│ list      List every registered profile; mark the active one with *.                             │
│ show      Render one profile's details + active status.                                          │
│ use       Activate a profile.                                                                    │
│ create    Register a new profile (or update an existing one).                                    │
│ delete    Remove a profile from the registry.                                                    │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk profiles create`

```

 Usage: mdk profiles create [OPTIONS] NAME

 Register a new profile (or update an existing one).

 Idempotent: re-running with the same name overwrites the prior
 entry. Treating create + update as one verb keeps the surface
 small; operators get one mental model.

 Examples:

   # Minimal — local-only profile
   $ mdk profiles create local

   # Full — production profile pointing at a deployed runtime
   $ mdk profiles create prod \
       --target prod-runtime \
       --tenant acme-prod \
       --description "Production for acme.com" \
       --use

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      TEXT  Profile name (lowercase + hyphens, e.g. 'dev', 'us-east-prod'). [required]  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target       -t      TEXT  Reference to an mdk config target name. Empty for local-only        │
│                              profiles (no deploy target). Required for profiles used by mdk      │
│                              promote.                                                            │
│ --tenant               TEXT  Multi-tenant scoping id. Defaults to the profile name (common case: │
│                              `dev` profile = tenant_id `dev`). Override when names diverge.      │
│ --description  -d      TEXT  One-line human-readable note. Surfaces in `mdk profiles list`.      │
│ --use                        Activate the new profile immediately after creating it.             │
│ --help                       Show this message and exit.                                         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk profiles current`

```

 Usage: mdk profiles current [OPTIONS]

 Print the active profile name (or exit 1 if none set).

 Plain stdout — no Rich. Designed for shell substitution:

   $ MY_PROFILE=$(mdk profiles current)
   $ mdk secrets list --profile "$MY_PROFILE"

 Faster typing than mdk profiles show --active-only for
 the single most-asked profile question. Same vibe as
 git branch --show-current.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk profiles delete`

```

 Usage: mdk profiles delete [OPTIONS] NAME

 Remove a profile from the registry.

 If the deleted profile was active, the active marker is also
 cleared — no dangling "active profile X doesn't exist" state.
 Dry-run mode (no ``--force``) just confirms which profile would
 be deleted, useful for verifying name selection before commit.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      TEXT  Profile name to remove. [required]                                          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --force          Required to actually delete. The default behavior is a dry-run preview (exit 1) │
│                  — matches `mdk snapshot delete`'s safety gate. Profiles can carry meaningful    │
│                  operational state once secrets ship in Sprint O; deletion should be a           │
│                  deliberate operator action.                                                     │
│ --help           Show this message and exit.                                                     │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

```

### `mdk profiles use`

```

 Usage: mdk profiles use [OPTIONS] NAME

 Activate a profile.

 Writes the marker file at ``~/.movate/active-profile``. Downstream
 Sprint O commands (`mdk secrets`, `mdk env`, `mdk promote`) read
 this on each invocation.

 The active profile is process-independent — switching in one
 shell affects every shell. That's the kubectl convention and
 matches operator mental model ("I'm working in prod" is a global
 state, not a per-process one). Override per-command with
 profile-specific flags when needed.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      TEXT  Profile name to activate. [required]                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk project add-agent`

```

 Usage: mdk project add-agent [OPTIONS] PROJECT_ID

 Attach a new agent to a project.

 Pass exactly one of ``--bundle``, ``--from-llm``, or
 ``--from-catalog`` — they pick the source. Other modes
 (``--from-spec``, ``--from-wizard``) ship alongside the Mova iO
 wizard work; the runtime already accepts those bodies.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    project_id      TEXT  Project id to attach the agent to. [required]                         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --bundle               FILE  Path to a bundle .tar.gz / .zip — uploaded as source=bundle.        │
│ --from-llm             TEXT  Natural-language description — runs the LLM authoring pipeline.     │
│                              Live SSE progress streams to the terminal.                          │
│ --from-catalog         TEXT  Catalog slug, optionally suffixed with @<version> (e.g.             │
│                              `support-ticket-triage@2.1.0`).                                     │
│ --rename               TEXT  When cloning from catalog or generating via LLM, rename the agent.  │
│ --target               TEXT  Deploy target nickname (resolved via `mdk auth`). Currently a no-op │
│                              placeholder — env-var resolution is the only path.                  │
│ --auto-seed-kb               LLM: seed a starter KB context.                                     │
│ --include-evals              LLM: generate an eval set.                                          │
│ --include-judge              LLM: generate a judge agent.                                        │
│ --help                       Show this message and exit.                                         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk promote`

```

 Usage: mdk promote [OPTIONS] SNAP

 Record a snapshot's promotion to a profile.

 Examples:

 $ mdk promote abc1234 --to staging
 $ mdk promote abc1234 --to staging --dry-run
 $ mdk promote abc1234 --to prod -d "v0.7 release"
 $ mdk promote abc1234 --to prod --eval-pass-rate 0.85
 $ mdk promote --list
 $ mdk promote --list --profile prod
 $ mdk promote --current prod

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   snap      TEXT  Snapshot hash or prefix to promote. Omit when using --list or --current. Run   │
│                   mdk snapshot list to browse snapshots.                                         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --to              -t      PROFILE  Destination profile (e.g. staging, prod).                     │
│ --description     -d      TEXT     Operator note recorded with the promotion (e.g. release tag,  │
│                                    ticket).                                                      │
│ --eval-pass-rate          FLOAT    Observed eval pass rate (0.0-1.0) for the audit trail.        │
│                                    Operators run mdk eval separately and supply the score.       │
│ --list                             Show recorded promotions. Combine with --profile <name> to    │
│                                    filter.                                                       │
│ --current                 PROFILE  Show the most recent promotion to PROFILE (e.g. --current     │
│                                    prod).                                                        │
│ --profile         -p      PROFILE  Filter --list output to a single profile.                     │
│ --dry-run                          Show what would be recorded without writing the log.          │
│ --help                             Show this message and exit.                                   │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk replay`

```

 Usage: mdk replay [OPTIONS] RUN_ID

 Re-execute a past run with the same input.

 The recorded ``input`` dict goes verbatim to the executor; the
 agent on disk runs against it. If you've edited the prompt since
 the original run, that's the whole point — see how the new prompt
 handles the old input.

 With --target the replay runs on a deployed runtime
 (``POST /api/v1/runs/{id}/replay``, ADR 045 D13) against the published — or a
 pinned --against version:X — agent version, returning the
 original vs replayed side-by-side. Without it, replay is local (below).

 Examples:

   $ mdk replay r-abc-123                    # re-run locally, print new output
   $ mdk replay r-abc-123 --diff             # side-by-side with original
   $ mdk replay r-abc-123 --mock             # offline / hermetic
   $ mdk replay r-abc-123 --target prod      # replay on the deployed runtime
   $ mdk replay r-abc-123 --target prod --against version:0.2.0

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    run_id      TEXT  Run ID to replay (from mdk list or mdk logs). [required]                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --diff                   Render the original vs replayed output side-by-side. Without --diff,    │
│                          only the new output is shown.                                           │
│ --mock                   Use MockProvider — offline / hermetic / no API key needed. Useful for   │
│                          smoke-testing the replay wiring.                                        │
│ --tenant-id        TEXT  Tenant scope for storage lookup (default: 'local' for CLI use).         │
│                          [default: local]                                                        │
│ --json                   Emit the replayed RunRecord as JSON. Skips the Rich rendering.          │
│ --target           TEXT  Replay against a deployed runtime (named target or URL) via POST        │
│                          /api/v1/runs/{id}/replay (ADR 045 D13) instead of the local on-disk     │
│                          agent. Pair with --against to pick the version.                         │
│ --against          TEXT  Remote only (--target): the agent version to replay against — published │
│                          (latest) or version:X.                                                  │
│                          [default: published]                                                    │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk report`

```

 Usage: mdk report [OPTIONS] [AGENT]

 Offline rollup of agent health from the local store (ADR 031 D3).

 Aggregates the runs + eval summaries already persisted locally —
 pass-rate, cost, latency percentiles, top failing cases, per-agent /
 per-workflow — into an at-a-glance summary. No infra, no remote
 runtime: the offline answer to "how are my agents doing?".

 Examples:

   $ mdk report                       # everything, all-time
   $ mdk report triage                # one agent
   $ mdk report --agent triage --last 7   # one agent, last week
   $ mdk report --json | jq '.agents' # pipe to scripting / CI

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   agent      [AGENT]  Scope to one agent or workflow name (positional). Omit for all.            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --agent      -a      TEXT     Scope to one agent/workflow (same as the positional arg).          │
│ --last       -n      INTEGER  Only count runs / evals from the last N days. 0 (default) = no     │
│                               time window. Use 7 / 30 for weekly / monthly.                      │
│                               [default: 0]                                                       │
│ --tenant-id          TEXT     Filter to one tenant (omit for cross-tenant in single-tenant       │
│                               deploys).                                                          │
│ --top                INTEGER  How many failing cases to surface in the top-failures table.       │
│                               [default: 5]                                                       │
│ --json                        Emit a machine-readable rollup instead of a Rich summary — pipe to │
│                               jq / CI.                                                           │
│ --help                        Show this message and exit.                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk rollback`

```

 Usage: mdk rollback [OPTIONS] HASH_OR_PREFIX

 Restore the project to a prior snapshot.

 Defaults to dry-run. Run with ``--force`` to actually
 apply. Before applying, an automatic snapshot of the CURRENT state
 is captured — the rollback is itself a state-graph operation, not
 a destructive mutation. The pre-rollback snapshot's description
 encodes the rollback origin (``rolled back FROM <hash>``) for the
 audit trail.

 Examples:

   # Preview what rollback would restore
   $ mdk rollback abc12345

   # Actually roll back
   $ mdk rollback abc12345 --force

   # Roll forward — restore the auto-created pre-rollback snapshot
   $ mdk snapshot list   # find the pre-rollback hash
   $ mdk rollback <pre-rollback-hash> --force

 Files that aren't in the target snapshot are left alone —
 rollback restores captured files, not "everything the snapshot
 didn't know about." This preserves operator-edited scratch files
 outside the capture-root whitelist (movate.yaml, agents/, ...).

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    hash_or_prefix      TEXT  Snapshot hash or short-hash prefix to restore. Run mdk snapshot   │
│                                list to see available hashes.                                     │
│                                [required]                                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --force                  Required to actually perform the rollback. The default behavior is a    │
│                          dry-run preview that shows what would be restored. Rollback is          │
│                          auto-captured (a pre-rollback snapshot is created first) but it still   │
│                          rewrites files in the working tree — requiring --force matches the mdk  │
│                          snapshot delete safety gate.                                            │
│ --project  -p      PATH  Project root. Defaults to walking up from cwd.                          │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk run`

```

 Usage: mdk run [OPTIONS] PATH INPUT

 Run an agent or workflow against the given input.

 Agent examples:

   # Plain string — auto-wraps to the agent's single required string field
   $ movate run ./faq-agent "What is movate?"

   # See tokens as they arrive (dev-loop preview)
   $ movate run ./faq-agent "hi" --stream

   # Mock mode (no API calls)
   $ movate run ./faq-agent "hello" --mock

   # Replay a stored run against current code (regression debug)
   $ movate run ./faq-agent --replay 4f8a-...

   # Hit a deployed runtime (Azure ACA / local-serve)
   $ mdk run faq "hello world" --target dev

 Workflow examples:

   # Initial state as JSON
   $ movate run ./returns-workflow '{"order_id": "ord-123"}' --mock

   # Initial state from a file
   $ movate run ./returns-workflow --input initial_state.json

 Inside a project you can pass a bare agent or workflow
 name (resolved under ``./agents/<name>/`` or ``./workflows/<name>/``):

   # Both forms work — full path or just the name
   $ mdk run rag-qa '{"question":"..."}'
   $ mdk run ./agents/rag-qa '{"question":"..."}'

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    path           PATH   Path to an agent or workflow directory. [required]                    │
│      input_arg      INPUT  Input: agent mode accepts a plain string (auto-wraps), JSON, file, or │
│                            '-' for stdin. Workflow mode requires JSON, a file, or '-'.           │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --input               -i      TEXT         Alternative way to pass input (preferred for explicit │
│                                            JSON).                                                │
│ --replay                      TEXT         Re-run a recorded RunRecord by id against the current │
│                                            agent code. Pins the original input; everything else  │
│                                            (prompt, model, schemas) comes from disk. Mutually    │
│                                            exclusive with positional INPUT/--input.              │
│ --mock                                     Use the deterministic MockProvider (no API keys; for  │
│                                            smoke tests).                                         │
│ --target                      TEXT         Run against a deployed runtime instead of locally.    │
│                                            Resolves to a target from ~/.movate/config.yaml (URL  │
│                                            + key_env). POSTs the input to                        │
│                                            /api/v1/agents/<name>/runs?wait=true and renders the  │
│                                            resulting RunView the same way as a local run. With   │
│                                            --stream, POSTs to /api/v1/agents/<name>/runs/stream  │
│                                            and renders tokens live over SSE. Mutually exclusive  │
│                                            with --replay (remote runtime owns the RunRecord      │
│                                            history).                                             │
│ --stream                                   Render model tokens to stderr as they arrive          │
│                                            (preview). Final output is still schema-validated +   │
│                                            persisted normally; this flag only adds a live        │
│                                            preview. Workflow + replay modes ignore it.           │
│ --trace                                    After the run, print a table of KB chunks retrieved   │
│                                            by any kb-vector-lookup skill calls. Useful for       │
│                                            debugging retrieval quality.                          │
│ --estimate                                 Predict the cost + latency of this run WITHOUT        │
│                                            executing it. Prints an estimate table (no LLM call,  │
│                                            no job enqueued, no charge). The estimate reflects    │
│                                            this agent's real assembled prompt + real historical  │
│                                            runs. Works locally and against a deployed --target.  │
│                                            RAG agents exclude retrieved-chunk tokens unless      │
│                                            --estimate-retrieval is also passed (small embedding  │
│                                            cost).                                                │
│ --estimate-retrieval                       With --estimate, run the agent's retrieval so         │
│                                            retrieved-chunk tokens are folded into the estimate.  │
│                                            Embeds the query (small cost). No effect on non-RAG   │
│                                            agents or without --estimate.                         │
│ --runtime                     TEXT         Override the workflow execution backend for THIS run  │
│                                            only (ADR 055 D3): native (in-process, default),      │
│                                            temporal (durable/deterministic, needs mdk +          │
│                                            TEMPORAL_HOST), or langgraph (not yet wired — fails   │
│                                            loud). Precedence: this flag > workflow.yaml          │
│                                            'runtime:' field > native. Read-only — never mutates  │
│                                            the spec. Agent runs ignore it.                       │
│ --output              -o      [json|text]  Output format. Defaults to text on interactive        │
│                                            terminals and json when stdout is piped. Use --output │
│                                            json to force JSON from a terminal (e.g. for          │
│                                            scripting).                                           │
│                                            [default: json]                                       │
│ --help                                     Show this message and exit.                           │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

 Usage: mdk runs show [OPTIONS] RUN_ID

 Use this to look up the result of a *past* deployed run by its id —

### `mdk scaffold tool`

```

 Usage: mdk scaffold tool [OPTIONS] NAME

 Generate a new tool directory under ``<target>/<name>/``.

 Example:

   # Scaffold a web-search tool
   $ movate scaffold tool web-search
   ✓ scaffolded tool at ./tools/web-search

   # Custom location
   $ movate scaffold tool sql-query --target ./shared/tools

 Generated layout:

   tools/<name>/
     tool.yaml          — metadata + handler ref + schema refs
     handler.py         — async def handler(input) -> dict stub
     schema/input.json  — TODO: replace stub field(s)
     schema/output.json — TODO: replace stub field(s)

 The tool runtime that actually invokes handler.py lands as
 Tier-2 work (#9 in the high-priority list). Scaffolding today
 means the boilerplate is ready the moment the runtime ships.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      TEXT  Tool name (lowercase, hyphenated). e.g. 'web-search', 'sql-query'.          │
│                      [required]                                                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target        PATH  Parent directory for the new tool. [default: tools]                        │
│ --force               Overwrite an existing tool directory at <target>/<name>/.                  │
│ --help                Show this message and exit.                                                │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk schedule set`

```

 Usage: mdk schedule set [OPTIONS] TARGET

 Set (or update) a cron schedule that enqueues agent/workflow jobs.

 Examples:

   # Run an agent every 6h with a fixed input
   $ mdk schedule set faq-agent --cadence 6h --input '{"text": "daily digest"}'

   # Run a workflow nightly, named, notify on finish
   $ mdk schedule set returns-pipeline -k workflow --cadence 1d \
       --name nightly-returns --notify-email me@co.com

 Drive the tick from cron: mdk scheduler-tick every few
 minutes (Azure: a Container Apps Job). The tick only enqueues schedules
 that are actually due, and drains eval schedules too.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    target      TEXT  Agent or workflow name to run on the cadence. [required]                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --cadence               TEXT                               How often to run: int seconds or a │
│                                                               duration (30m, 6h, 1d).            │
│                                                               [required]                         │
│    --kind          -k      [agent|workflow|eval|bench|observ  Job kind to enqueue: agent |       │
│                            ability_analyze|audit|finetune]    workflow.                          │
│                                                               [default: agent]                   │
│    --name                  TEXT                               Schedule handle (unique per        │
│                                                               tenant). Defaults to the target    │
│                                                               name.                              │
│    --input         -i      TEXT                               Job payload as JSON object, file   │
│                                                               path, or '-' for stdin. Default:   │
│                                                               {}.                                │
│    --disabled                                                 Create the schedule but leave it   │
│                                                               dormant (no enqueue).              │
│    --notify-email          TEXT                               Email to notify when an enqueued   │
│                                                               job finishes.                      │
│    --format                [table|json|markdown]              [default: table]                   │
│    --help                                                     Show this message and exit.        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk scheduler-tick`

```

 Usage: mdk scheduler-tick [OPTIONS]

 Run one unified scheduler tick — enqueue ALL due jobs (ADR 017 D2).

 The unified cron entrypoint. Drains BOTH the eval schedules (ADR 016)
 and the generic agent/workflow schedules (ADR 017) in one pass, so a
 single Container Apps Job (or any cron) keeps every cadence current.
 Enqueues one job per due schedule and stamps each so it won't
 re-enqueue inside its cadence window. A running worker then executes
 the jobs.

 Examples:

   # Run the unified tick (cron calls this on an interval)
   $ mdk scheduler-tick

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --format        [table|json|markdown]  [default: table]                                          │
│ --help                                 Show this message and exit.                               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk schema compile`

```

 Usage: mdk schema compile [OPTIONS] SOURCE

 Compile a schema file to JSON Schema.

 Detects the source DSL (canonical / shorthand / hand-written
 JSON Schema) by inspecting the top-level YAML keys, then
 dispatches to the appropriate compiler.

 Examples:

   # Compile + write to stdout
   $ mdk schema compile schema/input.yaml

   # Compile + write to a file (pretty-printed)
   $ mdk schema compile schema/input.yaml -o schema/input.json --format json-schema-pretty

   # CI smoke: did this file compile cleanly?
   $ mdk schema compile schema/input.yaml --check

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    source      PATH  Path to a .yaml schema file (canonical, shorthand, or JSON                │
│                        Schema-in-YAML).                                                          │
│                        [required]                                                                │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --format  -f      TEXT  Output format: json-schema (default; compact) or json-schema-pretty      │
│                         (indented).                                                              │
│                         [default: json-schema]                                                   │
│ --output  -o      PATH  Write output to this file (default: stdout).                             │
│ --check                 Validate the source compiles cleanly but don't emit output. CI-friendly. │
│ --help                  Show this message and exit.                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk secrets export-shell`

```

 Usage: mdk secrets export-shell [OPTIONS]

 Emit shell ``export`` statements for every secret in the profile.

 Designed for command substitution into the current shell:

   $ eval $(mdk secrets export-shell)

 Plain stdout, no Rich. Each secret becomes ``export NAME='value'``
 with single-quote-escaped value (handles embedded ``$`` / quotes
 safely). The secrets remain in the parent shell's process env
 for child commands to read — same pattern `dotenv` uses.

 ⚠ never run this on a screenshared terminal
 — the export lines render the values in plain text. Use the
 explicit ``mdk secrets get`` for safer one-off retrieval.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --profile  -p      TEXT  Override the active profile.                                            │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk secrets get`

```

 Usage: mdk secrets get [OPTIONS] NAME

 Print a secret's value to stdout.

 Plain stdout write, no Rich formatting — designed
 for command substitution: ``MY_KEY=$(mdk secrets get MY_KEY)``.

 Use sparingly: any command that echoes a secret risks leaking it
 via shell history or terminal scrollback. For shell sourcing,
 prefer mdk secrets export-shell which never echoes
 the value to a terminal that's likely to be screenshared.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      TEXT  Secret name to retrieve. [required]                                         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --profile  -p      TEXT  Override the active profile.                                            │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk secrets list`

```

 Usage: mdk secrets list [OPTIONS]

 List secret names in the active profile. NEVER displays values.

 Values stay opaque in this view — operators check them via
 explicit `get`. Reduces accidental-shoulder-surfing risk.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --profile  -p      TEXT  Override the active profile.                                            │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk secrets set`

```

 Usage: mdk secrets set [OPTIONS] NAME

 Store a secret in the active profile.

 Re-running on an existing name updates the value + bumps the
 last_rotated timestamp. The original created_at is preserved
 so rotation history is auditable later.

 ⚠ MVP: secrets are stored UNENCRYPTED on disk
 (file permission 0600 is the only line of defense). For
 production secrets use Key Vault directly today; native
 encryption + cloud sync land as Sprint O follow-ups.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      TEXT  Secret name (e.g. OPENAI_API_KEY). [required]                               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --value                TEXT  The secret value. Omit to be prompted interactively (input hidden — │
│                              preferred for security).                                            │
│ --description  -d      TEXT  Operator-supplied note about this secret.                           │
│ --profile      -p      TEXT  Override the active profile for this operation only.                │
│ --help                       Show this message and exit.                                         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk serve`

```

 Usage: mdk serve [OPTIONS]

 Start the movate FastAPI runtime.

 Examples:

 # Default — binds 127.0.0.1:8000, scans ./agents/, 60 req/min/key
 $ movate serve

 # Custom port + remote-accessible
 $ movate serve --host 0.0.0.0 --port 8080

 # Higher rate limit for a high-traffic prod deploy
 $ movate serve --rate-limit-per-minute 600

 # Disable rate limiting (single-tenant dev)
 $ movate serve --rate-limit-per-minute 0

 # Local dev: auto-seed a dev key + print the playground command
 $ movate serve --dev

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --host                         TEXT     Bind host. [default: 127.0.0.1]                          │
│ --port                         INTEGER  Bind port. [default: 8000]                               │
│ --agents-path                  PATH     Directory to scan for agent.yaml files. Falls back to    │
│                                         empty catalog if missing.                                │
│                                         [env var: MDK_AGENTS_PATH, MOVATE_AGENTS_PATH]           │
│                                         [default: agents]                                        │
│ --skills-path                  PATH     Directory where POST /api/v1/skills persists uploaded    │
│                                         skill bundles, and where the agent loader looks for      │
│                                         skill registry entries. Defaults to                      │
│                                         <agents-path>/skills/ to match the loader's project-root │
│                                         fallback.                                                │
│                                         [env var: MDK_SKILLS_PATH, MOVATE_SKILLS_PATH]           │
│ --log-level                    TEXT     uvicorn log level (debug | info | warning | error).      │
│                                         [default: info]                                          │
│ --rate-limit-per-minute        INTEGER  Per-API-key token-bucket capacity (steady-state          │
│                                         requests/min). Default 60. Set to 0 to disable rate      │
│                                         limiting entirely (returns ``X-RateLimit-Limit: 0``      │
│                                         headers — operator's signal that limiting is OFF).       │
│                                         [env var: MDK_RATE_LIMIT_PER_MINUTE,                     │
│                                         MOVATE_RATE_LIMIT_PER_MINUTE]                            │
│                                         [default: 60]                                            │
│ --cors-origins                 TEXT     Comma-separated list of allowed origins for the CORS     │
│                                         middleware (e.g.                                         │
│                                         'http://localhost:4200,https://mova-io.movate.com').     │
│                                         Empty string (default) leaves the middleware off — fine  │
│                                         for server-to-server use cases; required for the Mova iO │
│                                         Angular front end to call this runtime from the browser. │
│                                         Use '*' for fully-permissive local dev only.             │
│                                         [env var: MDK_CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGINS,                      │
│                                         MOVATE_CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGINS]                             │
│ --dev                                   LOCAL-DEV ONLY. Auto-mint + seed a known dev API key on  │
│                                         startup and print the ready-to-run playground command,   │
│                                         so testing against this runtime is a single copy-paste.  │
│                                         Does NOT disable auth — it only seeds a valid key (auth  │
│                                         still enforced). REFUSED on a non-loopback --host (never │
│                                         seeds a known key on a publicly reachable bind). NEVER   │
│                                         use in production.                                       │
│ --help                                  Show this message and exit.                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk simulate`

```

 Usage: mdk simulate [OPTIONS] CHATBOT

 Stress-test a chatbot by running it through multi-turn scenarios.

 Each scenario is a (persona, goal, initial_message) tuple. A
 simulated "user" LLM drives the conversation toward the goal;
 the chatbot replies; we capture every turn. Operators read
 transcripts to spot chatbots that lose the thread, refuse when
 they shouldn't, or hallucinate.

 Where mdk eval checks single input→output pairs,
 simulate checks the conversational ARC — the surface
 area single-turn evals miss.

 Examples:

   $ mdk simulate triage --num 3                # 3 generated scenarios
   $ mdk simulate triage --scenarios cases.jsonl
   $ mdk simulate triage --num 5 --max-turns 8 --output sim.json
   $ mdk simulate triage --num 3 --mock         # offline / hermetic

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      CHATBOT  Chatbot agent name (resolved under agents/<name>) or a literal path to   │
│                         the agent directory.                                                     │
│                         [required]                                                               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --num             -n      INTEGER  How many scenarios to run when --scenarios is not given.      │
│                                    Default 3; max 50.                                            │
│                                    [default: 3]                                                  │
│ --scenarios               TEXT     Path to a JSONL of scenarios. Each line: {persona, goal,      │
│                                    initial_message, max_turns}. Overrides --num when provided.   │
│ --max-turns               INTEGER  Per-scenario turn cap (default 6; max 20). Each scenario from │
│                                    a file may override this via its own max_turns.               │
│                                    [default: 6]                                                  │
│ --output          -o      TEXT     Save full transcripts to PATH (JSON). Skipped if empty.       │
│ --pass-rate-gate          FLOAT    CI gate: exit non-zero if goal-achievement rate < threshold   │
│                                    (0.0 to 1.0). Default -1 = no gate. Example: --pass-rate-gate │
│                                    0.7 fails if fewer than 70% of scenarios reached their goal.  │
│                                    [default: -1.0]                                               │
│ --mock                             Run scenarios deterministically with MockProvider — no LLM    │
│                                    call. Each scenario runs one chatbot turn + auto-marks        │
│                                    achieved. Useful for tests + sanity-checking the wiring.      │
│ --help                             Show this message and exit.                                   │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk skills add-mcp`

```

 Usage: mdk skills add-mcp [OPTIONS] ENTRY

 Register an MCP server as a skill in one command.

 Connects to the server, discovers available tools via ``tools/list``,
 and scaffolds a ``skills/<name>/skill.yaml`` with ``kind: mcp``.
 When ``--tool`` is omitted, creates a multi-tool skill that exposes
 ALL tools from the server as namespaced callables.

 Examples:

   # stdio server — multi-tool
   $ mdk skills add-mcp 'npx -y @modelcontextprotocol/server-github'

   # HTTP/SSE server — multi-tool
   $ mdk skills add-mcp https://mcp.example.com/api

   # single tool only
   $ mdk skills add-mcp 'npx -y @modelcontextprotocol/server-github' --tool create_issue

   # custom name
   $ mdk skills add-mcp https://mcp.slack.com --name slack-mcp

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    entry      TEXT  MCP server URL (https://...) or subprocess command (e.g. 'npx -y           │
│                       @modelcontextprotocol/server-github').                                     │
│                       [required]                                                                 │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --name     -n      TEXT  Override the auto-derived skill name.                                   │
│ --tool     -t      TEXT  Restrict to a single tool (single-tool mode). Omit for multi-tool.      │
│ --project  -p      PATH  Project root. The skill lands at ``<project>/skills/<name>/``.          │
│                          [default: .]                                                            │
│ --force                  Overwrite ``skills/<name>/`` if it already exists.                      │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk skills run`

```

 Usage: mdk skills run [OPTIONS] NAME INPUT_JSON

 Invoke a skill directly, bypassing the agent + tool-use loop.

 Validates the input against the skill's schema, dispatches via
 the matching backend (python | http | mcp), validates the output,
 and prints the result as JSON. The same code path the executor
 runs for each tool call inside a real agent.

 Use this to iterate on ``impl.py`` (or the HTTP API shape behind
 an http skill) without paying the LLM cost of a full agent run.

 Examples:

   # Run a Python skill with a synthetic input
   $ mdk skills run calculator '{"expression": "41 + 1"}'

   # Run an HTTP skill (env vars for auth are read from the shell)
   $ CRM_TOKEN=... mdk skills run warranty-lookup '{"case_id": "abc-123"}'

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name            TEXT  Skill name as it appears in the project's skills/ registry.           │
│                            [required]                                                            │
│ *    input_json      TEXT  JSON input dict, matching the skill's input schema. [required]        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --project     -p      PATH     Project root containing ``skills/<name>/``. [default: .]          │
│ --timeout-ms          INTEGER  Per-call timeout in milliseconds. Used for debug invocations;     │
│                                agent-driven calls inherit from agent.yaml instead.               │
│                                [default: 60000]                                                  │
│ --help                         Show this message and exit.                                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk skills scaffold`

```

 Usage: mdk skills scaffold [OPTIONS] NAME

 Scaffold a starter skill from the packaged template.

 Creates ``<project>/skills/<name>/`` with a complete sample:
 ``skill.yaml`` wired to ``impl.py:run``, a starter Python function
 that echoes its input, and a README that walks through how to test
 it (`mdk skills run`) and wire it into an agent.

 Examples:

   # Drop a starter calculator skill in cwd
   $ mdk skills scaffold calculator

   # Drop it in a specific project
   $ mdk skills scaffold calculator --project ~/work/my-project

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      TEXT  Skill name (lowercase, hyphen-separated). Matches the directory created.    │
│                      [required]                                                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --project  -p      PATH  Project root. The skill lands at ``<project>/skills/<name>/``.          │
│                          [default: .]                                                            │
│ --force                  Overwrite ``skills/<name>/`` if it already exists.                      │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk skills search`

```

 Usage: mdk skills search [OPTIONS]

 Search the project's skill registry by tag, freetext, and/or kind.

 Outputs a Rich table: name | kind | version | tags | description.

 Examples:

   # All skills tagged 'crm'
   $ mdk skills search --tag crm

   # Skills whose name or description contains 'lookup'
   $ mdk skills search --query lookup

   # HTTP-backed skills only
   $ mdk skills search --kind http

   # Combine filters
   $ mdk skills search --tag crm --kind http

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --tag      -t      TEXT  Filter by tag (exact match, case-insensitive).                          │
│ --query    -q      TEXT  Freetext match against skill name and description (case-insensitive).   │
│ --kind     -k      TEXT  Filter by backend kind: python | http | mcp | agent.                    │
│ --project  -p      PATH  Project root containing ``skills/<name>/``. Defaults to cwd.            │
│                          [default: .]                                                            │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk skills validate`

```

 Usage: mdk skills validate [OPTIONS] [AGENT]

 Validate skill compatibility for agent(s).

 For each agent x skill pair checks:

 (a) each skill name resolves in the project's skill registry;
 (b) the skill's output schema has the fields the agent's prompt
     references via ``{{skill_name.field}}`` patterns
     (best-effort parse);
 (c) produces a pass/fail table per agent x skill.

 Examples:

   # Validate all agents
   $ mdk skills validate

   # Validate one agent
   $ mdk skills validate rag-qa

   # From a different project root
   $ mdk skills validate --project ~/work/my-project

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   agent      [AGENT]  Agent name (resolves under ``agents/<name>/``) or path to an agent         │
│                       directory. Omit to validate every agent in the project.                    │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --project  -p      PATH  Project root containing ``agents/`` and ``skills/``. Defaults to cwd.   │
│                          [default: .]                                                            │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk snapshot`

```

 Usage: mdk snapshot [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Capture / compare / restore project state. Snapshots are immutable + content-addressed (git-style
 hash); two snapshots of identical state collide deterministically. Pairs with mdk diff, rollback,
 promote (next in Sprint N).

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ create   Capture the current project state as an immutable snapshot.                             │
│ list     List every snapshot in the project's ``.movate/snapshots/`` dir.                        │
│ show     Display a snapshot's manifest in detail.                                                │
│ delete   Remove a snapshot from disk.                                                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk snapshot create`

```

 Usage: mdk snapshot create [OPTIONS]

 Capture the current project state as an immutable snapshot.

 Captures: movate.yaml, policy.yaml, knowledge.yaml, and every
 file under agents/ + contexts/ + workflows/ + skills/. Each
 file is hashed (sha256); the snapshot's own hash is the SHA-256
 of the manifest. Idempotent — re-running over identical state
 returns the same hash + skips the disk write.

 Files live at .movate/snapshots/<short-hash>/:
   - manifest.yaml — the metadata
   - files/ — copy of captured project files

 Future operational commands operate on these snapshots:
   mdk diff <a> <b>     # what changed between two snapshots
   mdk rollback <hash>  # restore a prior snapshot
   mdk audit <hash>     # production-readiness scan

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --description  -d      TEXT  One-line description of what this snapshot represents. Surfaced in  │
│                              mdk snapshot list + show. Pick something searchable: 'green deploy  │
│                              before model swap', 'staging baseline 2026-05-15', etc.             │
│ --project      -p      PATH  Project root. Defaults to walking up from cwd for movate.yaml.      │
│ --help                       Show this message and exit.                                         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk snapshot delete`

```

 Usage: mdk snapshot delete [OPTIONS] HASH_OR_PREFIX

 Remove a snapshot from disk.

 Defaults to dry-run. Run with ``--force`` to actually
 delete. Snapshots are immutable + part of the project audit trail;
 deleting one should be a deliberate decision, not a reflex.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    hash_or_prefix      TEXT  Snapshot hash or short-hash prefix to remove. [required]          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --force                  Required to actually delete — the default behavior is to print what     │
│                          would be deleted and exit non-zero. Snapshots are immutable + part of   │
│                          the audit trail; deleting one should be a deliberate operator decision. │
│ --project  -p      PATH  Project root.                                                           │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk submit`

```

 Usage: mdk submit [OPTIONS] AGENT INPUT

 Queue a job at a deployed runtime and (optionally) wait for completion.

 Examples:

 # Fire-and-forget against the active target
 $ movate submit faq-agent '{"text": "what is movate?"}'
 → prints {"job_id": "...", "status": "queued"} on stdout

 # Wait for completion + desktop chime when done
 $ movate submit faq-agent '{"text": "..."}' --wait --notify

 # Workflow kind, against prod
 $ movate submit returns-pipeline -t prod -k workflow -i initial_state.json

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    agent          TEXT   Agent or workflow name registered on the target runtime (see `movate  │
│                            jobs list-agents`).                                                   │
│                            [required]                                                            │
│      input_arg      INPUT  Input as JSON object, file path, or '-' for stdin. If the agent has   │
│                            exactly one required string field, a plain string is auto-wrapped.    │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --input          -i      TEXT                                Alternative way to pass input.      │
│ --kind           -k      [agent|workflow|eval|bench|observa  [default: agent]                    │
│                          bility_analyze|audit|finetune]                                          │
│ --target         -t      TEXT                                Deployment target name (from        │
│                                                              `movate config list-targets`). Omit │
│                                                              to use the active target.           │
│ --wait           -w                                          Block until the job reaches a       │
│                                                              terminal state, then print the      │
│                                                              result.                             │
│ --timeout                FLOAT                               Max seconds to wait when --wait is  │
│                                                              set. After this the job continues   │
│                                                              server-side; CLI exits 124.         │
│                                                              [default: 300.0]                    │
│ --poll-interval          FLOAT                               Seconds between job-status polls    │
│                                                              (--wait only).                      │
│                                                              [default: 1.0]                      │
│ --notify                                                     Desktop notification when --wait    │
│                                                              completes (macOS terminal-notifier  │
│                                                              / osascript, Linux notify-send).    │
│                                                              No-op on unsupported platforms.     │
│ --notify-email           TEXT                                Email address the server-side       │
│                                                              worker emails when the job reaches  │
│                                                              a terminal status. Worker must have │
│                                                              SMTP configured (MDK_SMTP_HOST +    │
│                                                              creds) or it falls back to logging  │
│                                                              only.                               │
│ --output         -o      [table|json]                        [default: table]                    │
│ --help                                                       Show this message and exit.         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

 Usage: mdk teams-bot [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 design.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ serve   Boot the Teams bot webhook on ``host:port``.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk teams-bot serve`

```

 Usage: mdk teams-bot serve [OPTIONS]

 Boot the Teams bot webhook on ``host:port``.

 Quickstart for local dev:

 Terminal 1 — run the Movate runtime:

     $ mdk serve --agents-path ./agents --port 8000

 Terminal 2 — issue an API key for the bot:

     $ mdk auth create-key --tenant local --name teams-bot

 Terminal 3 — run the Teams bot pointed at the runtime:

     $ MOVATE_TEAMS_FLEET_API_KEY=mvt_... \
         mdk teams-bot serve --runtime-url http://127.0.0.1:8000

 Terminal 4 — point the Bot Framework Emulator at
 ``http://localhost:3978/api/messages``. ``@movate ping`` confirms
 the wire works; ``@movate run faq-agent {"question": "hi"}``
 drives a real round-trip through the runtime and renders the
 result as an Adaptive Card.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --host                        TEXT     Bind host. [default: 0.0.0.0]                             │
│ --port                        INTEGER  Bind port. 3978 is the Bot Framework Emulator default —   │
│                                        leave it unless you have a reason to change.              │
│                                        [default: 3978]                                           │
│ --log-level                   TEXT     uvicorn log level (debug | info | warning | error).       │
│                                        [default: info]                                           │
│ --runtime-url                 TEXT     Base URL of the Movate runtime the bot forwards `run` /   │
│                                        `eval` commands to. Required when the bot is expected to  │
│                                        actually run anything (it is, in 3.1.b+).                 │
│                                        [env var: MDK_RUNTIME_URL, MOVATE_RUNTIME_URL]            │
│                                        [default: http://127.0.0.1:8000]                          │
│ --fleet-api-key               TEXT     The bot's API key for the runtime. Required when          │
│                                        --runtime-url is set. Falls back to the                   │
│                                        MOVATE_TEAMS_FLEET_API_KEY env var; warned (not failed)   │
│                                        when absent so the bot still boots for `ping` / `help`    │
│                                        smoke tests.                                              │
│                                        [env var: MDK_TEAMS_FLEET_API_KEY,                        │
│                                        MOVATE_TEAMS_FLEET_API_KEY]                               │
│ --langfuse-public-host        TEXT     Public Langfuse base URL. When set, successful run cards  │
│                                        include a 'View trace' button. Off by default — only      │
│                                        enable when the URL is routable for the audience (don't   │
│                                        show prospects an internal-only URL).                     │
│                                        [env var: MDK_TEAMS_LANGFUSE_PUBLIC_HOST,                 │
│                                        MOVATE_TEAMS_LANGFUSE_PUBLIC_HOST]                        │
│ --no-identity                          Disable per-user identity binding (3.1.c) — the bot uses  │
│                                        only the fleet API key for every user. Lets you run the   │
│                                        bot without MOVATE_TEAMS_ENCRYPTION_KEY for smoke tests.  │
│ --require-binding                      Strict mode: reject `run` from users who haven't bound    │
│                                        their own Movate API key. Default OFF (alpha) — the bot   │
│                                        falls back to the fleet key for unbound users. Turn ON    │
│                                        for multi-tenant deployments where every run must be      │
│                                        attributable.                                             │
│                                        [env var: MDK_TEAMS_REQUIRE_BINDING,                      │
│                                        MOVATE_TEAMS_REQUIRE_BINDING]                             │
│ --help                                 Show this message and exit.                               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk templates list`

```

 Usage: mdk templates list [OPTIONS]

 List every template `mdk init -t <name>` / `mdk add <name>` accepts.

 Renders a Rich table by default; pass ``--json`` for machine output
 consumed by scripts and external editors. The table view includes a
 legacy-fallback row for any template missing the new ADR 028
 ``template.yaml`` so partial migrations don't drop rows.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --json               Emit a JSON array of template records to stdout. The shape follows          │
│                      :meth:`TemplateInfo.to_dict` and is a stable public contract (CLAUDE.md     │
│                      rule 5). Templates missing a ``template.yaml`` are omitted from the JSON    │
│                      view — use the rendered table for the full legacy listing.                  │
│ --shape        TEXT  Filter rows by shape — agent or workflow. Omit to list everything.          │
│ --help               Show this message and exit.                                                 │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk templates show`

```

 Usage: mdk templates show [OPTIONS] NAME

 Show full metadata + on-disk file tree for one template.

 Fails with exit code 1 when the template name is unknown so scripts
 can detect missing templates cleanly. Output is Rich by default;
 pass ``--json`` for a stable machine-readable record.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      TEXT  Template name to inspect. [required]                                        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --json          Emit one template record as JSON. Same shape as the records from ``mdk templates │
│                 list --json`` so scripts can use either command interchangeably. The file tree   │
│                 is omitted from JSON — callers wanting it can walk ``directory`` themselves.     │
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

### `mdk tenants clear-budget`

```

 Usage: mdk tenants clear-budget [OPTIONS] TENANT_ID

 Remove the budget cap for ``tenant_id`` (unlimited spend).

 The row stays in the table so the audit trail (``created_at`` /
 ``updated_at``) is preserved — the limit just becomes ``NULL``.

 Prompts before clearing — this can cost real money if it's a
 misclick — pass ``-y`` to bypass for scripts.

│ *    tenant_id      TEXT  Tenant id. [required]                                                  │

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮

### `mdk tenants quota`

```

 Usage: mdk tenants quota [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 View or update per-tenant quotas (ADR 036 D2).

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ show   Show the configured quota + current usage + remaining for ``tenant_id``.                  │

╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk tenants quota set`

```

 Usage: mdk tenants quota set [OPTIONS] TENANT_ID

 Write the per-tenant quota row to the config file.

 CLI side only — the runtime reads the file at app build / on the next
 cache miss. Existing rows for ``tenant_id`` are replaced; new rows are
 appended. Unset limits stay unset (no ceiling for that counter).

 Examples:

   # Warn-only ceiling at $500/month (rollout posture)
   $ movate tenants quota set 4f1a7c... --monthly-cost 500 --mode warn

   # Hard 50k-tokens/day ceiling on a free-tier tenant
   $ movate tenants quota set 4f1a7c... --daily-tokens 50000 --mode deny

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    tenant_id      TEXT  Tenant id. [required]                                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --daily-tokens          INTEGER  Daily token ceiling (input + output). Pass 0 / omit to leave    │
│                                  unset.                                                          │
│ --daily-requests        INTEGER  Daily request-count ceiling. Pass 0 / omit to leave unset.      │
│ --monthly-cost          FLOAT    Monthly cost ceiling in USD. Pass 0 / omit to leave unset.      │
│ --mode                  TEXT     warn (log + header + allow) or deny (429 over ceiling).         │
│                                  [default: warn]                                                 │
│ --help                           Show this message and exit.                                     │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk tenants quota show`

```

 Usage: mdk tenants quota show [OPTIONS] TENANT_ID

 Show the configured quota + current usage + remaining for ``tenant_id``.

 Surfaces the values the runtime middleware uses for its admission
 check — so the operator can preview "is this tenant about to be
 blocked / warned?" before it happens.

 Reads the quota config via :func:`load_quota_config` and the
 persisted runs via the configured ``StorageProvider`` (same as the
 runtime; consistent answer).

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    tenant_id      TEXT  Tenant id. [required]                                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

 # Cap a customer at $500/mo

│                                tenant once current-month spend hits this value.                  │

│    --help                      Show this message and exit.                                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

### `mdk trigger create`

```

 Usage: mdk trigger create [OPTIONS] TARGET

 Register an inbound event/webhook trigger.

 Mints a per-trigger secret + a stable public webhook id, persists the
 trigger (secret hashed at rest), and prints the webhook URL, the secret
 once (irrecoverable after), and an example signed ``curl``.

 Examples:

   # Fire a ticket-triage agent on an inbound ticket webhook
   $ mdk trigger create triage-agent --name zendesk-ticket \
       --input-defaults '{"source": "zendesk"}'

   # A disabled (dormant) workflow trigger
   $ mdk trigger create returns-pipeline -k workflow --disabled

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    target      TEXT  Agent or workflow name to run when the trigger fires. [required]          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --kind            -k      [agent|workflow|eval|bench|observa  Job kind to enqueue: agent |       │
│                           bility_analyze|audit|finetune]      workflow.                          │
│                                                               [default: agent]                   │
│ --name                    TEXT                                Trigger handle (unique per         │
│                                                               tenant). Defaults to the target    │
│                                                               name.                              │
│ --input-defaults  -i      TEXT                                Default job payload merged UNDER   │
│                                                               the event body: JSON object, file, │
│                                                               or '-'. Default: {}.               │
│ --disabled                                                    Create the trigger but leave it    │
│                                                               dormant (won't fire).              │
│ --format                  [table|json|markdown]               [default: table]                   │
│ --help                                                        Show this message and exit.        │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```
