### `mdk tune`

```

 Usage: mdk tune [OPTIONS] AGENT INPUT

 Sweep one knob across a list of values and show the outputs.

 Same input + same prompt + different knobs. Helps you answer "what
 happens when I lower temperature?" without standing up
 a real A/B framework. Not auto-prompt-engineering —
 no prompt edits, no iteration, no recommendations. You read the
 comparison table and decide.

 Examples:

   $ mdk tune triage '{"text": "x"}' --sweep temperature=0.0,0.5,1.0
   $ mdk tune triage '{"text": "x"}' --sweep max_tokens=128,512 --runs 3
   $ mdk tune triage '{"text": "x"}' [/dim]
       --sweep model=openai/gpt-4o-mini,anthropic/claude-haiku-4-5-20251001 --mock

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    agent_name      AGENT  Agent name (resolved under agents/<name>) or a literal path to an    │
│                             agent directory.                                                     │
│                             [required]                                                           │
│ *    input_arg       INPUT  Input as a JSON object, a path to a JSON file, or '-' for stdin.     │
│                             Same syntax mdk run accepts.                                         │
│                             [required]                                                           │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --sweep          TEXT     What to sweep, KEY=V1,V2,V3 form. Valid keys: temperature,          │
│                              max_tokens, model. Example: --sweep temperature=0.0,0.5,1.0.        │
│                              [required]                                                          │
│    --runs           INTEGER  Samples per swept value. Bump to 3+ to surface variance when the    │
│                              agent uses non-deterministic decoding. Default 1.                   │
│                              [default: 1]                                                        │
│    --mock                    Use MockProvider — offline / hermetic / no API key needed.          │
│    --persist                 Persist the swept runs to storage. Off by default — sweep runs are  │
│                              usually noise that pollutes mdk costs report. Reserved: today the   │
│                              executor always persists; this flag will become meaningful once the │
│                              executor exposes a no-persist hook (Sprint S+).                     │
│    --json                    Emit per-(value, sample) results as JSON. Skips the Rich rendering. │
│    --help                    Show this message and exit.                                         │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk validate`

```

 Usage: mdk validate [OPTIONS] [PATH]

 Validate ``agent.yaml`` (or ``workflow.yaml``) plus its references.

 Inside a project you can pass a bare name (``mdk validate rag-qa``);
 it resolves under ``./agents/<name>/`` or ``./workflows/<name>/``.

 Use --all to validate every agent + workflow in the
 current project in one shot — handy right after
 mdk init --project --with-agents X,Y,Z.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│   path      [PATH]  Path to an agent or workflow directory. Omit with --all to validate every    │
│                     agent + workflow in the current project.                                     │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --all              Validate every agent under ./agents/ AND every workflow under ./workflows/ in │
│                    the current project. Renders a summary table; exits non-zero if any fail.     │
│                    Pairs with mdk init --project --with-agents as the natural next step.         │
│ --strict           Promote lint warnings to errors (exit 2 on any warning). CI gate flag.        │
│ --no-lint          Skip the prompt linter (schema + policy checks still run).                    │
│ --json             Emit a machine-readable JSON result instead of Rich output. Useful for CI     │
│                    dashboards and scripts that parse validate output.                            │
│ --help             Show this message and exit.                                                   │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk voice`

```

 Usage: mdk voice [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Terminal voice conversation + voice provider tooling. Requires mdk (``pip install 'movate-cli'``).

 Examples:
 $ mdk voice try my-agent                  # live mic → WS → TTS
 $ mdk voice try my-agent --mode realtime  # realtime path
 $ mdk voice providers list                # show STT/TTS providers

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ try          Start a terminal voice conversation with an agent.                                  │
│ say          Speak a one-shot answer: text in → the agent answers → spoken audio out.            │
│ transcribe   Transcribe an audio file: audio in → transcript out (STT only).                     │
│ ask          Ask in one shot: spoken audio in → transcript + answer + spoken audio out.          │
│ call         Initiate an outbound phone call and connect it to an mdk voice agent.               │
│ bench        Run the voice eval/regression harness over a golden audio corpus.                   │
│ providers    Voice provider tooling — list available STT/TTS providers.                          │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk voice ask`

```

 Usage: mdk voice ask [OPTIONS] AGENT AUDIO

 Ask in one shot: spoken audio in → transcript + answer + spoken audio out.

 The request/response companion to ``voice try`` — drives the REST one-shot
 ``POST /api/v1/agents/{name}/voice`` (ADR 050 D2). Prints the recognized
 transcript and the agent's answer, and saves/sizes the synthesized reply
 audio.

 Examples:

   # One-shot spoken Q&A against a recorded question
   $ mdk voice ask faq-bot question.wav --out answer.pcm

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    agent      TEXT  Agent name on the target runtime. [required]                               │
│ *    audio      TEXT  Path to an audio file (the spoken question). [required]                    │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target    -t      TEXT  Runtime URL or config target name.                                     │
│ --api-key           TEXT  Bearer key for the runtime (falls back to env vars).                   │
│ --out       -o      TEXT  Write the synthesized answer audio to this file.                       │
│ --stt               TEXT  STT provider override.                                                 │
│ --tts               TEXT  TTS provider override.                                                 │
│ --voice-id          TEXT  TTS voice id override.                                                 │
│ --language          TEXT  STT language hint.                                                     │
│ --codec             TEXT  Codec of the input audio (pcm16/opus/mulaw). [default: pcm16]          │
│ --mock                    Run the agent stage offline (no live LLM key).                         │
│ --help                    Show this message and exit.                                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk voice bench`

```

 Usage: mdk voice bench [OPTIONS]

 Run the voice eval/regression harness over a golden audio corpus.

 Benchmarks configured STT providers on WER + latency, and TTS providers on
 first-byte + total latency. Compares against a saved baseline to catch
 regressions (ADR 049 D5 — standing bake-off).

 Examples:

   # Run with fake providers (CI / harness validation)
   $ mdk voice bench --fakes

   # Run and save a baseline
   $ mdk voice bench --fakes --save-baseline

   # Run and fail on regression
   $ mdk voice bench --fakes --fail-on-regression

   # JSON output for CI consumption
   $ mdk voice bench --fakes --output json

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --corpus                      TEXT  Path to corpus directory with manifest.json (default:        │
│                                     tests/voice/corpus).                                         │
│ --output              -o      TEXT  Output format: 'table' (default) or 'json'. [default: table] │
│ --save-baseline                     Write results as voice-bench-baseline.json for future        │
│                                     regression checks.                                           │
│ --fail-on-regression                Compare against voice-bench-baseline.json; exit non-zero on  │
│                                     regression.                                                  │
│ --baseline                    TEXT  Path to baseline file (default: voice-bench-baseline.json in │
│                                     project root).                                               │
│ --fakes                             Use in-memory fake providers (for CI / harness validation).  │
│ --help                              Show this message and exit.                                  │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

```

 Usage: mdk voice call [OPTIONS] AGENT

 Initiate an outbound phone call and connect it to an mdk voice agent.

 For testing: calls ``--to`` from your Twilio number and bridges the call
 to the agent via the Twilio Media Stream. Requires the ````

 Example:

   $ mdk voice call support-agent --to +12175551234 --from +12179195393

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --to                 TEXT  Phone number to call (E.164, e.g. +12175551234). [required]        │
│    --from               TEXT  Your Twilio phone number (E.164). Defaults to TWILIO_PHONE_NUMBER  │
│                               env var.                                                           │
│    --target     -t      TEXT  Runtime URL (defaults to local dev).                               │
│    --transport          TEXT  Telephony transport to use. [default: twilio]                      │
│    --help                     Show this message and exit.                                        │

### `mdk voice providers list`

```

 Usage: mdk voice providers list [OPTIONS]

 List available STT and TTS voice providers on the target runtime.

 Reads the ``GET /api/v1/capabilities`` endpoint (ADR 050 D4) and prints the
 ``voice`` section: which modes are available, which STT/TTS providers are
 configured, and whether voice is enabled at all.

 Examples:

   # Against the local runtime
   $ mdk voice providers list

   # Against a specific target
   $ mdk voice providers list --target https://mdk-prod.example.com

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target   -t      TEXT  Runtime URL or config target name.                                      │
│ --api-key          TEXT  Bearer key for the runtime (falls back to env vars).                    │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

### `mdk voice say`

```

 Usage: mdk voice say [OPTIONS] AGENT TEXT

 Speak a one-shot answer: text in → the agent answers → spoken audio out.

 Drives ``POST /api/v1/agents/{name}/voice`` (ADR 050 D2/D11) with the typed
 ``text`` — STT is bypassed server-side, so this is the "have the agent say
 something" path. Prints the agent's answer text and saves/sizes the
 synthesized audio.

 Examples:

   # Have faq-bot answer a question and save the spoken reply
   $ mdk voice say faq-bot "what are your hours?" --out reply.pcm

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    agent      TEXT  Agent name on the target runtime. [required]                               │
│ *    text       TEXT  Text for the agent to answer / speak. [required]                           │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target    -t      TEXT  Runtime URL or config target name.                                     │
│ --api-key           TEXT  Bearer key for the runtime (falls back to env vars).                   │
│ --out       -o      TEXT  Write the synthesized answer audio to this file.                       │
│ --tts               TEXT  TTS provider override (e.g. 'cartesia').                               │
│ --voice-id          TEXT  TTS voice id override.                                                 │
│ --mock                    Run the agent stage offline (no live LLM key).                         │
│ --help                    Show this message and exit.                                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk voice transcribe`

```

 Usage: mdk voice transcribe [OPTIONS] AUDIO

 Transcribe an audio file: audio in → transcript out (STT only).

 Drives ``POST /api/v1/agents/{name}/voice?audio=none`` (ADR 050 D2/D11):
 sends the file, prints the recognized transcript, and skips synthesis (no
 answer audio). The agent still runs (a voice turn IS a run, ADR 050 D1), but
 only the transcript is surfaced.

 Examples:

   # Transcribe a recording
   $ mdk voice transcribe call.wav --target https://mdk-prod.example.com

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    audio      TEXT  Path to an audio file to transcribe. [required]                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --agent     -a      TEXT  Agent whose voice route runs the transcription (any agent works).      │
│                           [default: default]                                                     │
│ --target    -t      TEXT  Runtime URL or config target name.                                     │
│ --api-key           TEXT  Bearer key for the runtime (falls back to env vars).                   │
│ --stt               TEXT  STT provider override (e.g. 'deepgram').                               │
│ --language          TEXT  STT language hint (e.g. 'en').                                         │
│ --codec             TEXT  Codec of the input audio (pcm16/opus/mulaw). [default: pcm16]          │
│ --help                    Show this message and exit.                                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk voice try`

```

 Usage: mdk voice try [OPTIONS] AGENT

 Start a terminal voice conversation with an agent.

 Captures mic audio via sounddevice (part of the  extra), streams
 PCM frames over the WS ``/api/v1/agents/{name}/voice`` endpoint, prints
 partial and final transcripts to the terminal, and plays TTS audio replies
 through the default audio output device.

 Press Ctrl-C to end the call.

 Examples:

   # Pipeline (STT → unchanged text agent → TTS)
   $ mdk voice try my-agent

   # Against a specific runtime target
   $ mdk voice try my-agent --target https://mdk-prod.example.com

   # Realtime (voice↔voice) path
   $ mdk voice try my-agent --mode realtime

   # Override STT/TTS provider for this session
   $ mdk voice try my-agent --stt deepgram --tts cartesia

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    agent      TEXT  Agent name on the target runtime. [required]                               │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target   -t      TEXT  Runtime URL or config target name.                                      │
│ --api-key          TEXT  Bearer key for the runtime (falls back to env vars).                    │
│ --mode             TEXT  Voice pipeline mode: 'pipeline' (default) or 'realtime'.                │
│                          [default: pipeline]                                                     │
│ --stt              TEXT  STT provider override (e.g. 'deepgram', 'openai', 'azure').             │
│ --tts              TEXT  TTS provider override (e.g. 'cartesia', 'openai', 'azure').             │
│ --help                   Show this message and exit.                                             │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk watch`

```

 Usage: mdk watch [OPTIONS] PATH

 Re-run ``movate validate`` whenever the agent's files change.

 With ``--run`` it instead re-executes the agent against a test input
 on every save and prints the new output plus a diff vs. the previous
 run — the live-reload test loop (ADR 027). The same loop drives
 ``mdk dev``.

 Examples:

   # Watch an agent — re-runs validate on every save
   $ movate watch ./agents/faq-agent

   # Live-reload test loop: re-run the agent + diff on every save
   $ movate watch ./agents/faq-agent --run --mock

   # Drive the loop with a specific input
   $ movate watch ./agents/faq-agent --run -i '{"text": "hello"}'

   # Slow shared filesystem? Raise the poll interval.
   $ movate watch ./agents/faq-agent --poll-interval 2

   # CI-strict mode: lint warnings fail the validate
   $ movate watch ./agents/faq-agent --strict

 Exit with Ctrl-C. Each re-run prints with a timestamp so you can
 tell at a glance which save triggered which result.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    path      PATH  Path to an agent directory. [required]                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --run,--test         --no-run,--no-test           Re-execute the agent on every save (output +   │
│                                                   diff vs. the previous run) instead of only     │
│                                                   re-validating. Resolves a test input from      │
│                                                   --input, then the first evals/dataset.jsonl    │
│                                                   row, then prompts you once.                    │
│                                                   [default: no-run]                              │
│ --input          -i                        TEXT   Test input for --run (plain string or JSON).   │
│                                                   Defaults to the first row of                   │
│                                                   evals/dataset.jsonl, else prompts once.        │
│                                                   Ignored without --run.                         │
│ --mock                                            Use the deterministic MockProvider for --run   │
│                                                   (no API keys needed).                          │
│ --poll-interval                            FLOAT  Seconds between filesystem polls. 0.5s feels   │
│                                                   instant for human edits; raise to 2-5s if      │
│                                                   you're watching a slow shared filesystem.      │
│                                                   [default: 0.5]                                 │
│ --strict                                          Pass --strict to the underlying validate       │
│                                                   (promote lint warnings to errors).             │
│ --help                                            Show this message and exit.                    │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk webhooks`

```

 Usage: mdk webhooks [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Manage outbound webhook subscriptions for lifecycle events (ADR 035 D2).

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ list       List this tenant's webhook subscriptions.                                             │
│ create     Subscribe a URL to lifecycle events.                                                  │
│ show       Show one subscription's current state (no full secret).                               │
│ delete     Remove a webhook subscription (revokes its signing secret).                           │
│ enable     Re-enable a disabled subscription.                                                    │
│ disable    Disable a subscription (the worker stops delivering until re-enabled).                │
│ attempts   List recent delivery attempts for a subscription (newest-first).                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk webhooks attempts`

```

 Usage: mdk webhooks attempts [OPTIONS] WEBHOOK_ID

 List recent delivery attempts for a subscription (newest-first).

 Each row carries the HTTP status, the truncated response excerpt,
 and the ``error_kind`` (``ok`` / ``http_error`` / ``timeout`` /
 ``connection`` / ``max_retries``). Useful for triaging a flaky
 subscriber.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    webhook_id      TEXT  Webhook id from `mdk webhooks list`. [required]                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --limit   -n      INTEGER       Max attempts to fetch (1..500). [default: 50]                    │
│ --target  -t      TEXT          Deployment target name.                                          │
│ --output  -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                                 │
│ --help                          Show this message and exit.                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk webhooks create`

```

 Usage: mdk webhooks create [OPTIONS]

 Subscribe a URL to lifecycle events.

 Prints the HMAC signing secret ONCE on stderr (with a save-now
 warning) — copy it immediately, it is never retransmitted. Each
 delivery carries an ``X-MDK-Signature: t=<ts>,v1=<hex>`` header
 (HMAC-SHA256 of ``"<ts>.<raw_body>"`` under the secret); the
 subscriber verifies by recomputing under the captured secret.

 Examples:

   # Subscribe to every event
   $ mdk webhooks create --url https://example.com/hook

   # Just run terminals + eval failures
   $ mdk webhooks create --url https://example.com/hook \
       -k run.completed,run.failed,eval.failed

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --url       -u      TEXT          HTTPS URL to POST events to. http:// is rejected at create  │
│                                      time.                                                       │
│                                      [required]                                                  │
│    --kind      -k      TEXT          Comma-separated event kinds (e.g.                           │
│                                      'run.completed,eval.failed'). Use '*' to receive every      │
│                                      kind. Default: '*'.                                         │
│                                      [default: *]                                                │
│    --disabled                        Create the subscription dormant (won't receive deliveries   │
│                                      until enabled).                                             │
│    --target    -t      TEXT          Deployment target name.                                     │
│    --output    -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                            │
│    --help                            Show this message and exit.                                 │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk webhooks delete`

```

 Usage: mdk webhooks delete [OPTIONS] WEBHOOK_ID

 Remove a webhook subscription (revokes its signing secret).

 Idempotent: deleting a non-existent subscription is a no-op
 success. Confirms first unless ``--yes`` is set.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    webhook_id      TEXT  Webhook id from `mdk webhooks list`. [required]                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --yes     -y            Skip the confirmation prompt.                                            │
│ --target  -t      TEXT  Deployment target name.                                                  │
│ --help                  Show this message and exit.                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk webhooks enable`

```

 Usage: mdk webhooks enable [OPTIONS] WEBHOOK_ID

 Re-enable a disabled subscription.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    webhook_id      TEXT  Webhook id from `mdk webhooks list`. [required]                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target  -t      TEXT  Deployment target name.                                                  │
│ --help                  Show this message and exit.                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk webhooks list`

```

 Usage: mdk webhooks list [OPTIONS]

 List this tenant's webhook subscriptions.

 Each row carries ``secret_hint`` (last 4 chars) only; the full
 HMAC secret is irrecoverable from this surface — it is shown ONCE
 on creation. Use ``mdk webhooks create`` again if you've lost the
 secret.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --target            -t                    TEXT          Deployment target name.                  │
│ --include-disabled      --enabled-only                  Show disabled subscriptions. Default:    │
│                                                         include disabled.                        │
│                                                         [default: include-disabled]              │
│ --output            -o                    [table|json]  [default: table]                         │
│ --help                                                  Show this message and exit.              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk worker`

```

 Usage: mdk worker [OPTIONS]

 Drain the queue, dispatch each job, persist the result.

 Examples:

 # Default: drain all tenants, scan ./agents and ./workflows
 $ movate worker

 # Tenant-scoped (production: one worker pool per tenant)
 $ movate worker --tenant-id <tenant-uuid>

 # Hermetic smoke (no API keys)
 $ movate worker --mock

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --tenant-id             TEXT   Drain only this tenant's queue. Omit to drain all tenants         │
│                                (operator/dev mode).                                              │
│ --agents-path           PATH   Directory to scan for agent.yaml files.                           │
│                                [env var: MDK_AGENTS_PATH, MOVATE_AGENTS_PATH]                    │
│                                [default: agents]                                                 │
│ --workflows-path        PATH   Directory to scan for workflow.yaml files. Optional;              │
│                                JobKind.WORKFLOW jobs ERROR if no workflows are registered.       │
│                                [env var: MDK_WORKFLOWS_PATH, MOVATE_WORKFLOWS_PATH]              │
│                                [default: workflows]                                              │
│ --poll-interval         FLOAT  Seconds to sleep when the queue is empty. [default: 0.5]          │
│ --mock                         Use the deterministic MockProvider (no API keys; for smoke        │
│                                tests).                                                           │
│ --backend               TEXT   Worker backend (ADR 055 D4): queue (default) drains the job queue │
│                                and serves native + langgraph (in-process) workflows — unchanged. │
│                                temporal connects to the Temporal service                         │
│                                (TEMPORAL_HOST/NAMESPACE/TLS_CERT), registers every 'runtime:     │
│                                temporal' workflow + the activities, and runs a Temporal worker   │
│                                (needs mdk).                                                      │
│                                [default: queue]                                                  │
│ --from-storage                 (temporal backend, ADR 088) ALSO load published 'runtime:         │
│                                temporal' workflows from storage for --tenant-id, not just the    │
│                                filesystem — so `mdk workflow publish <wf>` makes it hostable     │
│                                without writing to the agents volume. Default off; the filesystem │
│                                scan wins on a name clash.                                        │
│                                [env var: MDK_TEMPORAL_WORKFLOWS_FROM_STORAGE]                    │
│ --help                         Show this message and exit.                                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk workflow`

```

 Usage: mdk workflow [OPTIONS] COMMAND [ARGS]...

 Inspect + resume (HITL) workflow runs on a deployed movate runtime.

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --help          Show this message and exit.                                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Commands ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ runs       List this tenant's workflow runs on the target runtime, newest first.                 │
│ signal     Signal a human decision to resume a paused workflow run.                              │
│ replay     Replay a Temporal-backed workflow run against its recorded history.                   │
│ history    Fetch and display the full event history for a Temporal workflow run.                 │
│ list       List workflow definitions on the target runtime, newest-first.                        │
│ show       Show the full spec + bundle metadata for one workflow.                                │
│ publish    Promote a workflow version to "published".                                            │
│ revert     Roll a workflow back to a prior version (non-destructive).                            │
│ validate   Validate a local workflow.yaml against the target runtime.                            │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk workflow history`

```

 Usage: mdk workflow history [OPTIONS] RUN_ID

 Fetch and display the full event history for a Temporal workflow run.

 The event history is Temporal's durable record of every decision the
 workflow made -- it is the input ``mdk workflow replay`` verifies against.

 Use ``--output history.json`` to export the history to a file for offline
 replay (``mdk workflow replay <run_id> --from-file history.json``).

 Examples:

   # Print a human-readable table of events
   $ mdk workflow history 1f3c...

   # Export to a JSON file for offline replay
   $ mdk workflow history 1f3c... --output history.json

   # Pipe JSON to jq
   $ mdk workflow history 1f3c... --format json | jq '.events | length'

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    run_id      TEXT  The workflow_run_id whose event history to fetch (== the Temporal         │
│                        workflow id, ADR 054 D6).                                                 │
│                        [required]                                                                │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --output  -o      PATH  Write the history as JSON to this file path. When omitted the history is │
│                         printed to stdout.                                                       │
│ --format  -f      TEXT  Output format: 'json' (machine-readable) or 'table' (human-readable,     │
│                         default for terminal). Defaults to 'json' when piped or --output is set. │
│ --target  -t      TEXT  Temporal namespace / deployment target to connect to.                    │
│ --help                  Show this message and exit.                                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮

│                                         version.                                                 │
│ --limit           -n      INTEGER       Max rows to return. [default: 100]                       │
│ --target          -t      TEXT          Deployment target name.                                  │
│ --output          -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                         │
│ --help                                  Show this message and exit.                              │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

 Usage: mdk workflow publish [OPTIONS] NAME

╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

### `mdk workflow replay`

```

 Usage: mdk workflow replay [OPTIONS] RUN_ID

 Replay a Temporal-backed workflow run against its recorded history.

 Time-travel for a past ``runtime: temporal`` run: fetch its full event
 history from Temporal (the run's id == the mdk workflow_run_id, ADR 054
 D6), recompile the workflow from its on-disk definition (the SAME Track-B
 compile path the worker uses), and re-feed history through the workflow
 code via :class:`temporalio.worker.Replayer`. If the code reproduces every
 decision the history recorded, the run is deterministic; any
 drift surfaces as a non-determinism error rather than a silent pass.

 Replay does NOT re-execute activities (no LLM calls, no side effects, no
 cost) — it replays the workflow's *decisions* against the durable history.

 This is a verification/diagnosis tool: use it after editing a workflow to
 confirm an in-flight run's trajectory still type-checks against the new
 code, or to reproduce exactly what a past run decided.

 Offline mode: pass ``--from-file history.json`` to replay from
 an exported event-history file (no live Temporal connection needed). Export
 with ``mdk workflow history <run_id> --output history.json``.

 Examples:

   # Verify a past run replays deterministically
   $ mdk workflow replay 1f3c...

   # Replay from an exported history file (offline)
   $ mdk workflow replay 1f3c... --from-file history.json

   # Verbose output showing each activity replay step
   $ mdk workflow replay 1f3c... --verbose

   # Machine-readable result
   $ mdk workflow replay 1f3c... --json

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    run_id      TEXT  The workflow_run_id to replay (== the Temporal workflow id, ADR 054 D6).  │
│                        From mdk workflow runs or mdk runs show.                                  │
│                        [required]                                                                │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --workflows-path          PATH  Directory holding the workflow bundles (the same layout mdk      │
│                                 worker scans). The run's workflow is recompiled from its on-disk │
│                                 definition here.                                                 │
│                                 [default: workflows]                                             │
│ --tenant-id               TEXT  Tenant scope for the storage lookup (default: 'local' for CLI    │
│                                 use).                                                            │
│                                 [default: local]                                                 │
│ --target          -t      TEXT  Temporal namespace / deployment target to connect to.            │
│ --from-file               PATH  Replay from an exported event-history JSON file instead of       │
│                                 fetching from a live Temporal server. Use mdk workflow history   │
│                                 <run_id> --output history.json to export.                        │
│ --verbose         -v            Print each activity replay step as it is re-executed.            │
│ --json                          Emit the replay result as JSON instead of a table.               │
│ --help                          Show this message and exit.                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

### `mdk workflow revert`

```

 Usage: mdk workflow revert [OPTIONS] NAME

 Roll a workflow back to a prior version (non-destructive).

 The targeted version's bundle is re-published as a NEW latest version
 with a ``+revert.N`` suffix; the prior history stays intact so a
 follow-up revert is always possible.

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    name      TEXT  Workflow name. [required]                                                   │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --to-version          TEXT  Existing version to roll back to (re-published forward).          │
│                                [required]                                                        │
│    --target      -t      TEXT  Deployment target name.                                           │
│    --json                      Emit the response as JSON.                                        │
│    --help                      Show this message and exit.                                       │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```

╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ --paused                        Only show PAUSED runs awaiting a human signal (the HITL queue).  │
│ --limit   -n      INTEGER       Max rows to return (server caps at 100). [default: 20]           │
│ --target  -t      TEXT          Deployment target name.                                          │
│ --output  -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                                 │
│ --help                          Show this message and exit.                                      │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

### `mdk workflow signal`

```

 Usage: mdk workflow signal [OPTIONS] WORKFLOW_RUN_ID

 Signal a human decision to resume a paused workflow run.

 The runtime validates the decision against the gate's
 ``output_contract``, merges it into the checkpoint, and enqueues a
 continuation job that the worker resumes from the gate's successor. This
 prints the continuation job id (poll it with ``mdk jobs wait <id>``).

 Examples:

   # Approve and continue
   $ mdk workflow signal 1f3c... --decision '{"decision": "approve"}'

   # Decision from a file
   $ mdk workflow signal 1f3c... -d ./approval.json

╭─ Arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *    workflow_run_id      TEXT  Paused workflow_run_id to resume. [required]                     │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
╭─ Options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│ *  --decision  -d      TEXT          The human decision as a JSON object, a file path, or '-'    │
│                                      for stdin. Must include every key the gate's                │
│                                      output_contract names.                                      │
│                                      [required]                                                  │
│    --target    -t      TEXT          Deployment target name.                                     │
│    --output    -o      [table|json]  [default: table]                                            │
│    --help                            Show this message and exit.                                 │
╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

```
